Of course, when we die, we don’t cease to exist. We continue to live on the other side of the veil.</p>
<p data-aid="149808301" id="p21" style="--height:172.813px;">Still very much alive, our ancestors deserve to be remembered.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a> We remember our heritage through oral histories, clan records and family stories, memorials or places of remembrance, and celebrations with photos, foods, or items which remind us of loved ones.</p>
<p data-aid="149808309" id="p22" style="--height:288.021px;">Think of where you live—isn’t it wonderful how your country and community remember and honor ancestors, family, others who served and sacrificed? For example, at the autumn harvest remembrance in South Molton, Devonshire, England, Sister Gong and I loved finding the little church and community where generations of our Bawden family lived. We honor our ancestors by opening the heavens through temple and family history work<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> and by becoming a welding link<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> in the chain of our generations.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808318" id="p23" style="--height:115.208px;">In this age of “I choose me,” societies benefit when generations connect in meaningful ways. We need roots to have wings—real relationships, meaningful service, life beyond fleeting social media veneers.</p>
<p data-aid="149808327" id="p24" style="--height:230.417px;">Connecting with our ancestors can change our lives in surprising ways. From their trials and accomplishments, we gain faith and strength.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> <span class="page-break" data-page="45"></span>From their love and sacrifices, we learn to forgive and move forward. Our children become resilient. We gain protection and power. Ties with ancestors increase family closeness, gratitude, miracles. Such ties can bring help from the other side of the veil.</p>
<p data-aid="149808338" id="p25" style="--height:201.615px;">Just as joys come in families, so can sorrows. No individual is perfect, nor is any family. When those who should love, nurture, and protect us fail to do so, we feel abandoned, embarrassed, hurt. Family can become a hollow shell. Yet, with heaven’s help, we can come to understand our family and make peace with each other.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808348" id="p26" style="--height:230.417px;">Sometimes unwavering commitment to abiding family relationships helps us accomplish hard things. In some cases, community becomes family. A remarkable young woman whose troubled family moved frequently found a loving Church family wherever she was to nurture and give her place. Genetics and family patterns influence but do not determine us.</p>
<p data-aid="149808358" id="p27" style="--height:259.219px;">God wants our families to be happy and forever. Forever is too long if we make each other unhappy. Happy is too short if cherished relationships stop with this life. Through sacred covenants, Jesus Christ offers His love, power, and grace to change us<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a> and heal our relationships. Selfless temple service for dear ones makes our Savior’s Atonement real for them and us. Sanctified, we can return home to God’s presence as families united eternally.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808368" id="p28" style="--height:86.4063px;">Each of our stories is a journey still in progress, as we discover, create, and become with possibilities beyond imagination.</p>
<p data-aid="149808378" id="p29" style="--height:230.417px;">The Prophet Joseph Smith said, “It may seem to some to be a very bold doctrine that we talk of—a power which records or binds on earth and binds in heaven.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a> The sociality we create here can exist with eternal glory there.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a> Indeed, “we without [our family members] cannot be made perfect; neither can they without us be made perfect,” that is, in “a whole and complete and perfect union.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808388" id="p30" style="--height:28.8021px;">What can we do now?</p>
<p data-aid="149808398" id="p31" style="--height:288.021px;">First, imagine your image reflected back and forth between two mirrors of eternity. In one direction, picture yourself as daughter, granddaughter, great-granddaughter; in the other direction, smile at yourself as aunt, mother, grandmother. How quickly time passes! In each time and role, notice who is with you. Gather their photos and stories; make their memories real. Record their names, experiences, key dates. They are your family—the family you have and the family you want.</p>
<p data-aid="149808408" id="p32" style="--height:144.01px;">As you perform temple ordinances for family members, the spirit of Elijah, “a manifestation of the Holy Ghost bearing witness of the divine nature of the family,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a> will knit the hearts of your fathers, mothers, and children together in love.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note24" data-scroll-id="note24"><sup class="marker">24</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808418" id="p33" style="--height:259.219px;">Second, let the adventure of family history be intentional and spontaneous. Call your grandmother. Look deeply into the eyes of that new baby. Make time—discover eternity—at each stage of your journey. Learn and acknowledge with gratitude and honesty your family heritage. Celebrate and become the positive and, where needed, humbly do everything possible not to pass on the negative. Let good things begin with you.</p>
<p data-aid="149808429" id="p34" style="--height:172.813px;">Third, visit FamilySearch.org. Download the available mobile apps. They’re free and fun. Discover, connect, belong. See how you are related to people in a room, how easy and rewarding it is to add names to your living family tree, to find and bless your roots and branches.</p>
<p data-aid="149808440" id="p35" style="--height:144.01px;">Fourth, help unite families eternally. Remember the demographics of heaven. There are many more on the other side of the veil than on this side. As more temples come closer to us, please offer those waiting for temple ordinances opportunity to receive them.</p>
<p data-aid="149808451" id="p36" style="--height:288.021px;">The promise at Easter and always is that, in and through Jesus Christ, we can become our best story and our families can become happy and forever. In all our generations, Jesus Christ heals the brokenhearted, delivers the captives, sets at liberty them that are bruised.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note25" data-scroll-id="note25"><sup class="marker">25</sup></a> Covenant belonging with God and each other<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note26" data-scroll-id="note26"><sup class="marker">26</sup></a> includes knowing our spirit and body will be reunited in resurrection and our most precious relationships can continue beyond death with a fulness of joy.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note27" data-scroll-id="note27"><sup class="marker">27</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808462" id="p37" style="--height:115.208px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="46"></span>We each have a story. Come discover yours. Come find your voice, your song, your harmony in Him. This is the very purpose for which God created the heavens and the earth and saw that they were good.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/26gong?lang=eng#note28" data-scroll-id="note28"><sup class="marker">28</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808474" id="p38" style="--height:144.01px;">Praise God’s plan of happiness, Jesus Christ’s Atonement, continuing restoration in His gospel and Church. Please come find your family, all your generations, and bring them home. In the sacred and holy name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149805182" id="p1" style="--height:28.8021px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="47"></span>Is the plan working?</p>
<p data-aid="149805186" id="p44" style="--height:259.219px;">Recently I had a conversation with a young adult who served a mission several years ago and was now involved in his professional work. In some ways, his life was going well. But his faith was in decline. He was sinking into a sea of doubt about the Savior and His Church. He explained that he wasn’t receiving the blessings he expected from the restored gospel. He didn’t feel that the plan of happiness was working in his life.</p>
<p data-aid="149805191" id="p2" style="--height:115.208px;">My message today is for all those who might have similar feelings. I speak to those who at one time “felt to sing the song of redeeming love” but do not “feel so now.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149805196" id="p3" style="--height:115.208px;">Our Heavenly Father has prepared a wonderful plan for our eternal happiness. But when life does not unfold the way we hoped, it might seem that the plan is not working.</p>
<p data-aid="149805201" id="p4" style="--height:86.4063px;">Perhaps we feel the way Jesus’s disciples felt when they were in a ship “in the midst of the sea, tossed with waves: for the wind was contrary.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149805206" id="p5" style="--height:28.8021px;">Then, very early in the morning:</p>
<p data-aid="149805212" id="p6" style="--height:28.8021px;">“Jesus went unto them, walking on the sea.</p>
<p data-aid="149805217" id="p7" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And when the disciples saw him walking on the sea, they were troubled, … and they cried out for fear.</p>
<p data-aid="149805222" id="p8" style="--height:57.6042px;">“But straightway Jesus spake unto them, saying, Be of good cheer; it is I; be not afraid.</p>
<p data-aid="149805231" id="p9" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And Peter answered him and said, Lord, if it be thou, bid me come unto thee on the water.</p>
<p data-aid="149805238" id="p10" style="--height:86.4063px;">“And he said, Come. And when Peter was come down out of the ship, he walked on the water, to go to Jesus.</p>
<p data-aid="149805245" id="p11" style="--height:57.6042px;">“But when he saw the wind boisterous, he was afraid; and beginning to sink, he cried, … Lord, save me.</p>
<p data-aid="149808252" id="p12" style="--height:86.4063px;">“And immediately Jesus stretched forth his hand, and caught him, and said unto him, O thou of little faith, wherefore didst thou doubt?”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808260" id="p13" style="--height:115.208px;">Could I share with you three principles I learn from Peter? I pray that these principles might help anyone who feels that the plan of happiness isn’t working in their lives.</p>
<p data-aid="149808268" id="p14" style="--height:28.8021px;"><strong>First, act in faith in Jesus Christ.</strong></p>
<p data-aid="149808277" id="p15" style="--height:201.615px;">I am in awe of Peter’s faith. At Jesus’s simple invitation to “come,” he left his storm-tossed ship. He seemed to know that if Jesus Christ invited him to do something, he could do it.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a> Peter trusted the Savior more than he trusted his boat. And that faith gave him power to act with courage during a stressful, frightening situation.</p>
<p data-aid="149808285" id="p16" style="--height:144.01px;">Peter’s faith reminds me of an experience that I heard from Elder José&nbsp;L. Alonso. Shortly after Elder Alonso’s son passed away, leaving a family with young children, Elder Alonso overheard the children talking.</p>
<p data-aid="149808294" id="p41" style="--height:28.8021px;">“What are we going to do?” they asked.</p>
<p data-aid="149808304" id="p42" style="--height:57.6042px;">A nine-year-old daughter answered, “Daddy is OK. He is preaching the gospel of Jesus Christ.”</p>
<p data-aid="149808313" id="p43" style="--height:115.208px;">Like Peter, this little girl saw beyond her challenges and trusted in Jesus Christ and His Atonement. Faith in the Savior brings peace and the strength to move forward.</p>
<p data-aid="149808323" id="p17" style="--height:230.417px;">If you look back on your life, I believe you will see that you have exercised faith many times. Joining the Church is an act of faith. Speaking with Heavenly Father in prayer is an act of faith. Reading the scriptures is an act of faith. Listening to my message in this general conference is an act of faith. As President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson has said, “Do not minimize the faith you already have.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808333" id="p18" style="--height:28.8021px;">Another lesson I learn from Peter is this:</p>
<p data-aid="149808343" id="p19" style="--height:28.8021px;"><strong><span class="page-break" data-page="48"></span>In times of trouble, turn to Jesus Christ right away.</strong></p>
<p data-aid="149808353" id="p20" style="--height:172.813px;">As he walked toward the Savior, Peter was frightened by the wind and began to sink. But when Peter realized what was happening, he did not try to tread water on his own or swim back to the ship. Rather than let go of his faith in Christ, he held on more tightly, crying, “Lord, save me.”</p>
<p data-aid="149808363" id="p21" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And immediately Jesus stretched forth his hand, and caught him.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808373" id="p22" style="--height:345.625px;">All of us face boisterous winds that can shake our faith and cause us to sink. When this happens, please remember that Heavenly Father’s plan of happiness has another name—the plan of redemption. The plan was not for us to glide easily through life, never stumbling, never sinking, with a smile always on our face. Heavenly Father knew that we would need to be redeemed. This is why He prepared the plan of redemption.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a> This is why He sent a Redeemer. When we struggle—for any reason—that does not mean the plan isn’t working. That is when we need the plan the most!</p>
<p data-aid="149808383" id="p23" style="--height:57.6042px;">In those moments, follow the example of Peter. Turn to the Savior right away.</p>
<p data-aid="149808393" id="p24" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Now is the time and the day of your salvation. … Do not procrastinate the day of your repentance.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808403" id="p26" style="--height:86.4063px;">No matter where we are and where we have been, repentance is the way forward. President Nelson has taught:</p>
<p data-aid="149808413" id="p27" style="--height:86.4063px;">“Nothing is more liberating, more ennobling, or more crucial to our individual progression than is a regular, daily focus on repentance.&nbsp;…</p>
<p data-aid="149808423" id="p28" style="--height:172.813px;">“Whether you are diligently moving along the covenant path, have slipped or stepped from the covenant path, or can’t even see the path from where you are now, I plead with you to repent. Experience the strengthening power of daily repentance—of doing and being a little better each day.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808434" id="p29" style="--height:144.01px;">Coming unto Christ means more than just thinking about Him or talking about Him or even loving Him. It means following Him. It means living the way He teaches us to live. And for all of us, that means repenting, without delay.</p>
<p data-aid="149808445" id="p30" style="--height:144.01px;">One of my daughters used to work at the missionary training center. She told me of an elder she taught who confided in her that he wasn’t sure the Book of Mormon was true. He had prayed and prayed for a spiritual witness, but he received no answer.</p>
<p data-aid="149808456" id="p31" style="--height:201.615px;">My daughter prayed to know what she should do to help this missionary. The impression she received was that the scriptures were not given only so we can read them and obtain a testimony; they were given also to teach us to keep the commandments of God. My daughter shared this thought with the missionary.</p>
<p data-aid="149808468" id="p32" style="--height:172.813px;">Later, she saw this missionary again, looking much happier. He told her that he had finally received a testimony that the Book of Mormon is true. He knew that this witness came because he was making a greater effort to <em>do</em> what the Book of Mormon teaches.</p>
<p data-aid="149808480" id="p33" style="--height:172.813px;">Let us follow Peter’s example of turning to the Savior during times of trouble. Follow Jesus Christ instead of relying on your own wisdom and strength. No matter how long you’ve been trying to tread water without Him, it’s never too late to reach out to Him. The plan works!</p>
<p data-aid="149808492" id="p34" style="--height:57.6042px;">A third principle I learn from Peter and his experience is this:</p>
<p data-aid="149808504" id="p35" style="--height:57.6042px;"><strong>Humble yourself before the Lord, and He will lift you up to greater things.</strong></p>
<p data-aid="149808516" id="p36" style="--height:144.01px;">Peter had shown faith, both in walking on the water and in reaching out to the Savior when he needed help. Even so, the Savior saw in Peter the potential for so much more. “O thou of little faith,” He said, <span class="page-break" data-page="49"></span>“wherefore didst thou doubt?”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808528" id="p37" style="--height:201.615px;">Peter could have resented this rebuke. But he accepted it humbly. He continued to seek greater faith in Jesus Christ. Through many additional faith-building experiences—some of them very, very difficult—Peter eventually became the rock-solid leader the Lord needed him to be. He accomplished great things in the Lord’s service.</p>
<p data-aid="149808540" id="p38" style="--height:201.615px;">What great things does the Lord want you to accomplish? In His Church and kingdom, there are many opportunities to serve and minister to others as the Savior did. He wants you to be part of His great work. Never will the plan of happiness become more real to you than when you are helping others to live it.</p>
<p data-aid="149808552" id="p39" style="--height:172.813px;">In building my own faith, these words of Alma were life-changing: “Blessed are they who humble themselves without being compelled to be humble.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a> Let us humbly put ourselves in a position where Jesus can lift us, lead us, and make the most of our abilities.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808564" id="p40" style="--height:201.615px;">I testify that the plan of happiness works. It was created by your Heavenly Father, who loves you. It works because Jesus Christ overcame sin and death through His Atonement. Come unto Him, follow Him, and “immediately shall the great plan of redemption be brought about unto you.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/27ochoa?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149805208" id="p1" style="--height:172.813px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="50"></span>President Thomas&nbsp;S. Monson once shared the story of prison warden Clinton Duffy. “During the 1940s and 1950s, [Warden Duffy] was well known for his efforts to rehabilitate the men in his prison. Said one critic, ‘You should know that leopards don’t change their spots!’ </p>
<p data-aid="149805214" id="p2" style="--height:86.4063px;">“Replied Warden Duffy, ‘You should know I don’t work with leopards. I work with men, and men change every day.’”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149805224" id="p3" style="--height:201.615px;">One of Satan’s greatest lies is that men and women cannot change. This untruth gets told and retold in many different ways as the world says that we simply cannot change—or worse yet, that we should not change. We are taught that our circumstances define us. We should “embrace who we really are,” the world says, “and be authentic to our true selves.”</p>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149805227" id="title2" style="--height:33.6111px;">We Can Change</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149805234" id="p4" style="--height:316.823px;">While it is indeed good to be authentic, we should be authentic to our real, true selves as sons and daughters of God with a divine nature and destiny to become like Him.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> If our goal is to be authentic to this divine nature and destiny, then we will all need to change. The scriptural word for change is <i>repentance</i>. “Too many people,” President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson teaches, “consider repentance as punishment—something to be avoided except in the most serious circumstances. … When Jesus asks you and me to ‘repent,’ He is inviting us to change.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a></p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149805241" id="title3" style="--height:33.6111px;">God’s Conditions</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149805249" id="p5" style="--height:115.208px;">Computer software developers use conditional statements to tell computers what to do. These are sometimes referred to as if-then statements. As in, if <i>x</i> is true, then do <i>y</i>.</p>
<p data-aid="149808256" id="p6" style="--height:115.208px;">The Lord also operates through conditions: conditions of faith, conditions of righteousness, conditions of repentance. There are many examples of conditional statements from God such as:</p>
<p data-aid="149808262" id="p7" style="--height:86.4063px;">“<em>If</em> you keep my commandments and endure to the end [<em>then</em>] you shall have eternal life, which gift is the greatest of all the gifts of God.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808270" id="p8" style="--height:115.208px;">Or “<em>if</em> ye shall ask with a sincere heart, with real intent, having faith in Christ, [<em>then</em>] he will manifest the truth of it unto you, by the power of the Holy Ghost.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808279" id="p9" style="--height:57.6042px;">Even God’s love, although infinite and perfect, is also subject to conditions.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> For example:</p>
<p data-aid="149808288" id="p10" style="--height:86.4063px;">“<em>If</em> ye keep my commandments, [<em>then</em>] ye shall abide in my love; even as I have kept my Father’s commandments, and abide in his love.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808298" id="p11" style="--height:201.615px;">Elder D.&nbsp;Todd Christofferson further expounded on this gospel truth when he taught: “Some are wont to say, ‘The Savior loves me just as I am,’ and that is certainly true. But He cannot take any of us into His kingdom just as we are, ‘for no unclean thing can dwell there, or dwell in his presence’ [<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/pgp/moses/6.57?lang=eng#p57">Moses 6:57</a>]. Our sins must first be resolved.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a></p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808307" id="title4" style="--height:33.6111px;">Weak Things Can Become Strong</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808316" id="p12" style="--height:288.021px;">The blessing of receiving God’s <span class="page-break" data-page="51"></span>power to help us change is also conditional. The Savior, speaking through the prophet Moroni in the Book of Mormon, taught: “If men come unto me I will show unto them their weakness. I give unto men weakness that they may be humble; and my grace is sufficient for all men that humble themselves before me; for if they humble themselves before me, and have faith in me, then will I make weak things become strong unto them.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808326" id="p13" style="--height:201.615px;">Looking more closely at what the Lord is teaching us here, we see that He first says that He gives men and women <em>weakness</em>, singular, which is part of our mortal experience as fallen or carnal beings. We have become natural men and women because of the Fall of Adam. But through the Atonement of Jesus Christ, we can overcome our weakness, or our fallen natures.</p>
<p data-aid="149808336" id="p14" style="--height:172.813px;">He then says that His grace is sufficient and that <em>if</em> we will humble ourselves and have faith in Him, <em>then</em> He will “make weak <em>things</em> [plural] become strong unto [us].” In other words, as we first change our fallen natures, our weakness, then we will be able to change our behaviors, our weaknesses.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808346" id="title5" style="--height:33.6111px;">Requirements of Change</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808356" id="p15" style="--height:57.6042px;">Let’s review the requirements to change according to the Lord’s pattern:</p>
<p data-aid="149808366" id="p16" style="--height:172.813px;"><strong>First, we must humble ourselves.</strong> The Lord’s condition for change is humility. “<em>If</em> they humble themselves before me,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a> He said. The opposite of humility is pride. Pride exists when we think we know better—when what <em>we</em> think or feel takes priority over what <em>God</em> thinks or feels.</p>
<p data-aid="149808376" id="p17" style="--height:172.813px;">King Benjamin taught that “the natural man is an enemy to God, … and will be, forever and ever, unless he … putteth off the natural man and becometh a saint through the atonement of Christ the Lord, and becometh as a child, submissive, meek, [and] humble.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808386" id="p18" style="--height:201.615px;">In order to change, we need to put off the natural man and become humble and submissive. We must be humble enough to follow a living prophet. Humble enough to make and keep temple covenants. Humble enough to repent daily. We must be humble enough to want to change, to “yield our hearts unto God.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808396" id="p19" style="--height:230.417px;"><strong>Second, we must have faith in Jesus Christ.</strong> Again, the words of the Savior: “If they humble themselves before me, <em>and have faith in me</em>,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> He will give us the power to overcome our weaknesses. Humility, coupled with faith in Jesus Christ, will allow us to access the enabling power of His grace and the fulness of blessings available because of His Atonement.</p>
<p data-aid="149808406" id="p20" style="--height:115.208px;">President Nelson has taught that “true repentance begins with faith that Jesus Christ has the power to cleanse, heal, and strengthen us. … It is <em>our</em> faith that unlocks the power of God in <em>our</em> lives.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808416" id="p21" style="--height:259.219px;"><strong>Third, through His grace He can make weak things become strong.</strong> <em>If</em> we humble ourselves and have faith in Jesus Christ, <em>then</em> His grace will enable us to change. In other words, He will empower us to change. This is possible because, as He says, “my grace is sufficient for all men.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a> His strengthening, enabling grace gives us power to overcome <em>all</em> obstacles, <em>all</em> challenges, and <em>all</em> weaknesses as we seek to change.</p>
<p data-aid="149808427" id="p22" style="--height:115.208px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="52"></span>Our greatest weaknesses can become our greatest strengths. We can be changed and “become new creatures.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> Weak things literally can “become strong unto [us].”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808438" id="p23" style="--height:201.615px;">The Savior worked out His infinite and eternal Atonement so that we could in fact change, repent, and become better. We can actually be born again. We can overcome habits, addictions, and even the “disposition to do evil.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a> As sons and daughters of a loving Father in Heaven, we have the power within us to change.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808449" id="title6" style="--height:33.6111px;">Examples of Change</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808460" id="p24" style="--height:57.6042px;">The scriptures are full of examples of men and women who changed.</p>
<p data-aid="149808472" id="p25" style="--height:86.4063px;">Saul, a Pharisee and active persecutor of the early Christian church,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a> became Paul, an Apostle of the Lord Jesus Christ.</p>
<p data-aid="149808484" id="p26" style="--height:115.208px;">Alma was a priest in the court of wicked King Noah. He heard the words of Abinadi, fully repented, and became one of the great missionaries of the Book of Mormon.</p>
<p data-aid="149808496" id="p27" style="--height:115.208px;">His son Alma spent his youth seeking to destroy the Church. He was among “the very vilest of sinners”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a> until he had a change of heart and became a powerful missionary in his own right.</p>
<p data-aid="149808508" id="p28" style="--height:144.01px;">Moses was adopted into Pharaoh’s family and raised in luxury as an Egyptian prince. But when he came to understand who he really was and learned of his divine destiny, he changed and became the great lawgiving prophet of the Old Testament.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808520" id="p29" style="--height:288.021px;">My wife’s grandfather James&nbsp;B. Keysor has always impressed me with his own mighty change of heart.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a> Born of faithful Latter-day Saint pioneer ancestors in the Salt Lake Valley in 1906, he lost his mother at a young age and struggled throughout his youth. His teenage and young adult years were spent away from the Church, during which time he acquired a number of bad habits. Nevertheless, he met and married a faithful woman, and together they raised five children.</p>
<p data-aid="149808532" id="p30" style="--height:201.615px;">In 1943, following the difficult years of the Great Depression and during World War&nbsp;II, Bud, as he was called by friends and family, left Utah and moved to Los Angeles, California, to look for employment. During this time away from home, he lived with his sister and her husband, who was serving as the bishop of their ward.</p>
<p data-aid="149808544" id="p31" style="--height:115.208px;">With the love and influence of his sister and brother-in-law, he started to revive his interest in the Church and began to read the Book of Mormon each night before going to sleep.</p>
<p data-aid="149808556" id="p32" style="--height:57.6042px;">One night, while he was reading in <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/bofm/alma/34?lang=eng">Alma chapter 34</a>, his heart was touched as he read the following words:</p>
<p data-aid="149808569" id="p33" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Yea, I would that ye would come forth and harden not your hearts any longer.&nbsp;…</p>
<p data-aid="149808581" id="p38" style="--height:86.4063px;">“For behold, this life is the time for men to prepare to meet God; yea, behold the day of this life is the day for men to perform their labors.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808593" id="p34" style="--height:345.625px;">While he was reading these verses, a powerful feeling came over him and he knew that he had to change, to repent, and he knew what he must do. He got up from his bed and knelt down and began to pray, pleading with the Lord to forgive him and to give him the strength he needed to make changes in his life. His prayer was answered, and from that time forward, he never looked back. Bud went on to serve in the Church and remained a faithful, committed Latter-day Saint to the end of his life. He was changed in every way. His mind, his heart, his actions, his very being were changed.</p>
<p data-aid="149808605" id="p35" style="--height:259.219px;">Brothers and sisters, our divine destiny and purpose is ultimately to become like our Heavenly Father and Savior, Jesus Christ. We do this as we change, or repent. We receive the Savior’s “image in [our] countenances.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note24" data-scroll-id="note24"><sup class="marker">24</sup></a> We become new, clean, different, and we simply continue to work at it every day. Sometimes it may feel like two steps forward and one step back, but we continue to humbly move forward in faith.</p>
<p data-aid="149808617" id="p36" style="--height:86.4063px;">And as we humble ourselves and exercise faith in Jesus Christ, <span class="page-break" data-page="53"></span>the grace of Christ and His infinite atoning sacrifice make it possible to change.</p>
<p data-aid="149808629" id="p37" style="--height:115.208px;">I witness and testify that Jesus Christ is in reality our Savior and Redeemer. His grace is indeed sufficient. I declare that He is “the way, the truth, and the life.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/28hamilton?lang=eng#note25" data-scroll-id="note25"><sup class="marker">25</sup></a> In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</section>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149807484" id="p1" style="--height:115.208px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="54"></span>I am grateful for President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson’s powerful prophetic call to missionary service and President M.&nbsp;Russell Ballard’s and Elder Marcos&nbsp;A. Aidukaitis’s inspiring missionary messages today.</p>
<p data-aid="149807491" id="p2" style="--height:460.833px;">A missionary assignment to Great Britain late last year allowed me to reflect on the precious spiritual events that were foundational to my decision to serve as a missionary.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> When I was 15 years old, my beloved older brother, Joe, was 20—the age of eligibility then to serve a mission. In the United States, because of the Korean conflict, very few were allowed to serve. Only one could be called from each ward per year.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> It was a surprise when our bishop asked Joe to explore this possibility with our father. Joe had been preparing applications for medical school. Our father, who was not active in the Church, had made financial preparations to help him and was not in favor of Joe going on a mission. Dad suggested that Joe could do more good by going to medical school. This was a huge issue in our family.</p>
<p data-aid="149807498" id="p3" style="--height:288.021px;">In a remarkable discussion with my wise and exemplary older brother, we concluded that his decision on whether to serve a mission and delay his education depended on three questions: (1)&nbsp;Is Jesus Christ divine? (2)&nbsp;Is the Book of Mormon the word of God? and (3)&nbsp;Is Joseph Smith the Prophet of the Restoration? If the answer to these questions was yes, it was clear that Joe could do more good taking the gospel of Jesus Christ to the world than becoming a doctor at an earlier date.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807507" id="p4" style="--height:345.625px;">That night I prayed fervently and with real intent. The Spirit, in an undeniably powerful way, confirmed to me that the answer to all three of these questions was yes. This was a seminal event for me. I realized that every decision I would make for the rest of my life would be influenced by these truths. I also knew that I would serve a mission if given the opportunity. Over a lifetime of service and spiritual experiences, I have come to understand that true conversion is the result of the conscious acceptance of the will of God and that we can be guided in our actions by the Holy Ghost.</p>
<p data-aid="149807513" id="p5" style="--height:115.208px;">I already had a testimony of the divinity of Jesus Christ as Savior of the world. That night I received a spiritual testimony of the Book of Mormon<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a> and the Prophet Joseph Smith.</p>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807520" id="title2" style="--height:67.2222px;">Joseph Smith Was an Instrument in the Lord’s Hands</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807527" id="p6" style="--height:345.625px;">Your testimony will be strengthened when you know in your heart through your prayers that the Prophet Joseph Smith was an instrument in the Lord’s hands. During the past eight years, one of my assignments in the Twelve Apostles was to review <span class="page-break" data-page="55"></span>and read all the remarkable Joseph Smith papers and documents and the research that led to the publication of the <em>Saints</em> volumes.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a> My testimony and admiration of the Prophet Joseph Smith have been greatly strengthened and enhanced after reading the inspiring details of his life and foreordained prophetic ministry.</p>
<p data-aid="149807535" id="p7" style="--height:230.417px;">Joseph’s translation of the Book of Mormon by the gift and power of God was foundational to the Restoration.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> The Book of Mormon is internally consistent, beautifully written, and contains the answers to life’s great questions. It is another testament of Jesus Christ. I testify that Joseph Smith was righteous, full of faith, and an instrument in the Lord’s hands in bringing forth the Book of Mormon.</p>
<p data-aid="149807544" id="p8" style="--height:201.615px;">The revelations and events recorded in the Doctrine and Covenants provide the keys, ordinances, and covenants necessary for salvation and exaltation. They not only set forth the essentials required to establish the Church but also provide profound doctrine that allows us to understand the purpose of life and gives us an eternal perspective.</p>
<p data-aid="149807553" id="p9" style="--height:345.625px;">One of the numerous examples of Joseph Smith’s prophetic role is found in the <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/dc-testament/dc/76?lang=eng">76th section of the Doctrine and Covenants</a>. It is an explicit record of the vision of heaven, including kingdoms of glory, which the Prophet Joseph and Sidney Rigdon were blessed to receive on February&nbsp;16, 1832. At that time, the vast majority of churches were teaching that the Savior’s Atonement would not provide salvation for most people. It was believed that a few would be saved and the vast majority would be doomed to hell and damnation, including endless tortures “of the most awful and unspeakable intensity.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807562" id="p10" style="--height:259.219px;">The revelation contained in the 76th section provides a glorious vision of the degrees of glory where the vast majority of Heavenly Father’s children who were valiant in their premortal estate are profoundly blessed following the ultimate judgment.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a> The vision of the three degrees of glory, the lowest of which “surpasses all understanding,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a> is a direct refutation of the then strong but erroneous doctrine that the majority would be doomed to hell and damnation.</p>
<p data-aid="149807572" id="p11" style="--height:201.615px;">When you realize Joseph Smith was only 26 years old, had a limited education, and had little or no exposure to the classical languages from which the Bible was translated, he was truly an instrument in the Lord’s hands. In the <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/dc-testament/dc/76.17?lang=eng#p17">17th verse of section 76</a>, he was inspired to use the word <i>unjust</i> instead of <i>damnation</i> that was used in the Gospel of John.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807580" id="p12" style="--height:201.615px;">It is interesting that 45 years later an Anglican church leader and academically credentialed classical scholar,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a> Frederic&nbsp;W. Farrar, who wrote <cite>The Life of Christ</cite>,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a> asserted that the definition of <em>damnation</em> in the King James Version of the Bible was the result of translation errors from Hebrew and Greek to English.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807589" id="p13" style="--height:316.823px;">In our day, many have adopted the concept that there should be no consequence for sin. They support the unconditional condoning of sin without repentance. Our revealed <span class="page-break" data-page="56"></span>doctrine not only refutes the idea that most people would be eternally condemned to hell and damnation but also establishes that personal repentance is a commanded prerequisite to partake of the Savior’s Atonement and inherit the celestial kingdom.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> I testify that Joseph Smith was truly an instrument in the Lord’s hands in bringing forth the Restoration of His gospel!</p>
<p data-aid="149807600" id="p14" style="--height:201.615px;">Because of the Restoration of the gospel of Jesus Christ, we understand the importance of both repentance and the “works of righteousness.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a> We understand the overwhelming significance of the Savior’s Atonement and of His saving ordinances and covenants, including those performed in the temple.</p>
<p data-aid="149807609" id="p15" style="--height:230.417px;">The “works of righteousness” emanate from and are the fruits of conversion. True conversion is brought about by the conscious acceptance and commitment to follow the will of God.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> The banquet of consequences and blessings that flow from conversion is true and permanent peace and the personal assurance of ultimate happiness<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a>—despite the storms of this life.</p>
<p data-aid="149807618" id="p16" style="--height:86.4063px;">Conversion to the Savior changes a natural man into a sanctified, born again, purified person—a new creature in Christ Jesus.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a></p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807627" id="title3" style="--height:100.833px;">Many Are Kept from the Truth Because They Know Not Where to Find It</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807636" id="p17" style="--height:115.208px;">What are the obligations that flow from conversion? In Liberty Jail, the Prophet Joseph noted that many “are only kept from the truth because they know not where to find it.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807644" id="p18" style="--height:547.24px;">In the Lord’s preface to the Doctrine and Covenants, a big-picture declaration of the Lord’s purpose for us was set forth. He declared, “Wherefore, I the Lord, knowing the calamity which should come upon the inhabitants of the earth, called upon my servant Joseph Smith, Jun., and spake unto him from heaven, and gave him commandments.” He further instructs, “That the fulness of my gospel might be proclaimed by the weak and the simple unto the ends of the world.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a> That includes full-time missionaries. That includes each of us. This should be a laser-like focus to everyone who has been blessed with a conversion to the will of God. The Savior graciously invites us to be His voice and His hands.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a> The love of the Savior will be our guiding light. The Savior taught His disciples, “Go ye therefore, and teach all nations.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a> And to Joseph Smith, He declared, “Preach my gospel unto every creature who has not received it.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807652" id="p19" style="--height:201.615px;">One week after the dedication of the Kirtland Temple on April&nbsp;3, 1836, which was Easter Sunday and also Passover, the Lord appeared in a magnificent vision to Joseph and Oliver Cowdery. The Lord accepted the temple and declared, “This is the beginning of the blessing which shall be poured out upon the heads of my people.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note24" data-scroll-id="note24"><sup class="marker">24</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807661" id="p20" style="--height:115.208px;">After this vision closed, Moses appeared “and committed … the keys of the gathering of Israel from the four parts of the earth, and the leading of the ten tribes from the land of the north.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note25" data-scroll-id="note25"><sup class="marker">25</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807670" id="p21" style="--height:172.813px;">President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson, our beloved prophet today who holds these same keys, taught this morning: “You young men have been reserved for this time when the promised gathering of Israel is taking place. As you serve missions, you play a pivotal role in this unprecedented event!”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note26" data-scroll-id="note26"><sup class="marker">26</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807678" id="p22" style="--height:345.625px;">For the Savior’s mandate to share the gospel to become part of who we are, we need to become <strong>converted</strong> to the will of God; we need to <strong>love</strong> our neighbors, <strong>share</strong> the restored gospel of Jesus Christ, and <strong>invite</strong> all to come and see. As members of the Church, we cherish the Prophet Joseph’s reply to John Wentworth, the editor of the <cite>Chicago Democrat</cite>, in 1842. He was requesting information about the Church. Joseph concluded his response by using the “Standard of Truth” as a preface to the thirteen Articles of Faith. The standard conveys, in a concise way, what must be accomplished:</p>
<p data-aid="149807686" id="p23" style="--height:259.219px;">“No unhallowed hand can stop the work from progressing; persecutions may rage, mobs may combine, armies may assemble, calumny may defame, but the truth of God will go forth boldly, nobly, and independent, till it has penetrated every continent, visited every clime, swept every country, and sounded in every ear, till the purposes of God shall be accomplished, and the Great Jehovah shall say the work is done.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note27" data-scroll-id="note27"><sup class="marker">27</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807694" id="p24" style="--height:259.219px;">This has been the clarion call for generations of Latter-day Saints, especially missionaries. In the spirit of the “Standard of Truth,” we are grateful that in the midst of a worldwide pandemic, faithful missionaries have shared the gospel. Missionaries, we love you! The Lord asks each one of us to share His gospel in word <span class="page-break" data-page="57"></span>and deed. Our personal conversion includes the responsibility to share the gospel of Jesus Christ with the world.</p>
<p data-aid="149807702" id="p25" style="--height:230.417px;">The blessings of sharing the gospel include increasing our conversion to the will of God and letting God prevail in our lives.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note28" data-scroll-id="note28"><sup class="marker">28</sup></a> We bless others to experience a “mighty change” of heart.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note29" data-scroll-id="note29"><sup class="marker">29</sup></a> There is truly eternal joy in helping to bring souls unto Christ.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note30" data-scroll-id="note30"><sup class="marker">30</sup></a> Laboring for the conversion of oneself and others is <em>the</em> noble task.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/29cook?lang=eng#note31" data-scroll-id="note31"><sup class="marker">31</sup></a> I so testify in the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</section>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149805235" id="p7" style="--height:86.4063px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="58"></span>My dear sisters, as we begin this unique women’s session of general conference, I am pleased to deliver this introductory message from the First Presidency.</p>
<p data-aid="149805242" id="p8" style="--height:259.219px;">Our Saturday sessions have a history of different purposes and different audiences. This evening we add to that history as we embark upon a new purpose and procedure for the foreseeable future. The gospel of Jesus Christ does not change. Gospel doctrine does not change. Our personal covenants do not change. But over the years, the meetings we hold to communicate our messages do change and very likely will continue to change over the years.</p>
<p data-aid="149808253" id="p9" style="--height:144.01px;">For now, this Saturday evening meeting is a session of general conference, not a session of any organization. Like all sessions of general conference, the planning, speakers, and music are designated by the First Presidency.</p>
<p data-aid="149808261" id="p10" style="--height:201.615px;">We have asked President Jean&nbsp;B. Bingham, General President of the Relief Society, to conduct this session. Future Saturday evening sessions may be conducted by one of the other General Officers of the Church, such as members of the General Presidencies of Relief Society, Young Women, and Primary, designated by the First Presidency.</p>
<p data-aid="149808269" id="p11" style="--height:403.229px;">Tonight this Saturday evening session of general conference will concentrate on the concerns of Latter-day Saint women. This will include the doctrine of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints, <span class="page-break" data-page="59"></span>the policies of the Church that relate specially to women, and the general responsibilities and work of the organizations that include the women and girls of the Church. Though this session is deliberately broadcast to a worldwide audience like all sessions of general conference, the audience invited to be present in the Conference Center for this session is women and girls age 12 and older. We have included some priesthood leaders who preside over the participating organizations.</p>
<p data-aid="149808278" id="p12" style="--height:230.417px;">What we are initiating here is responsive to the communication resources currently available to the Lord’s worldwide Church leadership and membership. The doctrine of the gospel of Jesus Christ is for everyone, so that is our principal motive and extent of dissemination. We honor the daughters of God in this special session by concentrating on their concerns and those of their organizations.</p>
<p data-aid="149808287" id="p13" style="--height:201.615px;">We are grateful that broadcast technology now gives Church leaders the capacity to conduct detailed training by addressing specific audiences in the field. We also welcome the fact that current travel opportunities are increasing. That allows us to send Church leaders to conduct needed regular face-to-face leadership training in the field.</p>
<p data-aid="149808297" id="p14" style="--height:201.615px;">This is the work of the Lord Jesus Christ. We are His servants, directed by His Holy Spirit. We invoke the blessings of our Lord upon the leaders of these organizations and upon the faithful women and girls who serve the Lord in these organizations and in their individual lives. In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149808271" id="p1" style="--height:57.6042px;">What a joy it is to be gathered with each of you in this women’s session of general conference!</p>
<p data-aid="149808281" id="p2" style="--height:172.813px;">I grew up in western New York and attended a small branch of the Church about 20 miles (32&nbsp;km) from our home. As I sat in Sunday School class in the basement of our old rented chapel with only my friend Patti Jo, I never could have imagined being part of a global sisterhood of millions of women.</p>
<p data-aid="149808290" id="p3" style="--height:201.615px;">Five years ago my husband, Bruce, became seriously ill when we were serving with the consecrated Saints in the Europe East Area. We returned home, and he passed away only a few weeks later. My life changed overnight. I was grieving and felt weak and vulnerable. I pled with the Lord to direct my path: “What would Thou have me do?”</p>
<p data-aid="149808300" id="p4" style="--height:201.615px;">A few weeks later, I was going through my mail when a small picture in a catalog caught my eye. As I looked closer, I realized it was an artist’s rendition of the Samaritan woman with Jesus at the well. At that moment the Spirit spoke clearly to me: “<em>That</em> is what you are supposed to do.” A loving Heavenly Father was inviting me to come to the Savior and learn.</p>
<p data-aid="149808310" id="p5" style="--height:86.4063px;">I would like to share with you three lessons I am learning as I continue to drink from His well of “living water.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a></p>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808319" id="title2" style="--height:100.833px;">First: Our Past and Present Circumstances Do Not Determine Our Future</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808329" id="p6" style="--height:115.208px;">Sisters, I know that many of you feel as I did, unsure how to face difficult challenges and loss—loss because your life is not unfolding in the way you had hoped for, prayed for, and planned for.</p>
<p data-aid="149808340" id="p7" style="--height:115.208px;">No matter our circumstances, our lives are sacred and have meaning <span class="page-break" data-page="60"></span>and purpose. Each of us is a beloved daughter of God, born with divinity in our souls.</p>
<p data-aid="149808350" id="p8" style="--height:172.813px;">Our Savior, Jesus Christ, through His atoning sacrifice, made it possible for us to be cleansed and healed, enabling us to fulfill our purpose on earth regardless of decisions of family members, our marital status, physical or mental health, or any other situation.</p>
<p data-aid="149808360" id="p9" style="--height:201.615px;">Consider the woman at the well. What was her life like? Jesus perceived that she had had five husbands and was currently not married to the man she was living with. And yet, despite her life’s difficulties, one of the Savior’s first public declarations that He was the Messiah was to her. He said, “I that speak unto thee am he.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808370" id="p10" style="--height:115.208px;">She became a powerful witness, declaring to those in her city that Jesus was the Christ. “And many of the Samaritans of that city believed on him for the saying of the woman.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808380" id="p11" style="--height:144.01px;">Her past and present circumstances did not determine her future. Like her, we can choose to turn to the Savior today for the strength and healing that will enable us to fulfill <em>all</em> that we were sent here to do.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808391" id="title3" style="--height:33.6111px;">Second: The Power Is in Us</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808401" id="p12" style="--height:144.01px;">In a familiar verse in the Doctrine and Covenants, the Lord encourages women and men to be “anxiously engaged in a good cause, and do many things of their own free will, and bring to pass much righteousness; <em>for the power is in them</em>.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808411" id="p14" style="--height:57.6042px;">Sisters, the power is in <em>us</em> to bring to pass much righteousness!</p>
<p data-aid="149808421" id="p15" style="--height:144.01px;">President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson testified, “Every woman and every man who makes covenants with God and keeps those covenants, and who participates worthily in priesthood ordinances, has direct access to the power of God.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808432" id="p16" style="--height:144.01px;">I have come to know that as we strive to honor sacred covenants made at baptism and in holy temples, the Lord will bless us “with <em>His</em> healing, strengthening power” and with “spiritual insights and awakenings [we’ve] never had before.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a></p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808443" id="title4" style="--height:67.2222px;">Third: “Out of Small Things Proceedeth That Which Is Great”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a></h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808454" id="p17" style="--height:172.813px;">In the Sermon on the Mount, Jesus taught His disciples, “Ye are the <em>salt</em> of the earth”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a> and “Ye are the <em>light</em> of the world.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a> Later He compared the growth of the kingdom of heaven to leaven, “which a woman took, and hid in three measures of meal, till the whole was leavened.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a></p>
<ul class="bullet">
<li>
<p data-aid="149808466" id="p35" style="--height:28.8021px;">Salt</p>
</li>
<li>
<p data-aid="149808478" id="p36" style="--height:28.8021px;">Leaven</p>
</li>
<li>
<p data-aid="149808490" id="p37" style="--height:28.8021px;">Light</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-aid="149808502" id="p19" style="--height:86.4063px;">Even in very small amounts, each affects everything around it. The Savior invites us to use His power to be as <em>salt</em>, <em>leaven</em>, and <em>light</em>.</p>
<section>
<header>
<h3 data-aid="149808513" id="title5" style="--height:23.9931px;">Salt</h3>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808526" id="p20" style="--height:86.4063px;">It is surprising how much difference a sprinkling of salt makes in the flavor of what we eat. And yet salt is one of the least expensive and simplest ingredients.</p>
<p data-aid="149808539" id="p21" style="--height:172.813px;">In the book of 2&nbsp;Kings, we read of “a little maid”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a> who was captured by the Syrians and became a servant to the wife of Naaman, captain of the Syrian army. She was <em>as salt</em>; she was young, of no worldly importance, and her life as a slave in a foreign country was clearly not what she had hoped for.</p>
<p data-aid="149808551" id="p38" style="--height:115.208px;">However, she spoke two sentences with the power of God, testifying to Naaman’s wife: “Would God my lord were with the prophet that is in Samaria! for he would recover him of his leprosy.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808563" id="p23" style="--height:86.4063px;">Her words of faith were relayed to Naaman, who acted on her words, allowing him to be healed both physically and spiritually.</p>
<p data-aid="149808575" id="p24" style="--height:115.208px;">We often focus on the servants who convinced Naaman to bathe in the river Jordan, as the prophet Elisha directed, but Naaman would not have even been at Elisha’s door without “a little maid.”</p>
<p data-aid="149808587" id="p25" style="--height:86.4063px;">You may be young or feel of no importance, but you can be <em>as salt</em> in your family, at school, and in your community.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h3 data-aid="149808599" id="title6" style="--height:23.9931px;">Leaven</h3>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808611" id="p26" style="--height:115.208px;">Have you ever eaten bread without leaven? How would you describe it? Dense? Heavy? Hard? With only a small amount of leaven, bread rises, expanding to become lighter and softer.</p>
<p data-aid="149808623" id="p27" style="--height:115.208px;">When we invite the power of God into our lives, we can replace the “spirit of heaviness”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> with inspired perspectives that lift others and make room for hearts to be healed.</p>
<p data-aid="149808635" id="p28" style="--height:172.813px;">Recently a friend of mine lay in bed on Christmas morning, overcome with sorrow. Her children begged <span class="page-break" data-page="61"></span>her to get up; however, she was filled with the pain of her pending divorce. Lying in bed sobbing, she poured out her soul in prayer to her Heavenly Father, telling Him of her despair. </p>
<p data-aid="149808649" id="p39" style="--height:201.615px;">As she concluded her prayer, the Spirit whispered to her that God knew her pain. She was filled with His compassion for her. This sacred experience validated her emotions and gave her hope that she was not grieving alone. She got up, went outside, and built a snowman with her children, replacing the heaviness of the morning with laughter and joy.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h3 data-aid="149808661" id="title7" style="--height:23.9931px;">Light</h3>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808673" id="p29" style="--height:115.208px;">How much light does it take to pierce the darkness in a room? One small ray. And that ray of light in a dark place can emanate from the power of God in you.</p>
<p data-aid="149808685" id="p30" style="--height:144.01px;">Even though you may feel alone as the storms of life are raging, you can shine a light in the darkness of misunderstanding, confusion, and unbelief. Your light of faith in Christ can be steady and sure, leading those around you to safety and peace.</p>
</section>
<p data-aid="149808696" id="p31" style="--height:86.4063px;">Sisters, hearts can be changed and lives blessed as we offer a pinch of salt, a spoonful of leaven, and a ray of light.</p>
<p data-aid="149808707" id="p32" style="--height:172.813px;">I testify that the <em>Savior</em> is the salt in our lives, inviting <em>us</em> to taste of His joy and love.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> It is <em>He</em> who is the leaven when our lives are hard, bringing <em>us</em> hope<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a> and lifting our burdens<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> through His matchless power and redeeming love.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a> <em>He</em> is our light,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a> illuminating <em>our</em> path back home.</p>
<p data-aid="149808717" id="p34" style="--height:172.813px;">I pray that we can come to the Savior, like the woman at the well, and drink of His living water. With the people of Samaria, we can then declare, “Now we believe,&nbsp;… for we have heard him ourselves, and know that this is indeed the Christ, the Saviour of the world.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/32porter?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a> In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</section>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149807512" id="p1" style="--height:316.823px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="62"></span>Not long ago, a dear friend had an impression to visit a woman in her ward. She brushed off the prompting because she hardly knew her—it just didn’t make sense. But since the thought kept coming to her, she decided to act on the prompting. Because she was already feeling uncomfortable about the impending visit, she determined that taking something to the sister would help ease her anxiety. Certainly she couldn’t go empty-handed! So she bought a container of ice cream, and off she went to begin what she worried might be an awkward visit.</p>
<p data-aid="149807519" id="p2" style="--height:259.219px;">She knocked on the woman’s door, and shortly the sister answered. My friend handed her the ice cream in a brown paper bag, and the conversation began. It didn’t take long for my friend to realize why the visit was needed. As they sat together on the front porch, the woman unveiled a host of challenges she was facing. After an hour of talking in the warm summer weather, my friend noticed the ice cream melting through the brown paper bag.</p>
<p data-aid="149807526" id="p32" style="--height:57.6042px;">She exclaimed, “I am so sorry that your ice cream melted!”</p>
<p data-aid="149807534" id="p33" style="--height:57.6042px;">The woman sweetly responded, “It’s OK! I’m lactose intolerant!”</p>
<p data-aid="149807542" id="p3" style="--height:86.4063px;">In a dream, the Lord told the prophet Lehi, “Blessed art thou Lehi, because of the things which thou hast <em>done</em>.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/33craven?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807550" id="p4" style="--height:144.01px;">Being a disciple of Jesus Christ involves more than just hoping or believing. It calls for effort, movement, and commitment. It requires that we do something, being “doers of the word, and not hearers only.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/33craven?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807559" id="p5" style="--height:86.4063px;">In the case of the melted ice cream, what mattered most? The ice cream? Or that my friend simply did something?</p>
<p data-aid="149807567" id="p6" style="--height:115.208px;">I had a sweet experience with a darling young woman who asked a very sincere question: “Sister Craven, how do you know that anything about the Church is true? Because I feel nothing.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807578" id="p34" style="--height:86.4063px;">Before jumping to an answer, I first asked her some questions. “Tell me about your personal scripture study.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807585" id="p35" style="--height:28.8021px;">She replied, “I don’t read the scriptures.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807594" id="p36" style="--height:57.6042px;">I asked, “What about with your family? Do you study <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> together?”</p>
<p data-aid="149807603" id="p37" style="--height:28.8021px;">She said, “No.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807612" id="p38" style="--height:57.6042px;">I asked about her prayers: “What do you feel when you pray?”</p>
<p data-aid="149807621" id="p39" style="--height:28.8021px;">Her answer: “I don’t pray.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807631" id="p7" style="--height:57.6042px;">My response to her was simple: “If you want to know anything, you will have to do something.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807640" id="p40" style="--height:230.417px;">Isn’t that true with anything we want to learn or know? I invited my new friend to start <em>doing</em> the gospel of Jesus Christ: praying, studying, serving others, and trusting in the Lord. Conversion won’t come while doing nothing. It comes through the power of the Holy Ghost as we intentionally make an effort to know by asking, seeking, and knocking. It comes by doing.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/33craven?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807648" id="p8" style="--height:172.813px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="63"></span>In the Doctrine and Covenants, the Lord occasionally says, “It mattereth not.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/33craven?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a> It makes me ponder that if some things matter not, or matter less, there must be things that matter most. In our efforts to <em>do something</em> or <em>do anything</em>, we might ask ourselves, “What mattereth most?”</p>
<p data-aid="149807656" id="p9" style="--height:172.813px;">Advertisers often use slogans such as “Essential” or “Must Have” in the hope of luring us to believe the product they are selling is necessary for our happiness or well-being. But is what they are selling <em>really</em> essential? Must we <em>really</em> have it? Does it <em>really</em> matter?</p>
<p data-aid="149807665" id="p10" style="--height:57.6042px;">Here are some thoughts to consider. What mattereth most?</p>
<ul class="bullet">
<li>
<p data-aid="149807673" id="p11" style="--height:86.4063px;">How many “likes” we get on our social media posts? Or how much we are loved and valued by our Heavenly Father?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p data-aid="149807681" id="p12" style="--height:57.6042px;">Wearing the latest trend in clothing? Or showing respect for our bodies by dressing modestly?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p data-aid="149807689" id="p13" style="--height:86.4063px;">Finding answers through an internet search? Or receiving answers from God through the Holy Ghost?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p data-aid="149807697" id="p15" style="--height:57.6042px;">Wanting more? Or being content with what we have been given?</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-aid="149807705" id="p16" style="--height:28.8021px;">President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson teaches:</p>
<p data-aid="149807713" id="p30" style="--height:115.208px;">“With the Holy Ghost as your companion, you can see right through the celebrity culture that has smitten our society. You can be smarter than previous generations have ever been.&nbsp;…</p>
<p data-aid="149807720" id="p31" style="--height:28.8021px;">“Set a standard for the rest of the world!”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/33craven?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807727" id="p17" style="--height:201.615px;">It takes effort to stay focused on what is <em>truly essential</em> for lasting joy. Satan would love nothing more than for us to misplace our eternal values, leading us to waste precious time, talents, or spiritual strength on things that matter not. I invite each of us to prayerfully consider those things that distract us from doing what mattereth most.</p>
<p data-aid="149807734" id="p18" style="--height:172.813px;">Our oldest son’s third-grade teacher taught her class to “boss your brain.” It was a reminder to her young students that they were in control of their thoughts and could therefore control what they do. I remind myself to “boss <em>my</em> brain” when I find myself drifting toward things that matter less.</p>
<p data-aid="149807741" id="p19" style="--height:547.24px;">A high school student recently told me that it has become popular among some youth of the Church to disregard the commandments with a calculated plan to repent later. “It’s sort of a badge of honor,” I was told.
