Certainly the Lord will continue to forgive those who humbly repent “with real intent.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/33craven?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> But the Savior’s merciful Atonement should never be used in such a mocking way. We know the parable of the one lost sheep. Of course, a shepherd will leave the other 99 sheep to find the one who has strayed. But can you imagine the joy that those who choose to be the 99 bring to the Good Shepherd? The ones who stick together and help each other live their covenants? Can you visualize what the world or your school or your work or your home would be like if being obedient was the popular thing to do? It’s not about <em>doing</em> life perfectly—it’s about finding joy while <em>doing our best</em> to live the covenants we have made with the Lord.</p>
<p data-aid="149807748" id="p20" style="--height:172.813px;">With the world expressing more doubt about God and confusion and pressures increasing, this is the time we must stay closest to the prophet. As he is the Lord’s mouthpiece, we can trust that what he urges, counsels, and pleads with us to do are things that matter most.</p>
<p data-aid="149807755" id="p21" style="--height:345.625px;">Although it may not be easy, there is always a way to do the right thing. While talking with a group of friends <span class="page-break" data-page="64"></span>at school, a young woman felt her heart drop when the conversation turned to criticizing the standards of the Church. She realized she couldn’t stay silent—she had to do something. Respectfully, she spoke of the love of Heavenly Father and how the commandments He set are to bless and protect His children. It would have been much easier for her to do nothing. But what mattered most? Blending in with the crowd? Or standing <em>out</em> as a witness of God at “all times and in all things, and in all places”?<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/33craven?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807762" id="p22" style="--height:489.635px;">If the restored Church of Jesus Christ is going to come out of obscurity, we must come out of obscurity. As covenant-keeping women, we must shine our gospel light all over the world by stepping up and standing out. We do this together as daughters of God—a force of 8.2 million women ages 11 and beyond, whose work is exactly the same. We are gathering Israel as we participate in the work of salvation and exaltation: striving to live the gospel of Jesus Christ, caring for others in need, inviting all to receive the gospel, and uniting families for eternity.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/33craven?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a> The gospel of Jesus Christ is a gospel of action and a gospel of joy! Let us not underestimate our capacity to do those things that matter most. Our divine heritage gives us courage and confidence to do and be all that our loving Heavenly Father knows we can be.</p>
<p data-aid="149807769" id="p23" style="--height:28.8021px;">The youth theme for this year is from <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/ot/prov/3.5-6?lang=eng#p5">Proverbs 3:5–6</a>:</p>
<p data-aid="149807776" id="p24" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Trust in the Lord with all thine heart; and lean not unto thine own understanding.</p>
<p data-aid="149807783" id="p25" style="--height:57.6042px;">“In all thy ways acknowledge him, and he shall direct thy paths.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807790" id="p26" style="--height:86.4063px;">A key component of trusting in the Lord is moving forward, believing He will guide us even when we don’t have all the answers.</p>
<p data-aid="149807797" id="p27" style="--height:115.208px;">Sisters, it’s not about the ice cream. And it’s not about doing more. It’s about doing what matters. It’s applying the doctrine of Christ in our lives as we strive to become more like Him.</p>
<p data-aid="149807804" id="p28" style="--height:230.417px;">The more we do to stay firmly on the covenant path, the more our faith in Jesus Christ will grow. The more our faith grows, the more we will desire to repent. And the more we repent, the more we will strengthen our covenant relationship with God. That covenant relationship draws us to the temple because keeping temple covenants is how we endure to the end.</p>
<p data-aid="149807811" id="p29" style="--height:115.208px;">As we center our lives on Jesus Christ, we will be guided to do what mattereth most. And we will be blessed with spiritual strength, contentment, and with <em>joy</em>! In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149808283" id="p1" style="--height:86.4063px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="65"></span>In 1979 President Spencer&nbsp;W. Kimball was in the hospital and asked his wife, Camilla, to read his talk to a general women’s meeting.</p>
<p data-aid="149808292" id="p2" style="--height:316.823px;"><strong>Sister Camilla Kimball:</strong> “Much of the major growth that is coming to the Church in the last days will come because many of the good women of the world (in whom there is often such an inner sense of spirituality) will be drawn to the Church in large numbers. This will happen to the degree that the women of the Church reflect righteousness and articulateness in their lives and to the degree that the women of the Church are seen as distinct and different—in happy ways﻿—from the women of the world.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/34video?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808302" id="p3" style="--height:230.417px;"><strong>President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson:</strong> “My dear sisters, you who are our vital associates during this winding-up scene, the day that President Kimball foresaw is today. You are the women he foresaw! Your virtue, light, love, knowledge, courage, character, faith, and righteous lives will draw good women of the world, along with their families, to the Church in unprecedented numbers!</p>
<p data-aid="149808311" id="p4" style="--height:172.813px;">“We … need your strength, your conversion, your conviction, your ability to lead, your wisdom, and your voices. The kingdom of God is not and cannot be complete without women who make sacred covenants and then keep them, women who can speak with the power and authority of God!&nbsp;…</p>
<p data-aid="149808320" id="p5" style="--height:288.021px;">“… Whatever your calling, whatever your circumstances, we need your impressions, your insights, and <span class="page-break" data-page="66"></span>your inspiration. We need you to speak up and speak out in ward and stake councils. We need each married sister to speak as ‘a <em>contributing</em> and <em>full</em> partner’ as you unite with your husband in governing your family. Married or single, you sisters possess distinctive capabilities and special intuition you have received as gifts from God. We brethren cannot duplicate your unique influence.</p>
<p data-aid="149808330" id="p6" style="--height:57.6042px;">“We know that the culminating act of all creation was the creation of woman! We need your strength!&nbsp;…</p>
<p data-aid="149808341" id="p7" style="--height:144.01px;">“… I thank you, my dear sisters, and bless you to rise to your full stature, to fulfill the measure of your creation, as we walk arm in arm in this sacred work. Together we will help prepare the world for the Second Coming of the Lord.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/34video?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a></p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149808324" id="p1" style="--height:201.615px;">Sisters, what a joy to gather in a worldwide sisterhood! As women who make and keep covenants with God, we share spiritual bonds that help us meet the challenges of our day and prepare us for the Second Coming of Jesus Christ. And keeping those covenants allows us to be women of influence who can draw others to the Savior.</p>
<p data-aid="149808334" id="p2" style="--height:345.625px;">Those who have been baptized covenanted on that never-to-be-forgotten day to take Jesus Christ’s name upon them, to always remember Him, to keep His commandments, and to serve Him to the end. When we do these things, Heavenly Father promises to forgive our sins and give us the companionship of the Holy Ghost. These blessings start us on the path that, if we press forward and endure to the end, will allow us to live with Him and His Son in the celestial kingdom. <em>Every</em> baptized person has the promise of these privileges if she or he keeps the covenant made that special day.</p>
<p data-aid="149808344" id="p3" style="--height:316.823px;">Those who make further covenants in the temple receive powerful promises conditioned on personal faithfulness. We solemnly promise to obey God’s commandments, live the gospel of Jesus Christ, be morally pure, and dedicate our time and talents to the Lord. In return, God promises blessings in this life and the opportunity to return to Him.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> In that process, we are given, or endowed with, the power to discern between truth and error, between right and wrong, amid the confusing and negative voices that bombard us. What a powerful gift!</p>
<p data-aid="149808354" id="p4" style="--height:259.219px;">In preparation for my first trip to the temple, my mother and experienced Relief Society sisters helped me select the items I would need, including beautiful ceremonial clothing. But the most important preparation came <span class="page-break" data-page="67"></span>even before knowing what to wear. After interviewing me to determine if I was worthy, my bishop explained the covenants I would make. His careful explanation gave me the chance to think about and be prepared to make those covenants.</p>
<p data-aid="149808364" id="p5" style="--height:345.625px;">When the day came, I participated with a feeling of gratitude and peace. Even though I did not understand the full significance of the covenants I made, I did know that I was bound to God through those covenants and was promised blessings I could scarcely comprehend if I kept them. Since that first experience, I have been continually assured that keeping the covenants we make with God allows us to draw upon the Savior’s power, which strengthens us in our inevitable trials, provides protection from the adversary’s influence, and prepares us for eternal glory.</p>
<p data-aid="149808374" id="p6" style="--height:288.021px;">Life’s experiences can range from humorous to heart-wrenching, from grim to glorious. Each experience helps us understand more about our Father’s encompassing love and our capacity to change through the Savior’s gift of grace. Keeping our covenants allows the Savior’s power to cleanse us as we learn through experience—whether it is a minor misjudgment or a major failing. Our Redeemer is there to catch us when we fall <em>if</em> we turn to Him.</p>
<div><div class="imageWrapper-wTPPD"><img id="img1" data-img-id="e9240574b11e11ecb8b9eeeeac1e781d433ff547" data-assetid="e9240574b11e11ecb8b9eeeeac1e781d433ff547" data-missing-asset="false" data-width="500" data-height="323" data-aspect-ratio="1.5479876160990713" alt="Letting the Youth LeadÃƒÂ¢Ã‚Â€Ã‚Â”Rappelling to Become Anchored in Jesus Christ" class="imageWithModal-bCN6D" height="323" src="https://assets.ldscdn.org/fe/a6/fea6fa0fd889589b8830ab2ae768760a2f63c6f7/letting_the_youth_lead_rappelling.png" srcset="https://assets.ldscdn.org/25/76/257648575ea6c26dfe113266faab4efa03c5a723/letting_the_youth_lead_rappelling.png 60w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/03/29/032965c632f984a05e43112e904d77655f2e8d4f/letting_the_youth_lead_rappelling.png 100w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/60/b9/60b95e654378e957a741d57b3ba4d868bc69a660/letting_the_youth_lead_rappelling.png 200w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/27/b1/27b1d034e82c2631f54616df5db50b5c06ae3128/letting_the_youth_lead_rappelling.png 250w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/8d/d5/8dd5a2ce79f0c3ff839af48b5652f49ad2633f65/letting_the_youth_lead_rappelling.png 320w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/fe/a6/fea6fa0fd889589b8830ab2ae768760a2f63c6f7/letting_the_youth_lead_rappelling.png 500w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/e3/73/e37306e0e3fb0a8b6ab58802a2642aa30a08e24d/letting_the_youth_lead_rappelling.png 640w" width="500"></div></div>
<p data-aid="149808384" id="p7" style="--height:374.427px;">Have you ever stood on a high cliff with your toes on its edge and your back to the abyss below? In rappelling, even though you are securely connected to a system of strong ropes and equipment that can deliver you to safety, standing on the edge is still heart-racing. Stepping backward off the cliff and swinging into thin air requires trust in an anchor secured to an immovable object. It demands trust in the person who will apply tension to the rope as you descend. And although the equipment provides you with some ability to control your descent, you must have confidence that your partner will not allow you to fall.</p>
<div><div class="imageWrapper-wTPPD"><figure class="imageWithModal-bCN6D loadImageItem-u5D4D" title="Letting the Youth LeadÃ¢Â€Â”Rappelling to Become Anchored in Jesus Christ"><img width="500" height="323" alt=""><div class="container-W4jed"><div class="innerFlex-R9N_u"><svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" role="presentation" style="width: 1.5rem; height: 1.5rem;"> <path fill="currentColor" d="M20 4.75L19.25 4v16l.75-.75H4l.75.75V4L4 4.75h16zM3.25 4v16c0 .414.336.75.75.75h16a.75.75 0 0 0 .75-.75V4a.75.75 0 0 0-.75-.75H4a.75.75 0 0 0-.75.75zm11.07 8.888c.23-.357.606-.353.828-.008l2.887 4.482c.227.352.06.638-.357.638H6.326c-.421 0-.581-.3-.37-.648l4.006-6.622c.217-.358.567-.359.793.014l2.396 3.96 1.17-1.816zm1.59-2.735c1.14 0 2.066-.907 2.066-2.026 0-1.12-.926-2.027-2.067-2.027s-2.066.907-2.066 2.027c0 1.119.925 2.026 2.066 2.026z"> </path></svg><div class="sc-1szn76m-0 dODiQr i18nString-raclU">Image</div><div class="sc-1szn76m-0 dODiQr title-RrK9J">Letting the Youth LeadÃ¢Â€Â”Rappelling to Become Anchored in Jesus Christ</div></div></div></figure></div></div>
<div><div class="imageWrapper-wTPPD"><figure class="imageWithModal-bCN6D loadImageItem-u5D4D" title="Letting the Youth LeadÃƒÂ¢Ã‚Â€Ã‚Â”Rappelling to Become Anchored in Jesus Christ"><img width="500" height="323" alt=""><div class="container-W4jed"><div class="innerFlex-R9N_u"><svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" role="presentation" style="width: 1.5rem; height: 1.5rem;"> <path fill="currentColor" d="M20 4.75L19.25 4v16l.75-.75H4l.75.75V4L4 4.75h16zM3.25 4v16c0 .414.336.75.75.75h16a.75.75 0 0 0 .75-.75V4a.75.75 0 0 0-.75-.75H4a.75.75 0 0 0-.75.75zm11.07 8.888c.23-.357.606-.353.828-.008l2.887 4.482c.227.352.06.638-.357.638H6.326c-.421 0-.581-.3-.37-.648l4.006-6.622c.217-.358.567-.359.793.014l2.396 3.96 1.17-1.816zm1.59-2.735c1.14 0 2.066-.907 2.066-2.026 0-1.12-.926-2.027-2.067-2.027s-2.066.907-2.066 2.027c0 1.119.925 2.026 2.066 2.026z"> </path></svg><div class="sc-1szn76m-0 dODiQr i18nString-raclU">Image</div><div class="sc-1szn76m-0 dODiQr title-RrK9J">Letting the Youth LeadÃƒÂ¢Ã‚Â€Ã‚Â”Rappelling to Become Anchored in Jesus Christ</div></div></div></figure></div></div>
<p data-aid="149808394" id="p8" style="--height:230.417px;">I vividly remember rappelling with a group of young women. I was first in the group to go. As I stepped backwards off the cliff, I began to fall without control. Gratefully, the rope jerked and my too-rapid descent was stopped. As I dangled halfway down the jagged rock face, I prayed fervently for whomever or whatever was keeping me from dropping onto the rocks.</p>
<p data-aid="149808404" id="p9" style="--height:345.625px;">Later, I learned that the anchor bolt had not been securely set, and as I stepped off the edge, the person belaying me was jerked on his back and pulled towards the edge of the cliff. Somehow, he wedged his feet against some rocks. Stabilized in that position, he was able to laboriously lower me, hand over hand, with the rope. Although I couldn’t see him, I knew he was working with all his strength to save me. Another friend was at the bottom of the cliff, prepared to catch me if the rope ceased to hold. As I came within reach, he caught my harness and lowered me to the ground.</p>
<p data-aid="149808414" id="p10" style="--height:259.219px;">With Jesus Christ as our anchor and perfect partner, we are assured of His loving strength in trial and of eventual deliverance through Him. As President M.&nbsp;Russell Ballard taught: “Faith in God and in his Son, the Lord Jesus Christ, is the … anchor we must have in our lives to hold us fast during times of social turbulence and wickedness. … Our faith … must be centered in Jesus Christ, his life and his atonement, and in the restoration of his gospel.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808424" id="p19" style="--height:345.625px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="68"></span>The spiritual equipment that keeps us from being broken on the rocks of adversity is our testimony of Jesus Christ and the covenants we make. We can rely on these supports to guide and carry us to safety. As our willing partner, the Savior will not allow us to fall beyond His reach. Even in our times of suffering and sorrow, He is there to lift and encourage. His power helps us recover from the often-devastating impact of others’ choices. However, we each must put on the harness and make sure the knots are securely tied. We must choose to be anchored to the Savior, to be bound to Him by our covenants.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808435" id="p11" style="--height:230.417px;">How do we strengthen that anchor? We pray with a humble heart, study and ponder the scriptures, take the sacrament with a spirit of repentance and reverence, strive to keep the commandments, and follow the prophet’s counsel. And as we fulfill our everyday tasks in “higher and holier”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a> ways, we become more connected to the Savior and, at the same time, help others come unto Him.</p>
<p data-aid="149808446" id="p12" style="--height:432.031px;">What does that “higher and holier” way look like? We try to live the gospel in all our interactions. We care for those in need by truly ministering, expressing love through simple service. We share the good news of the gospel with those who need peace and strength and “know not where to find it.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a> We work to unite families for eternity on both sides of the veil. And for those who have made covenants in the house of the Lord, as President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson explained, “Each adult temple patron will wear the sacred garment of the priesthood, [which] … reminds us … to walk on the covenant path each day in a higher and holier way.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> These actions are not just an occasional splurge but are essential to our daily happiness—and eternal joy.</p>
<p data-aid="149808457" id="p13" style="--height:316.823px;">There is nothing more important to our eternal progress than keeping our covenants with God. When our temple covenants are in force, we can trust in a joyful reunion with loved ones on the other side of the veil. That child or parent or spouse who has left mortality is hoping with all his or her heart that you will be true to the covenants that bind you together. If we disregard or treat lightly our covenants with God, we are putting those eternal ties in danger. Now is the time to repent, repair, and try again.</p>
<p data-aid="149808469" id="p14" style="--height:316.823px;">Happiness is hollow if we exchange the blessings of eternal joy for momentary ease. No matter our age, that is the absolute truth: the key to lasting happiness is living the gospel of Jesus Christ and keeping our covenants. Our prophet, President Nelson, has affirmed that “our ultimate security and our only enduring happiness lies in holding to the iron rod of the restored gospel of Jesus Christ, complete with its covenants and ordinances. When we do so, we can safely navigate through rough waters because we have access to God’s power.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808481" id="p15" style="--height:403.229px;">Many of us are experiencing rough waters. As we are tossed by waves of adversity and are sometimes blinded by the torrents of tears that come in those difficulties, we may not know which direction to paddle our life’s boat. We may not even think we have the strength to get to shore. Remembering <em>who</em> you are—a beloved child of God—<em>why</em> you are on the earth, and your <em>goal</em> of living with God and your loved ones can clear your vision and point you in the right direction. In the midst of the storm, there is a bright light to show the way. “I am the light which shineth in darkness,” Jesus declared.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a> We are assured of safety when we look to His light and maintain the integrity of our covenants.</p>
<p data-aid="149808493" id="p16" style="--height:518.438px;">It has been a privilege to meet women of all ages living in a wide variety of circumstances who are keeping their covenants. Each day, they look to the Lord and His prophet for guidance, rather than to popular media. Despite their individual challenges and the detrimental philosophies of the world that try to dissuade them from keeping their covenants, they are determined to stay on the covenant path. They rely on the promise of “all that [the] Father <span class="page-break" data-page="69"></span>hath.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a> And whatever your age, each of you women who has made covenants with God has the ability to hold up the Lord’s light and lead others to Him.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a> Through your keeping of covenants, He will bless you with His priesthood power and enable you to have a profound influence on all with whom you interact. As President Nelson declared, you are the women who will fulfill the prophecies that have been foretold!<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808505" id="p17" style="--height:547.24px;">Dear sisters, above all else, stay on the covenant path to Jesus Christ! We have been blessed to come to earth when temples dot the globe. Making and keeping temple covenants is available to every worthy member of the Church. Young adults, you don’t need to wait until marriage or a mission to make those sacred covenants. You can prepare as a young woman to receive the protection and strength temple covenants give as soon after the age of 18 as you are ready and feel a desire to honor those temple covenants.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a> You who have already received the blessings of the temple, don’t let detractors or distractions pull you away from eternal truths. Study and ask trusted sources for greater understanding of the sacred significance of the covenants you have made. Go to the temple as often as you can and listen to the Spirit. You will feel sweet reassurance that you are on the Lord’s path. You will find the courage to continue as well as to bring others with you.</p>
<p data-aid="149808517" id="p18" style="--height:172.813px;">I testify that as we choose to make covenants with Heavenly Father and access the power of the Savior to keep them, we will be blessed with more happiness in this life than we can now imagine and a glorious eternal life to come.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/35bingham?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149807558" id="p1" style="--height:316.823px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="70"></span>Dear sisters, thank you for being here. I am honored to participate in this women’s session of general conference. On occasion I have also been privileged to attend Young Women classes. But let me point out the obvious—I am not young, and I am not a woman! I learned, however, that I feel less out of place if I can recite the Young Women theme along with the young women. The profound doctrine taught in the Young Women theme<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> is important for young women, but it is applicable to all, including those of us who are not young women.</p>
<p data-aid="149807565" id="p2" style="--height:259.219px;">The Young Women theme begins, “I am a beloved daughter of heavenly parents, with a divine nature and eternal destiny.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> This statement contains four important truths. First, you are a beloved daughter. Nothing you do—or do not do—can change that. God loves you because you are His spirit daughter. Sometimes we may not feel His love, but it is always there. God’s love is perfect.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> Our ability to sense that love is not.</p>
<p data-aid="149807574" id="p3" style="--height:259.219px;">The Spirit plays a pivotal role in communicating God’s love to us.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a> Yet the influence of the Holy Ghost can be obscured “by strong emotions, such as anger, hate, … [or] fear, … like trying to savor the delicate flavor of a grape while eating a jalapeño pepper. … [One flavor] completely overpowers the other.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a> So too, behaviors that distance us from the Holy Ghost, including sin,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> make it difficult for us to perceive God’s love for us.</p>
<p data-aid="149807583" id="p4" style="--height:230.417px;">Similarly, our sense of God’s love may be blunted by challenging circumstances and physical or mental illness, among other things. In all these cases, the counsel of trusted leaders or professionals can often be beneficial. We can also try to improve our receptivity to God’s love by asking ourselves, “Is my love for God constant, or do I love Him when I have good days but not so much when I have bad days?”</p>
<p data-aid="149807592" id="p5" style="--height:201.615px;">The second truth is that we have heavenly parents, a father and a mother.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a> The doctrine of a Heavenly Mother comes by revelation and is a distinctive belief among Latter-day Saints. President Dallin&nbsp;H. Oaks explained the importance of this truth: “Our theology begins with heavenly parents. Our highest aspiration is to be like them.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807601" id="p6" style="--height:288.021px;">Very little has been revealed about Mother in Heaven, but what we do know is summarized in a gospel topic found in our Gospel Library application.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a> Once you have read what is there, you will know everything that I know about the subject. I wish I knew more. You too may still have questions and want to find more answers. Seeking greater understanding is an important part of our spiritual development, but please be cautious. Reason cannot replace revelation.</p>
<p data-aid="149807610" id="p7" style="--height:230.417px;">Speculation will not lead to greater spiritual knowledge, but it can lead us to deception or divert our focus from what has been revealed.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a> For example, the Savior taught His disciples, “Always pray unto the Father in my name.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a> We follow this pattern and direct our worship to our Heavenly Father in the name of Jesus Christ and do not pray to Heavenly Mother.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807619" id="p9" style="--height:403.229px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="75"></span>Ever since God appointed prophets, they have been authorized to speak on His behalf. But they do not pronounce doctrines fabricated “of [their] own mind”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> or teach what has not been revealed. Consider the words of the Old Testament prophet Balaam, who was offered a bribe to curse the Israelites to benefit Moab. Balaam said, “If [the king of Moab] would give me his house full of silver and gold, I cannot go beyond the word of the Lord my God, to do less or more.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> Latter-day prophets are similarly constrained. Demanding revelation from God is both arrogant and unproductive. Instead, we wait on the Lord and His timetable to reveal His truths through the means that He has established.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807628" id="p10" style="--height:374.427px;">The third truth in the opening paragraph of the Young Women theme is that we have “a divine nature.” This is intrinsic to who we are. It is spiritually “genetic,” inherited from our heavenly parents,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> and requires no effort on our part. This is our most important identity, regardless of how else we choose to identify ourselves. Understanding this profound truth is important for everyone but especially for individuals belonging to groups who have been historically marginalized, oppressed, or subjugated. Remember that your most important identity relates to your divine nature as a child of God.</p>
<p data-aid="149807637" id="p11" style="--height:403.229px;">The fourth truth is that we have an “eternal destiny.” Such a destiny will not be forced on us. After death, we will receive what we have qualified for and “enjoy [only] that which [we] are willing to receive.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a> Realizing our eternal destiny is dependent on our choices. It requires making and keeping sacred covenants. This covenant path is the way we come unto Christ and is based on absolute truth and eternal, unchanging law. We cannot create our own path and expect God’s promised outcomes. To expect His blessings while not following the eternal laws upon which they are predicated<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a> is misguided, like thinking we can touch a hot stove and “decide” not to be burned.</p>
<p data-aid="149807645" id="p12" style="--height:345.625px;">You may know that I used to treat patients with heart failure. Their best outcomes were obtained by following established, evidence-based treatment plans. Despite knowing this, some patients tried to negotiate a different treatment plan. They said, “I don’t want to take so many medications” or “I don’t want to undergo so many follow-up tests.” Of course, patients were free to make their own decisions, but if they deviated from optimal treatment plans, their results suffered. Patients with heart failure cannot choose an inferior course and then blame their cardiologist for inferior outcomes.</p>
<p data-aid="149807653" id="p13" style="--height:288.021px;">The same is true for us. Heavenly Father’s prescribed path leads to the best eternal outcomes. We are free to choose, but we cannot choose the consequences of not following the revealed path.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a> The Lord has said, “That which breaketh a law, and abideth not by law, but seeketh to become a law unto itself, … cannot be sanctified by law, neither by mercy, justice, nor judgment.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a> We cannot deviate from Heavenly Father’s course and then blame Him for inferior outcomes.</p>
<p data-aid="149807662" id="p14" style="--height:345.625px;">The second paragraph in the Young Women theme reads: “As a disciple of Jesus Christ, I strive to become like Him. I seek and act upon personal revelation and minister to others in His holy name.” We can develop a testimony of Jesus Christ by acting in faith.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a> We can claim the spiritual gift “to know that Jesus Christ is the Son of God, and that he was crucified for the sins of the world.” Or we can receive the gift to believe on the words of those who do know,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a> until we know for ourselves. We can follow the Savior’s teachings and help others come unto Him. In this way, we join Him in His work.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807671" id="p15" style="--height:316.823px;">The Young Women theme continues, “I will stand as a witness of God at all times and in all things and in all places.” All members of the Church are needed as witnesses of God,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note24" data-scroll-id="note24"><sup class="marker">24</sup></a> although Apostles and Seventies are commissioned as special witnesses of the name of Christ.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note25" data-scroll-id="note25"><sup class="marker">25</sup></a> Imagine a soccer match in which only the goalie protects the goal. Without the help of <span class="page-break" data-page="76"></span>the other team players, the goalie will not be able to adequately defend the goal, and the team will always lose. So too, everyone is needed on the Lord’s team.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note26" data-scroll-id="note26"><sup class="marker">26</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807679" id="p16" style="--height:345.625px;">The final paragraph of the Young Women theme begins, “As I strive to qualify for exaltation, I cherish the gift of repentance and seek to improve each day.” Because of the Savior’s atoning sacrifice, we can repent, learn from our mistakes, and not be condemned by them. President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson taught: “Too many people consider repentance as punishment. … But this feeling of being penalized is engendered by Satan. He tries to block us from looking to Jesus Christ, who stands with open arms, hoping and willing to heal, forgive, cleanse, strengthen, purify, and sanctify us.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note27" data-scroll-id="note27"><sup class="marker">27</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807687" id="p17" style="--height:259.219px;">When we sincerely repent, no spiritual scar remains, no matter what we have done, how serious it was, or how many times we repeated it.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note28" data-scroll-id="note28"><sup class="marker">28</sup></a> As often as we repent and seek forgiveness with real intent, we can be forgiven.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note29" data-scroll-id="note29"><sup class="marker">29</sup></a> What a remarkable gift from our Savior, Jesus Christ!<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note30" data-scroll-id="note30"><sup class="marker">30</sup></a> The Holy Ghost can assure us that we have been forgiven. As we sense joy and peace,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note31" data-scroll-id="note31"><sup class="marker">31</sup></a> guilt is swept away,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note32" data-scroll-id="note32"><sup class="marker">32</sup></a> and we are no longer tormented by our sin.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note33" data-scroll-id="note33"><sup class="marker">33</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807695" id="p18" style="--height:259.219px;">Even after sincere repentance, however, we may stumble. Stumbling does not mean that the repentance was inadequate but may simply reflect human weakness. How comforting to know that “the Lord sees weaknesses differently than He [sees] rebellion.” We should not doubt the Savior’s ability to help us with our weaknesses, because “when the Lord speaks of weaknesses, it is always with mercy.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note34" data-scroll-id="note34"><sup class="marker">34</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807703" id="p19" style="--height:230.417px;">The Young Women theme concludes, “With faith, I will strengthen my home and family, make and keep sacred covenants, and receive the ordinances and blessings of the holy temple.” Strengthening home and family may mean forging the first link in a chain of faithfulness, carrying on a legacy of faith, or restoring it.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note35" data-scroll-id="note35"><sup class="marker">35</sup></a> Regardless, strength comes through faith in Jesus Christ and by making sacred covenants.</p>
<p data-aid="149807711" id="p20" style="--height:345.625px;">In the temple, we learn who we are and where we have been. The Roman philosopher Cicero said, “To be ignorant of what occurred before you were born is to remain always a child.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note36" data-scroll-id="note36"><sup class="marker">36</sup></a> He was, of course, referring to secular history, but his astute observation can be expanded. We live as perpetual children if we are ignorant of the eternal perspective gained in temples. There we grow up in the Lord, “receive a fulness of the Holy Ghost,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note37" data-scroll-id="note37"><sup class="marker">37</sup></a> and become more fully committed as disciples of the Savior.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note38" data-scroll-id="note38"><sup class="marker">38</sup></a> As we keep our covenants, we receive God’s power in our lives.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note39" data-scroll-id="note39"><sup class="marker">39</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807718" id="p21" style="--height:259.219px;">I invite you to center your life on Jesus Christ and remember the foundational truths in the Young Women theme. If you are willing, the Holy Ghost will guide you. Our Heavenly Father wants you to become His heir and receive all that He has.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/36renlund?lang=eng#note40" data-scroll-id="note40"><sup class="marker">40</sup></a> He cannot offer you more. He cannot promise you more. He loves you more than you know and wants you to be happy in this life and in the life to come. In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149808345" id="p1" style="--height:230.417px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="78"></span>As Job in the Old Testament, in a time of suffering some might feel that God has abandoned them. Because we know that God has power to prevent or remove any affliction, we may be tempted to complain if He does not do it, perhaps questioning, “If God does not grant the help I pray for, how can I have faith in Him?” At one point in his intense trials, righteous Job said: </p>
<p data-aid="149808355" id="p23" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Then know that God has wronged me and drawn his net around me. </p>
<p data-aid="149808365" id="p24" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Though I cry, ‘I’ve been wronged!’ I get no response; though I call for help, there is no justice.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808375" id="p2" style="--height:259.219px;">In His response to Job, God demands, “Wilt thou condemn me, that thou mayest be righteous?”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> Or in other words, “Will you even put me in the wrong? Will you condemn me that you may be justified?”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> Jehovah forcefully reminds Job of His omnipotence and omniscience, and Job in deepest humility admits he possesses nothing even close to the knowledge, power, and righteousness of God and cannot stand in judgment of the Almighty:</p>
<p data-aid="149808385" id="p32" style="--height:57.6042px;">“I know that thou canst do every thing,” he said, “and that no thought can be withholden from thee.</p>
<p data-aid="149808395" id="p33" style="--height:57.6042px;">“… I uttered that I understood not; things too wonderful for me, which I knew not.&nbsp;…</p>
<p data-aid="149808405" id="p34" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Wherefore I abhor myself, and repent in dust and ashes.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808415" id="p35" style="--height:86.4063px;">In the end, Job was privileged to see the Lord, and “the Lord blessed the latter end of Job more than his beginning.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808426" id="p3" style="--height:316.823px;">It truly is folly for us with our mortal myopia to presume to judge God, to think, for example, “I’m not happy, so God must be doing something wrong.” To us, His mortal children in a fallen world, who know so little of past, present, and future, He declares, “All things are present with me, for I know them all.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> Jacob wisely cautions: “Seek not to counsel the Lord, but to take counsel from his hand. For behold, ye yourselves know that he counseleth in wisdom, and in justice, and in great mercy, over all his works.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808437" id="p4" style="--height:432.031px;">Some misunderstand the promises of God to mean that obedience to Him yields specific outcomes on a fixed schedule. They might think, “If I diligently serve a full-time mission, God will bless me with a happy marriage and children” or “If I refrain from doing schoolwork on the Sabbath, God will bless me with good grades” or “If I pay tithing, God will bless me with that job I’ve been wanting.” If life doesn’t fall out precisely this way or according to an expected timetable, they may feel betrayed by God. But things are not so mechanical in the divine economy. We ought not to think of God’s plan as a cosmic vending machine where we (1) select a desired blessing, (2) insert the required sum of good works, and (3) the order is promptly delivered.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808448" id="p5" style="--height:345.625px;">God will indeed honor His covenants and promises to each of us. We need not worry about that.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a> The atoning power of Jesus Christ—who descended below all things and then ascended on high<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a> and who possesses all power in heaven and in earth<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a>—ensures that God can and will fulfill His promises. It is essential that we honor and obey His laws, but not every blessing predicated on obedience to law<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a> is shaped, designed, and timed according to our expectations. We do our best but must leave to Him the management of blessings, both temporal and spiritual.</p>
<p data-aid="149808459" id="p6" style="--height:288.021px;">President Brigham Young explained that his faith was not built <span class="page-break" data-page="79"></span>on certain outcomes or blessings but on his witness of and relationship with Jesus Christ. He said: “My faith is not placed upon the Lord’s working upon the islands of the sea, upon his bringing the people here, … nor upon the favors he bestows upon this people or upon that people, neither upon whether we are blessed or not blessed, but <em>my faith is placed upon the Lord Jesus Christ, and my knowledge I have received from him</em>.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808471" id="p39" style="--height:345.625px;">Our repentance and obedience, our service and sacrifices do matter. We want to be among those described by Ether as “always abounding in good works.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> But it is not so much because of some tally kept in celestial account books. These things matter because they engage us in God’s work and are the means by which we collaborate with Him in our own transformation from natural man to saint.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a> What our Heavenly Father offers us is Himself and His Son, a close and enduring relationship with Them through the grace and mediation of Jesus Christ, our Redeemer.</p>
<p data-aid="149808483" id="p36" style="--height:259.219px;">We are God’s children, set apart for immortality and eternal life. Our destiny is to be His heirs, “joint-heirs with Christ.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> Our Father is willing to guide each of us along His covenant path with steps designed to our individual need and tailored to His plan for our ultimate happiness with Him. We can anticipate a growing trust and faith in the Father and the Son, an increasing sense of Their love, and the consistent comfort and guidance of the Holy Spirit.</p>
<p data-aid="149808495" id="p8" style="--height:86.4063px;">Even so, this path cannot be easy for any of us. There is too much refining needed for it to be easy. Jesus said: </p>
<p data-aid="149808507" id="p25" style="--height:57.6042px;">“I am the true vine, and my Father is the husbandman. </p>
<p data-aid="149808519" id="p26" style="--height:115.208px;">“Every branch in me that beareth not fruit [the Father] taketh away: and every branch that beareth fruit, he purgeth it, that it may bring forth more fruit.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a> </p>
<p data-aid="149808531" id="p27" style="--height:144.01px;">The process of God-directed purging and purifying will, of necessity, be wrenching and painful at times. Recalling Paul’s expression, we are “joint-heirs with Christ; <em>if so be that we suffer with him</em>, that we may be also glorified together.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808543" id="p9" style="--height:201.615px;">So, in the midst of this refiner’s fire, rather than get angry with God, get close to God. Call upon the Father in the name of the Son. Walk with Them in the Spirit, day by day. Allow Them over time to manifest Their fidelity to you. Come truly to know Them and truly to know yourself.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a> Let God prevail.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a> The Savior reassures us:</p>
<p data-aid="149808555" id="p10" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Listen to him who is the advocate with the Father, who is pleading your cause before him—</p>
<p data-aid="149808567" id="p11" style="--height:144.01px;">“Saying: Father, behold the sufferings and death of him who did no sin, in whom thou wast well pleased; behold the blood of thy Son which was shed, the blood of him whom thou gavest that thyself might be glorified;</p>
<p data-aid="149808579" id="p12" style="--height:86.4063px;">“<em>Wherefore, Father, spare these my brethren [and my sisters] that believe on my name, that they may come unto me and have everlasting life</em>.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808591" id="p13" style="--height:201.615px;">Consider some examples of faithful men and women who trusted God, confident that His promised blessings would be upon them in life or in death. Their faith was based not on what God did or did not do in a particular circumstance or moment in time but on knowing Him as their benevolent Father and Jesus Christ as their faithful Redeemer.</p>
<p data-aid="149808603" id="p40" style="--height:259.219px;">When Abraham was about to be sacrificed by the Egyptian priest of Elkenah, he cried out to God to save him, and God did.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a> Abraham lived to become the father of the faithful through whose seed all the families of the earth would be blessed.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a> Earlier, on this very same altar, that same priest of Elkenah had offered up three virgins who “because of their virtue … would not bow down to worship gods of wood or of stone.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note24" data-scroll-id="note24"><sup class="marker">24</sup></a> They died there as martyrs.</p>
<p data-aid="149808615" id="p37" style="--height:489.635px;">Joseph of old, sold into slavery as a youth by his own brothers, in his <span class="page-break" data-page="80"></span>anguish turned to God. Gradually, he rose to prominence in his master’s house in Egypt but then had all this progress ripped away because of the false accusations of Potiphar’s wife. Joseph could have thought, “So prison is what I get for keeping the law of chastity.” Instead he continued to turn to God and was prospered even in prison. Joseph suffered a further crushing disappointment when the prisoner he befriended, despite his promise to help Joseph, forgot all about him after being restored to his position in Pharaoh’s court. In due course, as you know, the Lord intervened to put Joseph in the highest position of trust and power next to Pharaoh, enabling Joseph to save the house of Israel. Surely Joseph could attest “that all things work together for good to them that love God.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note25" data-scroll-id="note25"><sup class="marker">25</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808627" id="p38" style="--height:230.417px;">Abinadi was intent on fulfilling his divine commission. “I finish my message,” he said, “and then it matters not [what happens to me], if it so be that I am saved.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note26" data-scroll-id="note26"><sup class="marker">26</sup></a> He was not spared a martyr’s death, but assuredly he was saved in the kingdom of God, and his one precious convert, Alma, changed the course of Nephite history leading up to the coming of Christ.</p>
<p data-aid="149808639" id="p15" style="--height:259.219px;">Alma and Amulek were delivered from prison in Ammonihah in answer to their plea, and their persecutors were slain.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note27" data-scroll-id="note27"><sup class="marker">27</sup></a> Earlier, however, these same persecutors had cast believing women and their children into a raging fire. Alma, witnessing the horrific scene in agony, was constrained by the Spirit not to exercise the power of God to “save them from the flames,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note28" data-scroll-id="note28"><sup class="marker">28</sup></a> that they might be received up to God in glory.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note29" data-scroll-id="note29"><sup class="marker">29</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808651" id="p18" style="--height:259.219px;">The Prophet Joseph Smith languished in jail at Liberty, Missouri, powerless to help the Saints as they were pillaged and driven from their homes in the bitter cold of winter. “O God, where art thou?” Joseph cried. “How long shall thy hand be stayed?”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note30" data-scroll-id="note30"><sup class="marker">30</sup></a> In response, the Lord promised: “Thine adversity and thine afflictions shall be but a small moment; and then, if thou endure it well, God shall exalt thee on high. … Thou art not yet as Job.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note31" data-scroll-id="note31"><sup class="marker">31</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808662" id="p19" style="--height:57.6042px;">In the end, Joseph could declare with Job, “Though [God] slay me, yet will I trust in him.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note32" data-scroll-id="note32"><sup class="marker">32</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808674" id="p20" style="--height:86.4063px;">Elder Brook&nbsp;P. Hales related the story of Sister Patricia Parkinson, who was born with normal eyesight but by age 11 had gone blind. </p>
<p data-aid="149808686" id="p28" style="--height:374.427px;">Elder Hales recounted: “I’ve known Pat for many years and recently told her that I admired the fact that she is always positive and happy. She responded, ‘Well, you have not been at home with me, have you? I have my moments. I’ve had rather severe bouts of depression, and I’ve cried a lot.’ However, she added, ‘From the time I started losing my sight, it was strange, but I knew that Heavenly Father and the Savior were with my family and me. … To those who ask me if I am angry because I am blind, I respond, ‘Who would I be angry with? Heavenly Father is in this with me; I am not alone. He is with me all the time.’”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note33" data-scroll-id="note33"><sup class="marker">33</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808697" id="p22" style="--height:259.219px;">In the end, it is the blessing of a close and abiding relationship with the Father and the Son that we seek. It makes all the difference and is everlastingly worth the cost. We will testify with Paul “that the sufferings of this present [mortal] time are not worthy to be compared with the glory which shall be revealed in us.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note34" data-scroll-id="note34"><sup class="marker">34</sup></a> I bear witness that no matter what our mortal experience may entail, we can trust God and find joy in Him. </p>
<p data-aid="149808708" id="p29" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Trust in the Lord with all thine heart; and lean not unto thine own understanding. </p>
<p data-aid="149808718" id="p30" style="--height:57.6042px;">“In all thy ways acknowledge him, and he shall direct thy paths.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/41christofferson?lang=eng#note35" data-scroll-id="note35"><sup class="marker">35</sup></a> </p>
<p data-aid="149808728" id="p31" style="--height:28.8021px;">In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149807576" id="p1" style="--height:201.615px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="81"></span>A few years ago, at a family gathering, my then-eight-year-old nephew William asked our oldest son, Briton, if he would like to play ball with him. Briton enthusiastically responded, “Yes! I would love to!” After they had been playing for quite some time, a ball got away from Briton, and he accidentally broke one of his grandparents’ antique pots. </p>
<p data-aid="149807587" id="p31" style="--height:201.615px;">Briton felt awful. As he began picking up the broken pieces, William walked over to his cousin and lovingly patted him on the back. He then comforted, “Don’t worry, Briton. I broke something at Grandma and Grandpa’s house once, and Grandma put her arm around me and said, ‘It’s OK, William. You are only five.’” </p>
<p data-aid="149807596" id="p32" style="--height:28.8021px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="82"></span>To which Briton responded, “But, William, I’m 23!”</p>
<p data-aid="149807605" id="p2" style="--height:172.813px;">We can learn much from the scriptures about how our Savior, Jesus Christ, will help us successfully navigate the things in our lives that are broken, no matter our age. He can heal broken relationships with God, broken relationships with others, and broken parts of ourselves.</p>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807614" id="title2" style="--height:33.6111px;">Broken Relationships with God</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807623" id="p3" style="--height:374.427px;">While the Savior was teaching in the temple, a woman was brought to Him by the scribes and Pharisees. We do not know her full story, just that she was “taken in adultery.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> Often the scriptures give only a small portion of someone’s life, and based on that portion, we sometimes tend to exalt or condemn. No one’s life can be understood by one magnificent moment or one regrettable public disappointment. The purpose of these scriptural accounts is to help us see that Jesus Christ was the answer then, and He is the answer now. He knows our complete story and exactly what we suffer, as well as our capabilities and vulnerabilities.</p>
<p data-aid="149807632" id="p4" style="--height:172.813px;">Christ’s response to this precious daughter of God was “Neither do I condemn thee: go, and sin no more.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> Another way to say “go, and sin no more” could be “go forth and change.” The Savior was inviting her to repent: to change her behavior, her associations, the way she felt about herself, her heart. </p>
<p data-aid="149807641" id="p34" style="--height:201.615px;">Because of Christ, our decision to “go forth and change” can also allow us to “go forth and heal,” for He is the source of healing all that is broken in our lives. As the great Mediator and Advocate with the Father, Christ sanctifies and restores broken relationships—most important, our relationship with God.</p>
<p data-aid="149807649" id="p5" style="--height:316.823px;">The Joseph Smith Translation makes it clear that the woman <em>did</em> follow the Savior’s counsel and changed her life: “And the woman glorified God from that hour, and believed on his name.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> It is unfortunate that we do not know her name or other details about her life after this moment because it would have required great determination, humility, and faith in Jesus Christ for her to repent and change. What we do know is she was a woman who “believed on his name” with the understanding that she was not beyond the reach of His infinite and eternal sacrifice.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807657" id="title3" style="--height:33.6111px;">Broken Relationships with Others</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807666" id="p6" style="--height:115.208px;">In <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/luke/15?lang=eng">Luke chapter 15</a> we read a parable of a man who had two sons. The younger son asked his father for his inheritance, took his journey into a far country, and wasted his substance with riotous living.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807674" id="p7" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And when he had spent all, there arose a mighty famine in that land; and he began to be in want.</p>
<p data-aid="149807682" id="p8" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And he went and joined himself to a citizen of that country; and he sent him into his fields to feed swine.</p>
<p data-aid="149807690" id="p9" style="--height:86.4063px;">“And he would fain have filled his belly with the husks that the swine did eat: and no man gave unto him.</p>
<p data-aid="149807698" id="p10" style="--height:86.4063px;">“And when he came to himself, he said, How many hired servants of my father’s have bread enough and to spare, and I perish with hunger!</p>
<p data-aid="149807706" id="p11" style="--height:86.4063px;">“I will arise and go to my father, and will say unto him, Father, I have sinned against heaven, and before thee,</p>
<p data-aid="149807714" id="p12" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And am no more worthy to be called thy son: make me as one of thy hired servants.</p>
<p data-aid="149807721" id="p13" style="--height:115.208px;">“And he arose, and came to his father. But when he was yet a great way off, his father saw him, and had compassion, and ran, and fell on his neck, and kissed him.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807728" id="p14" style="--height:144.01px;">The fact that the father ran to his son, I believe, is significant. The personal hurt that the son had inflicted upon his father was surely deep and profound. Likewise, the father may have been genuinely embarrassed by his son’s actions.</p>
<p data-aid="149807735" id="p15" style="--height:144.01px;">So why didn’t the father wait for his son to apologize? Why didn’t he hold out for an offering of restitution and reconciliation before extending forgiveness and love? This is something I have often pondered.</p>
<p data-aid="149807742" id="p16" style="--height:259.219px;">The Lord teaches us that forgiving others is a universal commandment: “I, the Lord, will forgive whom I will forgive, but of you it is required to forgive all men.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> Extending forgiveness can take tremendous courage and humility. It can also take time. It requires us to put our faith and trust in the Lord as we assume accountability for the condition of our hearts. Here lies the significance and power of our agency. </p>
<p data-aid="149807749" id="p35" style="--height:201.615px;">With the depiction of this father in the parable of the prodigal son, the Savior emphasized that forgiveness is one of the noblest gifts we can give one another and most specifically <em>ourselves</em>. Unburdening our hearts through forgiveness isn’t always easy, but through the enabling power of Jesus Christ, it is possible.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807756" id="title4" style="--height:33.6111px;">Broken Parts of Ourselves</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807763" id="p17" style="--height:115.208px;">In <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/acts/3?lang=eng">Acts chapter 3</a> we learn about a <span class="page-break" data-page="83"></span>man who was born lame and “whom they laid daily at the gate of the temple which is called Beautiful, to ask alms of them that entered into the temple.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807770" id="p18" style="--height:115.208px;">The lame beggar was over 40 years old<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a> and had spent his entire life in a seemingly never-ending state of wanting and waiting, for he was dependent on the generosity of others.</p>
<p data-aid="149807777" id="p19" style="--height:57.6042px;">One day he saw “Peter and John about to go into the temple [and] asked an alms.</p>
<p data-aid="149807784" id="p20" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And Peter, fastening his eyes upon him with John, said, Look on us.</p>
<p data-aid="149807791" id="p21" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And he gave heed unto them, expecting to receive something of them.</p>
<p data-aid="149807798" id="p22" style="--height:86.4063px;">“Then Peter said, Silver and gold have I none; but such as I have give I thee: In the name of Jesus Christ of Nazareth rise up and walk.</p>
<p data-aid="149807805" id="p23" style="--height:86.4063px;">“And he took him by the right hand, and lifted him up: and immediately his feet and ankle bones received strength.</p>
<p data-aid="149807812" id="p24" style="--height:86.4063px;">“And he leaping up stood, and walked, and entered with them into the temple, walking, and leaping, and praising God.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807819" id="p25" style="--height:172.813px;">Oftentimes we can find ourselves, like the lame beggar at the gate of the temple, patiently—or sometimes impatiently—“wait[ing] upon the Lord.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a> Waiting to be healed physically or emotionally. Waiting for answers that penetrate the deepest part of our hearts. Waiting for a miracle.</p>
<p data-aid="149807826" id="p26" style="--height:259.219px;">Waiting upon the Lord can be a sacred place—a place of polishing and refining where we can come to know the Savior in a deeply personal way. Waiting upon the Lord may also be a place where we find ourselves asking, “O God, where art thou?”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a>—a place where spiritual perseverance requires us to exercise faith in Christ by intentionally choosing Him again and again and again. I know this place, and I understand this type of waiting.</p>
<p data-aid="149807833" id="p28" style="--height:230.417px;">I spent countless hours at a cancer treatment facility, united in my suffering with many who were yearning <span class="page-break" data-page="84"></span>to be healed. Some lived; others did not. I learned in a profound way that deliverance from our trials is different for each of us, and therefore our focus should be less about the <em>way</em> in which we are delivered and more about the Deliverer Himself. Our <em>emphasis</em> should always be on Jesus Christ! </p>
<p data-aid="149807839" id="p33" style="--height:172.813px;">Exercising faith in Christ means trusting not only in God’s will but also in His timing. For He knows exactly what we need and precisely when we need it. When we submit to the will of the Lord, we will ultimately receive substantially more than that which we had desired.</p>
<p data-aid="149807844" id="p29" style="--height:201.615px;">My dear friends, we all have something in our lives that is broken that needs to be mended, fixed, or healed. As we turn to the Savior, as we align our hearts and minds with Him, as we repent, He comes to us “with healing in his wings,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/42wright?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a> puts His arms lovingly around us, and says, “It’s OK. You are only 5—or 16, 23, 48, 64, 91. We can fix this together!”</p>
<p data-aid="149807849" id="p30" style="--height:144.01px;">I testify that there is nothing in your life that is broken that is beyond the curative, redeeming, and enabling power of Jesus Christ. In the sacred and holy name of He who is mighty to heal, Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</section>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149807584" id="p1" style="--height:316.823px;">Imagine with me, for a moment, standing on a mountain in Galilee, witnessing the wonder and glory of the resurrected Savior visiting His disciples. How awe-inspiring to consider personally hearing these words, which He shared with them, His solemn charge to “go ye therefore, and teach all nations, baptizing them in the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the Holy Ghost.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/43stevenson?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> Surely these words would empower, inspire, and move each of us, as they did His Apostles. Indeed, they devoted the rest of their lives to doing just that.</p>
<p data-aid="149807593" id="p2" style="--height:230.417px;">Interestingly, it wasn’t only the Apostles who took Jesus’s words to heart. Members of the early Church, from the newest to the most seasoned, took part in the Savior’s great commission, sharing the good news of the gospel with those they met and knew. The determination to share their testimony of Jesus Christ helped His newly established Church grow expansively.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/43stevenson?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807602" id="p3" style="--height:288.021px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="85"></span>We too, as Christ’s disciples, are invited to heed His commission today, as if we were there on that mountain in Galilee when He first proclaimed it. This commission began again in 1830, when Joseph Smith set apart his brother Samuel as an early missionary of the Church of Jesus Christ.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/43stevenson?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> Since that time, more than 1.5 million missionaries have traveled throughout the world teaching all nations and baptizing those who embrace the glad tidings of the restored gospel.</p>
<p data-aid="149807611" id="p4" style="--height:28.8021px;">This is our doctrine. Our fond desire.</p>
<p data-aid="149807620" id="p5" style="--height:230.417px;">From our young children to the eldest among us, we yearn for the time when we can heed the Savior’s call and share the gospel with the nations of the world. I am sure you young men and young women felt a similar empowering challenge from our prophet yesterday as he invited you to prepare for full-time missionary service just as the Savior did with His Apostles.</p>
<p data-aid="149807629" id="p6" style="--height:172.813px;">Like sprinters at the starting blocks, we wait with anticipation for the official invitation, complete with the prophet’s signature, signaling the start of the race! This desire is noble and inspirational; however, let’s consider this question: why don’t we <em>all</em> begin now?</p>
<p data-aid="149807638" id="p7" style="--height:144.01px;">You might ask, “How can I be a missionary without a name badge?” Or we tell ourselves, “The full-time missionaries are set apart to do this work. I would like to help but perhaps later when life has calmed down a bit.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807646" id="p8" style="--height:144.01px;">Brothers and sisters, it is much simpler than that! Gratefully, the Savior’s great commission can be accomplished through simple, easily understandable principles taught to each of us from childhood: love, share, and invite.</p>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807654" id="title2" style="--height:33.6111px;">Love</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807663" id="p9" style="--height:28.8021px;">The first thing we can do is love as Christ loved.</p>
<p data-aid="149807672" id="p10" style="--height:259.219px;">Our hearts are heavy with the human suffering and tensions that we see throughout the world during these tumultuous times. However, we can be also inspired by the outpouring of compassion and humanitarianism that has been demonstrated by people everywhere through their efforts to reach out to the marginalized—those displaced from their homes, separated from their families, or experiencing other forms of sorrow and despair.</p>
<p data-aid="149807680" id="p11" style="--height:259.219px;">Recently, news sources reported how a group of mothers in Poland, out of concern for desperate, fleeing families, left fully equipped strollers on a train station platform in a neat line, ready and waiting for refugee mothers and children who would need them at that border crossing as they deboarded a train. Surely, our Heavenly Father smiles upon acts of selfless charity such as these, for as we bear one another’s burdens, we “fulfil the law of Christ.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/43stevenson?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807688" id="p12" style="--height:86.4063px;">Whenever we show Christlike love toward our neighbor, we preach the gospel—even if we do not voice a single word.</p>
<p data-aid="149807696" id="p13" style="--height:172.813px;">Love for others is the eloquent expression of the second great commandment to love our neighbor;<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/43stevenson?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a> it shows the refining process of the Holy Spirit working within our own souls. By demonstrating Christ’s love to others, we may cause those who see our good works to “glorify [our] Father which is in heaven.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/43stevenson?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807704" id="p14" style="--height:28.8021px;">We do this expecting nothing in return.</p>
<p data-aid="149807712" id="p15" style="--height:86.4063px;">Our hope, of course, is they will accept our love and our message, though how they react is not within our control.</p>
<p data-aid="149807719" id="p16" style="--height:28.8021px;">What we do and who we are certainly are.</p>
<p data-aid="149807726" id="p17" style="--height:115.208px;">Through Christlike love for others, we preach the glorious, life-transforming properties of Christ’s <span class="page-break" data-page="86"></span>gospel, and we participate significantly in the fulfilling of His great commission.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807733" id="title3" style="--height:33.6111px;">Share</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807740" id="p18" style="--height:28.8021px;">The second thing we can do is share.</p>
<p data-aid="149807747" id="p19" style="--height:201.615px;">During the early months of the COVID-19 pandemic, Brother Wisan from Thailand felt prompted to share his feelings and impressions of what he was learning in his study of the Book of Mormon on his social media account. In one of his particularly personal posts, he shared a story of two Book of Mormon missionaries, Alma and Amulek.</p>
