<p data-aid="149807754" id="p20" style="--height:86.4063px;">His brother, Winai, although set in his religious beliefs, was touched by the post and responded, unexpectedly asking, “Can I get that book in Thai?”</p>
<p data-aid="149807761" id="p21" style="--height:86.4063px;">Wisan wisely arranged for a copy of the Book of Mormon to be delivered by two sister missionaries, who began teaching his brother.</p>
<p data-aid="149807768" id="p22" style="--height:144.01px;">Wisan joined in virtual lessons, during which he shared his feelings about the Book of Mormon. Winai learned to pray and study with a truth-seeking spirit, to accept and embrace the truth. Within months, Winai was baptized!</p>
<p data-aid="149807775" id="p23" style="--height:172.813px;">Wisan later said, “We have a responsibility to be an instrument in the hands of God, and we must be always ready for Him to do His work in His way through us.” Their family miracle came because Wisan simply shared the gospel in a normal and natural way.</p>
<p data-aid="149807782" id="p24" style="--height:115.208px;">We all share things with others. We do it often. We share what movies and food we like, funny things we see, places we visit, art we appreciate, quotes we’re inspired by.</p>
<p data-aid="149807789" id="p25" style="--height:86.4063px;">How might we simply add to the list of things we already share what we love about the gospel of Jesus Christ?</p>
<p data-aid="149807796" id="p26" style="--height:230.417px;">Elder Dieter&nbsp;F. Uchtdorf explained: “If someone asks about your weekend, don’t hesitate to talk about what you experienced at church. Tell about the little children who stood in front of a congregation and sang with eagerness how they are trying to be like Jesus. Talk about the group of youth who spent time helping the elderly in rest homes to compile personal histories.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/43stevenson?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807803" id="p27" style="--height:86.4063px;">Sharing isn’t about “selling” the gospel. You don’t have to write a sermon or correct someone’s incorrect perceptions.</p>
<p data-aid="149807810" id="p28" style="--height:86.4063px;">When it comes to missionary work, God doesn’t need you to be His sheriff; He does, however, ask that you be His sharer.</p>
<p data-aid="149807817" id="p29" style="--height:86.4063px;">By sharing our positive experiences in the gospel with others, we take part in fulfilling the Savior’s great commission.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807824" id="title4" style="--height:33.6111px;">Invite</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807831" id="p30" style="--height:28.8021px;">The third thing you can do is invite.</p>
<p data-aid="149807837" id="p31" style="--height:230.417px;">Sister Mayra is a recent convert from Ecuador. Her joy in the gospel skyrocketed immediately following her baptism as she invited friends and loved ones around her through social media accounts. Many family members and friends who saw her posts responded with questions. Mayra connected with them, often inviting them to her home to meet with the missionaries together.</p>
<p data-aid="149807842" id="p32" style="--height:259.219px;">Mayra’s parents, her siblings, her aunt, two cousins, and several of her friends were baptized because she courageously invited them to “come and see,” “come and serve,” and “come and belong.” Through her normal and natural invitations, over 20 people have accepted her invitation to be baptized members of the Church of Jesus Christ. This came about because Sister Mayra simply invited others to experience the joy she felt as a member of the Church.</p>
<div><div class="imageWrapper-wTPPD"><figure class="imageWithModal-bCN6D loadImageItem-u5D4D" title="Church Members"><img width="500" height="281" alt=""><div class="container-W4jed"><div class="innerFlex-R9N_u"><svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" role="presentation" style="width: 1.5rem; height: 1.5rem;"> <path fill="currentColor" d="M20 4.75L19.25 4v16l.75-.75H4l.75.75V4L4 4.75h16zM3.25 4v16c0 .414.336.75.75.75h16a.75.75 0 0 0 .75-.75V4a.75.75 0 0 0-.75-.75H4a.75.75 0 0 0-.75.75zm11.07 8.888c.23-.357.606-.353.828-.008l2.887 4.482c.227.352.06.638-.357.638H6.326c-.421 0-.581-.3-.37-.648l4.006-6.622c.217-.358.567-.359.793.014l2.396 3.96 1.17-1.816zm1.59-2.735c1.14 0 2.066-.907 2.066-2.026 0-1.12-.926-2.027-2.067-2.027s-2.066.907-2.066 2.027c0 1.119.925 2.026 2.066 2.026z"> </path></svg><div class="sc-1szn76m-0 dODiQr i18nString-raclU">Image</div><div class="sc-1szn76m-0 dODiQr title-RrK9J">Church Members</div></div></div></figure></div></div>
<p data-aid="149807847" id="p33" style="--height:288.021px;">There are hundreds of invitations we can extend to others. We can invite others to “come and see” a sacrament service, a ward activity, an online video that explains the gospel of Jesus Christ. “Come and see” can be an invitation to read the Book of Mormon or visit a new temple during its open house prior to its dedication. Sometimes the invitation is something we extend inward—an invitation to ourselves, giving us awareness and vision of opportunities surrounding us to act upon.</p>
<p data-aid="149807852" id="p34" style="--height:144.01px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="87"></span>In our digital age, members often share messages through social media. There are hundreds, if not thousands, of uplifting things you might find worthy of sharing. This content offers invitations to “come and see,” “come and serve,” and “come and belong.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807857" id="p35" style="--height:86.4063px;">As we invite others to learn more about the gospel of Jesus Christ, we take part in the Savior’s call to engage in the work of His commission.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807862" id="title5" style="--height:33.6111px;">Conclusion</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807867" id="p36" style="--height:144.01px;">My beloved brothers and sisters, we have spoken today of three simple things—easy things—that anyone can do. Things <em>you</em> can do! Perhaps you are already doing them—even without fully realizing that you are!</p>
<p data-aid="149807871" id="p37" style="--height:115.208px;">I invite you to consider ways you can love, share, and invite. As you do so, you will feel a measure of joy knowing that you are heeding the words of our beloved Savior.</p>
<p data-aid="149807875" id="p38" style="--height:144.01px;">What I am urging you to do is not a new program. You have heard these principles before. This is not the “next big thing” the Church is asking you to do. These three things are merely an extension of who we already are as disciples of Jesus Christ.</p>
<p data-aid="149807879" id="p39" style="--height:28.8021px;">No name badge or letter is required.</p>
<p data-aid="149807883" id="p40" style="--height:28.8021px;">No formal calling is needed.</p>
<p data-aid="149807887" id="p41" style="--height:86.4063px;">As these three things become a natural part of who we are and how we live, they will become an automatic, unforced expression of genuine love.</p>
<p data-aid="149807891" id="p42" style="--height:115.208px;">Like those disciples of Christ who gathered together to learn from Him in Galilee 2,000 years ago, we too can embrace the Savior’s charge and go into all the world preaching the gospel.</p>
<p data-aid="149807900" id="p43" style="--height:86.4063px;">As we love, share, and invite, we take part in that great and glorious work that prepares the earth for the return of its Messiah.</p>
<p data-aid="149807908" id="p44" style="--height:86.4063px;">That we may heed the Savior’s call and strive to engage in His great commission is my prayer in the name of Jesus the Christ, amen.</p>
</section>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149808372" id="p1" style="--height:230.417px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="88"></span>“For God so loved the world, that he gave his only begotten Son, that whosoever believeth in him should not perish, but have everlasting life” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/john/3.16?lang=eng#p16">John 3:16</a>). The first time I noticed this verse, I was not at church or in family home evening. I was watching a sporting event on television. No matter what station I watched, and no matter what game it was, at least one person held a sign that read “<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/john/3.16?lang=eng#p16">John 3:16</a>.”</p>
<p data-aid="149808382" id="p2" style="--height:86.4063px;">I have come to equally love <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/john/3.17?lang=eng#p17">verse 17</a>: “For God sent not his Son into the world to condemn the world; but that the world through him might be saved.”</p>
<p data-aid="149808392" id="p3" style="--height:115.208px;">God sent Jesus Christ, His only Son in the flesh, to lay down His life for every one of us. This He did because He loves us and designed a plan for each of us to return home to Him.</p>
<p data-aid="149808402" id="p4" style="--height:144.01px;">But this is not a blanket, catchall, hit-or-miss sort of plan. It is personal, set forth by a loving Heavenly Father, who knows our hearts, our names, and what He needs us to do. Why do we believe that? Because we are taught it in the holy scriptures.</p>
<p data-aid="149808412" id="p5" style="--height:259.219px;">Moses repeatedly heard Heavenly Father speak the words “Moses, my son” (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/pgp/moses/1.6?lang=eng#p6">Moses 1:6</a>; see also <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/pgp/moses/1.7,40?lang=eng#p7">verses 7, 40</a>). Abraham learned he was a child of God, chosen for his mission even before he was born (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/pgp/abr/3.12,23?lang=eng#p12">Abraham 3:12, 23</a>). By the hand of God, Esther was placed in a position of influence to save her people (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/ot/esth/4?lang=eng">Esther 4</a>). And God trusted a young woman, a servant, to testify of a living prophet so Naaman could be healed (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/ot/2-kgs/5.1-15?lang=eng#p1">2&nbsp;Kings 5:1–15</a>).</p>
<p data-aid="149808422" id="p6" style="--height:259.219px;">I especially love that good man, short in stature, who climbed a tree to see Jesus. The Savior knew he was there, stopped, looked up into the branches, and spoke these words: “Zacchaeus, … come down” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/luke/19.5?lang=eng#p5">Luke 19:5</a>). And we cannot forget the 14-year-old who went into a grove of trees and learned how personal the plan really is: “[Joseph,] <em>this is My Beloved Son. Hear Him!</em>” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/pgp/js-h/1.17?lang=eng#p17">Joseph Smith—History 1:17</a>).</p>
<p data-aid="149808433" id="p7" style="--height:115.208px;">Brothers and sisters, we are the focus of Heavenly Father’s plan and the reason for our Savior’s mission. Each of us, individually, is Their work and Their glory.</p>
<p data-aid="149808444" id="p8" style="--height:144.01px;">To me, no book of scripture illustrates this more clearly than has my study of the Old Testament. Chapter after chapter we discover examples of how Heavenly Father and Jehovah are intimately involved in our lives.</p>
<p data-aid="149808455" id="p9" style="--height:403.229px;">We have recently been studying about Joseph, the beloved son of Jacob. From his youth, Joseph was highly favored of the Lord, yet he experienced great trials at the hands of his brothers. Two weeks ago, many of us were touched by how Joseph forgave his brothers. In <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> we read: “In many ways, Joseph’s life parallels that of Jesus Christ. Even though our sins caused Him great suffering, the Savior offers forgiveness, delivering all of us from a fate far worse than famine. Whether we need to receive forgiveness or extend it—at some point we all need to do both—Joseph’s example points us to the Savior, the true source of healing and reconciliation.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/44ringwood?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808467" id="p10" style="--height:172.813px;">A lesson I love in that account comes from Joseph’s brother Judah, who played a part in God’s personal plan for Joseph. When Joseph was betrayed by his brothers, Judah convinced them not to take Joseph’s life but to sell him into slavery (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/ot/gen/37.26-27?lang=eng#p26">Genesis 37:26–27</a>).</p>
<p data-aid="149808479" id="p11" style="--height:115.208px;">Many years later, Judah and his brothers needed to take their youngest brother, Benjamin, to Egypt. Initially their father resisted. But Judah made a promise to Jacob—he <span class="page-break" data-page="89"></span>would bring Benjamin home.</p>
<p data-aid="149808491" id="p12" style="--height:230.417px;">In Egypt, Judah’s promise was put to the test. Young Benjamin was wrongly accused of a crime. Judah, true to his promise, offered to be jailed in Benjamin’s place. “For,” he said, “how shall I go up to my father, and the lad be not with me?” (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/ot/gen/44.33-34?lang=eng#p33">Genesis 44:33–34</a>). Judah was determined to keep his promise and return Benjamin safely. Do you ever feel about others the way Judah felt toward Benjamin?</p>
<p data-aid="149808503" id="p13" style="--height:115.208px;">Isn’t this how parents feel about their children? How missionaries feel about people they serve? How Primary and youth leaders feel about those they teach and love?</p>
<p data-aid="149808515" id="p14" style="--height:115.208px;">No matter who you are or your current circumstances, someone feels exactly this way about you. Someone wants to return to Heavenly Father with you.</p>
<p data-aid="149808527" id="p15" style="--height:115.208px;">I am grateful for those who never give up on us, who continue to pour out their souls in prayer for us, and who continue to teach and help us qualify to return home to our Father in Heaven.</p>
<p data-aid="149808537" id="p16" style="--height:172.813px;">Recently a dear friend spent 233 days in the hospital with COVID-19. During that time, he was visited by his deceased father, who asked that a message be delivered to his grandchildren. Even from beyond the veil, this good grandfather desired to help his grandchildren return to their heavenly home.</p>
<p data-aid="149808549" id="p17" style="--height:345.625px;">Increasingly, disciples of Christ are remembering the “Benjamins” in their lives. Across the world they have heard the clarion call of God’s living prophet, President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson. Young men and young women are engaged in the Lord’s youth battalion. Individuals and families are reaching out in a spirit of ministering—loving, sharing, and inviting friends and neighbors to come unto Christ. Youth and adults are remembering and striving to keep their covenants—filling God’s temples, finding names of deceased family members, and receiving ordinances on their behalf.</p>
<p data-aid="149808561" id="p18" style="--height:259.219px;">Why does Heavenly Father’s personalized plan for us include helping others return to Him? Because this is how we become like Jesus Christ. Ultimately, the account of Judah and Benjamin teaches us about the Savior’s sacrifice for us. Through His Atonement, He gave His life to bring us home. Judah’s words express the Savior’s love: “How shall I go up to my father, and [you] be not with me?” As gatherers of Israel, those can be our words as well.</p>
<p data-aid="149808573" id="p19" style="--height:172.813px;">The Old Testament is packed with miracles and tender mercies that are the hallmark of Heavenly Father’s plan. In <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/ot/2-kgs/4?lang=eng">2&nbsp;Kings 4</a>, the phrase “it fell on a day” is used three times to emphasize to me that important events happen according to God’s timing and no detail is too small for Him.</p>
<p data-aid="149808585" id="p20" style="--height:201.615px;">My new friend Paul testifies of this truth. Paul grew up in a home that was sometimes abusive and always intolerant of religion. While attending school on a military base in Germany, he noticed two sisters who seemed to have a spiritual light. Asking why they were different brought the answer that they belonged to The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints.</p>
<p data-aid="149808597" id="p21" style="--height:144.01px;">Soon Paul began meeting with missionaries and was invited to church. The next Sunday, as he got off the bus, he noticed two men dressed in <span class="page-break" data-page="90"></span>white shirts and ties. He asked them if they were elders of the Church. They answered yes, so Paul followed them.</p>
<p data-aid="149808609" id="p22" style="--height:115.208px;">During the service, a preacher pointed to people in the congregation and invited them to testify. At the end of each testimony, a drummer gave a drum salute and the congregation called out, “Amen.”</p>
<p data-aid="149808620" id="p23" style="--height:172.813px;">When the preacher pointed to Paul, he stood up and said, “I know Joseph Smith was a prophet and the Book of Mormon is true.” There was no drum salute or amens. Paul eventually realized he had gone to the wrong church. Soon, Paul found his way to the right place and was baptized.</p>
<p data-aid="149808632" id="p24" style="--height:259.219px;">On the day of Paul’s baptism, a member he didn’t know told him, “You saved my life.” A few weeks earlier, this man had decided to look for another church and attended a service with drums and amens. When the man heard Paul bear his testimony of Joseph Smith and the Book of Mormon, he realized that God knew him, recognized his struggles, and had a plan for him. For both Paul and the man, “it fell on a day,” indeed!</p>
<p data-aid="149808644" id="p25" style="--height:144.01px;">We too know that Heavenly Father has a personal plan of happiness for each of us. Because God sent His Beloved Son for us, the miracles we need will “[fall] on [the very] day” necessary for His plan to be fulfilled.</p>
<p data-aid="149808656" id="p26" style="--height:259.219px;">I testify that this year we can learn more about God’s plan for us in the Old Testament. That sacred volume teaches the role of prophets in uncertain times and of God’s hand in a world that was confused and often contentious. It is also about humble believers who faithfully looked forward to the coming of our Savior, just as we look forward to and prepare for His <em>Second</em> Coming—His long-prophesied, glorious return.</p>
<p data-aid="149808668" id="p27" style="--height:201.615px;">Until that day, we may not see with our natural eyes the design of God for all aspects of our lives (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/dc-testament/dc/58.3?lang=eng#p3">Doctrine and Covenants 58:3</a>). But we can remember Nephi’s response when faced with something he didn’t understand: while he didn’t know the meaning of all things, he knew that God loves His children (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/bofm/1-ne/11.17?lang=eng#p17">1&nbsp;Nephi 11:17</a>).</p>
<p data-aid="149808680" id="p28" style="--height:172.813px;">This is my witness on this beautiful Sabbath morning. May we write it on our hearts and allow it to fill our souls with peace, hope, and eternal joy: God so loved us that He sent His Only Begotten Son—not to condemn us, but to save us. In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149808389" id="p1" style="--height:86.4063px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="91"></span>Brothers and sisters, at this glorious Easter season we are so blessed to meet and receive counsel and direction from God’s servants.</p>
<p data-aid="149808400" id="p2" style="--height:201.615px;">Sacred guidance and teachings from our Heavenly Father help us navigate life in these perilous times. As was prophesied, “fires, and tempests,” “wars, rumors of wars, and earthquakes in divers places,” “and all manner of abominations,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> “plague,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> “famines, and pestilences”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> are ravaging families, communities, and even nations.</p>
<p data-aid="149808410" id="p3" style="--height:230.417px;">There is another scourge sweeping the globe: attacks on your and my religious freedom. This growing sentiment seeks to remove religion and faith in God from the public square, schools, community standards, and civic discourse. Opponents of religious freedom seek to impose restrictions on expressions of heartfelt convictions. They even criticize and ridicule faith traditions.</p>
<p data-aid="149808420" id="p4" style="--height:86.4063px;">Such an attitude marginalizes people, devaluing personal principles, fairness, respect, spirituality, and peace of conscience.</p>
<p data-aid="149808431" id="p5" style="--height:28.8021px;">What is religious freedom?</p>
<p data-aid="149808442" id="p6" style="--height:201.615px;">It is freedom of worship in all its configurations: freedom of assembly, freedom of speech, freedom to act on personal beliefs, and freedom for others to do the same. Religious freedom allows each of us to decide for ourselves what we believe, how we live and act according to our faith, and what God expects of us.</p>
<p data-aid="149808453" id="p7" style="--height:144.01px;">Efforts to curtail such religious liberty are not new. Throughout history, people of faith have suffered mightily at the hands of others. Members of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints are no different.</p>
<p data-aid="149808465" id="p8" style="--height:144.01px;">From our beginnings, many seeking God were drawn to this Church because of its teachings of divine doctrine, including faith in Jesus Christ and His Atonement, repentance, the plan of happiness, and the Second Coming of our Lord.</p>
<p data-aid="149808477" id="p9" style="--height:86.4063px;">Opposition, persecution, and violence plagued our first latter-day prophet, Joseph Smith, and his followers.</p>
<p data-aid="149808489" id="p10" style="--height:201.615px;">Amidst the turmoil in 1842, Joseph published 13 fundamental tenets of the growing Church, including this one: “We claim the privilege of worshiping Almighty God according to the dictates of our own conscience, and allow all men the same privilege, let them worship how, where, or what they may.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808501" id="p11" style="--height:57.6042px;">His statement is inclusive, liberating, and respectful. That is the essence of religious freedom.</p>
<p data-aid="149808514" id="p12" style="--height:28.8021px;">The Prophet Joseph Smith also stated: </p>
<p data-aid="149808525" id="p13" style="--height:230.417px;">“I am bold to declare before Heaven that I am just as ready to die in defending the rights of a Presbyterian, a Baptist, or a good man of any other denomination; for the same principle which would trample upon the rights of the … Saints <span class="page-break" data-page="92"></span>would trample upon the rights of the Roman Catholics, or of any other denomination who may be unpopular and too weak to defend themselves. </p>
<p data-aid="149808538" id="p14" style="--height:86.4063px;">“It is a love of liberty [that] inspires my soul—civil and religious liberty to the whole of the human race.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808550" id="p15" style="--height:374.427px;">Still, early Church members were attacked and driven thousands of miles, from New York to Ohio to Missouri, where the governor issued an order that members of the Church “must be treated as enemies and must be exterminated or driven from the state.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> They fled to Illinois, but the torment continued. A mob murdered the Prophet Joseph, thinking that killing him would destroy the Church and scatter the believers. But the faithful held firm. Joseph’s successor, Brigham Young, led thousands in a forced exodus 1,300 miles (2,100&nbsp;km) west to what is now the state of Utah.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a> My own ancestors were amongst those early pioneer settlers.</p>
<p data-aid="149808562" id="p16" style="--height:115.208px;">From those days of intense persecution, the Lord’s Church has grown steadily to nearly 17 million members, with well over half living outside the United States.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808574" id="p17" style="--height:172.813px;">In April 2020 our Church celebrated the 200th anniversary of the Restoration of the gospel with a proclamation to the world, prepared by our First Presidency and Quorum of the Twelve Apostles. It begins, “We solemnly proclaim that God loves His children in every nation of the world.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808586" id="p18" style="--height:57.6042px;">Our beloved prophet, Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson, has further expressed:</p>
<p data-aid="149808598" id="p45" style="--height:57.6042px;">“We believe in freedom, kindness, and fairness for all of God’s children.</p>
<p data-aid="149808610" id="p46" style="--height:115.208px;">“We are all brothers and sisters, each one a child of a loving Father in Heaven. His Son, the Lord Jesus Christ, invites all to come to Him, ‘black and white, bond and free, male and female’ (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/bofm/2-ne/26.33?lang=eng#p33">2&nbsp;Nephi 26:33</a>).”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808622" id="p19" style="--height:57.6042px;">Consider with me four ways that society and individuals benefit from religious freedom.</p>
<p data-aid="149808634" id="p20" style="--height:86.4063px;"><strong>First.</strong> Religious freedom honors the first and second great commandments, placing God at the center of our lives. We read in Matthew:</p>
<p data-aid="149808646" id="p21" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Thou shalt love the Lord thy God with all thy heart, and with all thy soul, and with all thy mind.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808658" id="p22" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And the second is like unto it, Thou shalt love thy neighbour as thyself.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808670" id="p23" style="--height:115.208px;">Whether in a chapel, synagogue, mosque, or tin-roofed hut, Christ’s disciples and all like-minded believers can express devotion to God by worship of Him and willingness to serve His children.</p>
<p data-aid="149808682" id="p24" style="--height:172.813px;">Jesus Christ is the perfect example of such love and service. During His ministry, He cared for the poor,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> healed the sick<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> and the blind.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a> He fed the hungry,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> opened His arms to little children,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a> and forgave those who wronged Him, even crucified Him.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808694" id="p25" style="--height:57.6042px;">The scriptures describe that Jesus “went about doing good.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a> So must we.</p>
<p data-aid="149808705" id="p26" style="--height:57.6042px;"><strong>Second.</strong> Religious freedom fosters expressions of belief, hope, and peace.</p>
<p data-aid="149808715" id="p27" style="--height:172.813px;">As a church, we join with other religions protecting people of all faiths and persuasions and their right to speak their convictions. This does not mean we accept their beliefs, nor they ours, but we have more in common than we have with those who desire to silence us.</p>
<p data-aid="149808725" id="p28" style="--height:230.417px;">I recently represented the Church at the annual G20 Interfaith Forum in Italy. I was encouraged, even buoyed up, when I met with government and faith leaders from around the world. I realized wounds and differences can be resolved and even healed when we honor God, the Father of us all, and Jesus Christ, His Son. The Great Healer of all is our Lord and Savior, Jesus Christ.</p>
<p data-aid="149808735" id="p29" style="--height:288.021px;">I had an interesting moment as I closed my talk. The previous seven speakers had not closed in any manner of a faith tradition or in the name of God. As I spoke, I thought, “Do I just say thank you and sit down, or do I close ‘in the name of Jesus Christ’?” I remembered who I was, and I knew the Lord would have me say His name <span class="page-break" data-page="93"></span>to conclude my message. So I did. Looking back, it was my opportunity to express my belief; and I had the freedom of religion to bear my witness of His holy name.</p>
<p data-aid="149808744" id="p30" style="--height:28.8021px;"><strong>Third.</strong> Religion inspires people to help others.</p>
<p data-aid="149808753" id="p31" style="--height:432.031px;">When religion is given the space and freedom to flourish, believers perform simple and sometimes heroic acts of service. The ancient Jewish phrase “tikkun olam,” meaning “to repair or heal the world,” is being reflected today in the efforts of so many. We have partnered with Catholic Charities, known as Caritas Internationalis; Islamic Relief; and any number of Jewish, Hindu, Buddhist, Sikh, and Christian organizations like the Salvation Army and the National Christian Foundation. Together we serve millions in need, most recently by aiding refugees of war with tents, sleeping bags, and food supplies,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a> and providing vaccinations, including polio<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a> and COVID.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a> The list of what is being done is long, but so are the needs.</p>
<p data-aid="149808762" id="p32" style="--height:115.208px;">No question, people of faith, working together, can make significant interventions. At the same time, one-on-one service is often unheralded but quietly changes lives.</p>
<p data-aid="149808771" id="p33" style="--height:230.417px;">I think of the example in Luke when Jesus Christ reached out to the widow of Nain. Jesus, accompanied by a group of followers, came upon the burial procession of the widow’s only son. Without him, she was facing emotional, spiritual, and even financial ruin. Jesus, seeing her tearstained face, said, “Weep not.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a> Then He touched the bier carrying the body, and the procession halted. </p>
<p data-aid="149808780" id="p34" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Young man,” He commanded, “I say unto thee, Arise. </p>
<p data-aid="149808789" id="p35" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And he that was dead sat up, and began to speak. And [Jesus] delivered him to his mother.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note24" data-scroll-id="note24"><sup class="marker">24</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808798" id="p36" style="--height:115.208px;">Raising the dead is a miracle, but every act of kindness and concern for someone struggling is the covenant way each of us can also “[go] about doing good,” knowing “God [is] with [us].”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note25" data-scroll-id="note25"><sup class="marker">25</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808806" id="p38" style="--height:57.6042px;">And <strong>fourth.</strong> Freedom of religion acts as a unifying and rallying force for shaping values and morality.</p>
<p data-aid="149808813" id="p39" style="--height:86.4063px;">In the New Testament we read of many turning away from Jesus Christ, murmuring of His doctrine, “This is an hard saying; who can hear it?”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note26" data-scroll-id="note26"><sup class="marker">26</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808820" id="p40" style="--height:374.427px;">That cry is still being heard today from those who seek to expel religion from discourse and influence. If religion is not there to help with shaping character and mediating hard times, who will be? Who will teach honesty, gratitude, forgiveness, and patience? Who will exhibit charity, compassion, and kindness for the forgotten and the downtrodden? Who will embrace those who are different yet deserving, as are all of God’s children? Who will open their arms to those in need and seek no recompense? Who will reverence peace and obedience to laws greater than the trends of the day? Who will respond to the Savior’s plea “Go, and do thou likewise”?<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note27" data-scroll-id="note27"><sup class="marker">27</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808827" id="p41" style="--height:28.8021px;">We will! Yes, brothers and sisters, we will.</p>
<p data-aid="149808834" id="p42" style="--height:86.4063px;">I invite you to champion the cause of religious freedom. It is an expression of the God-given principle of agency.</p>
<p data-aid="149808841" id="p43" style="--height:144.01px;">Religious freedom brings balance to competing philosophies. The good of religion, its reach, and the daily acts of love which religion inspires only multiply when we protect the freedom to express and act on core beliefs.</p>
<p data-aid="149808848" id="p44" style="--height:259.219px;">I witness that Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson is God’s living prophet. I testify that Jesus Christ leads and guides this Church. He atoned for our sins, was crucified on a cross, and was resurrected on the third day.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/45rasband?lang=eng#note28" data-scroll-id="note28"><sup class="marker">28</sup></a> Because of Him, we can live again for all eternity; and those who so desire can be with our Father in Heaven. This truth I proclaim to all the world. I am grateful <span class="page-break" data-page="94"></span>for the freedom to do so. In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149807615" id="p1" style="--height:230.417px;">I will speak about self-reliance and how it can be taught to children and to youth. Self-reliance may be perceived as being subject matter for adults. I’ve come to know that adults can best be on the path toward self-reliance when they have been taught the gospel of Jesus Christ and have practiced its doctrine and principles since childhood and as youth in the home.</p>
<p data-aid="149807624" id="p2" style="--height:172.813px;">The best illustration is a great real-life example. Wilfried Vanie, his seven siblings, and his mother joined the Church in Abidjan, Ivory Coast, when he was six years old. He was baptized at eight. His father, the main provider in the family, died when Wilfried was eleven.</p>
<p data-aid="149807633" id="p21" style="--height:288.021px;">Though saddened by the family situation, Wilfried decided to continue in school, with his mother’s encouragement and with Church support. He graduated from secondary school and served a full-time mission in the Ghana Cape Coast Mission, where he learned English. After his mission, he went on to the university and obtained a diploma in accounting and finance. Though it was hard to obtain employment in this field, he found work in the tourism and hospitality industry.</p>
<p data-aid="149807642" id="p22" style="--height:345.625px;">He started as a waiter in a five-star hotel, but his passion to improve pushed him to learn more until he became a bilingual receptionist there. When a new hotel opened, he was hired as the night auditor. Later, he enrolled in BYU–Pathway Worldwide and is currently studying a course to obtain a certificate in hospitality and tourism management. His desire is <span class="page-break" data-page="95"></span>to one day become the manager of a high-end hotel. Wilfried can provide for his eternal companion and two children, as well as help his mother and his siblings. He currently serves in the Church as a member of the stake high council.</p>
<p data-aid="149807650" id="p3" style="--height:316.823px;">Self-reliance is defined as “the ability, commitment, and effort to provide the spiritual and temporal necessities of life for self and family.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/46martinez?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> Striving to be self-reliant is part of our work along the covenant path that leads us back to Heavenly Father and to His Son, Jesus Christ. It will strengthen our faith in Jesus Christ and joyfully bind us to Him through the covenants and ordinances of salvation and exaltation. Self-reliance is a doctrine of the gospel of Jesus Christ, not a program. It is a process that lasts a lifetime, not an event.</p>
<p data-aid="149807658" id="p4" style="--height:201.615px;">We become self-reliant throughout our lives by growing in spiritual strength, improving our physical and emotional health, pursuing our education and employment, and being temporally prepared.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/46martinez?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> Is this task ever finished during our lives? <em>No</em>, it is a lifelong process of learning, growth, and work. It never ends; it is a continuous, daily process.</p>
<p data-aid="149807667" id="p5" style="--height:230.417px;">How can we teach the doctrine and principles of self-reliance to our children and youth? One important way is to regularly apply the principles of the Children and Youth program. Parents and children learn the gospel of Jesus Christ, participate in service and activities, and work together in four areas of personal development that are unique for each child. It is no longer the same prescribed program for all.</p>
<p data-aid="149807675" id="p23" style="--height:316.823px;">The <cite>Children’s Guidebook</cite> says: “When Jesus was your age, He learned and grew. You are learning and growing too. The scriptures say: ‘Jesus increased in wisdom and stature, and in favour with God and man’ (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/luke/2.52?lang=eng#p52">Luke 2:52</a>).”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/46martinez?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> This scripture refers to growth and learning in the spiritual aspect, favor with God; the social aspect, favor with man; the physical aspect, stature; and the intellectual aspect, wisdom. These developmental areas apply to all of us, no matter our age. When do we teach them? In <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/ot/deut/6.6-7?lang=eng#p6">Deuteronomy 6:6–7</a> we read:</p>
<p data-aid="149807683" id="p6" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And these words, which I command thee this day, shall be in thine heart:</p>
<p data-aid="149807691" id="p7" style="--height:115.208px;">“And thou shalt teach them diligently unto thy children, and shalt talk of them when thou sittest in thine house, and when thou walkest by the way, and when thou liest down, and when thou risest up.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807699" id="p8" style="--height:115.208px;">We teach these things to children by our good example, by working and serving with them, studying the scriptures, and following the teachings of Jesus Christ as taught by prophets.</p>
<p data-aid="149807707" id="p9" style="--height:144.01px;">I’ve mentioned that in the Children and Youth program, children choose different goals in each one of the four areas of development. It is important that they create their own goals in each area. Parents and leaders can teach, counsel, and support.</p>
<p data-aid="149807715" id="p24" style="--height:374.427px;">For example, our granddaughter Miranda is very motivated to grow spiritually by participating in daily early-morning seminary classes. She became interested by hearing positive comments from other seminary students in her ward. Her mother does not have to wake her up for class. On her own, she is up and connected by videoconference at the appointed time of 6:20 in the morning because she has developed good habits that help her to do so. My own parents told me recently that Miranda now talks more when she visits them, as she has grown in self-confidence. These are lessons for life and growth with noticeable outcomes.</p>
<p data-aid="149807722" id="p10" style="--height:432.031px;">Parents, grandparents, leaders, and friends assist in the growth and development of the children. Fully engaged ministering brothers and sisters, together with priesthood and organization leaders of the ward, provide support. “<a class="cross-ref" href="/study/scriptures/the-family-a-proclamation-to-the-world/the-family-a-proclamation-to-the-world?lang=eng">The Family: A Proclamation to the World</a>” says: “By divine design, fathers are to preside over their families in love and righteousness and are responsible to provide the necessities of life and protection for their families. Mothers <span class="page-break" data-page="96"></span>are primarily responsible for the nurture of their children. In these sacred responsibilities, fathers and mothers are obligated to help one another as equal partners. … Extended families should lend support when needed.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/46martinez?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a> That last line refers to grandparents, among others.</p>
<p data-aid="149807729" id="p11" style="--height:403.229px;">As we serve in West Africa, my wife, Nuria, has done a remarkable job ministering to and remaining connected with our family and grandchildren across the ocean. She does this by using technology. She reads books to the younger grandchildren. She teaches the older granddaughters topics like the story of our family, science, the history of Puerto Rico, the Articles of Faith, and the gospel of Jesus Christ. Distances nowadays do not limit connecting, belonging, and ministering to and teaching the rising generation of our families. I also join in with Nuria when I can to teach our precious grandchildren, to love them, and to spoil them and make them laugh.</p>
<p data-aid="149807736" id="p12" style="--height:288.021px;">You should notice the inspired similarities between the Children and Youth program and building self-reliance. The four areas of development in each are very similar. Spiritual strength in self-reliance relates to the spiritual in Children and Youth. Physical and emotional health in self-reliance connect with the physical and social in Children and Youth. Education, employment, and temporal preparedness in self-reliance are akin to the intellectual in the Children and Youth program.</p>
<p data-aid="149807743" id="p13" style="--height:115.208px;">In closing, let us follow our Savior, Jesus Christ, and His gospel by becoming self-reliant throughout our lives and teaching this to our children and youth. We can do this best by</p>
<ol class="decimal" start="1">
<li data-marker="1.">
<p data-aid="149807750" id="p14" style="--height:28.8021px;">being good examples of service to others,</p>
</li>
<li data-marker="2.">
<p data-aid="149807757" id="p15" style="--height:57.6042px;">living and teaching the doctrine and principles of self-reliance, and</p>
</li>
<li data-marker="3.">
<p data-aid="149807764" id="p16" style="--height:57.6042px;">obeying the commandment to build self-reliance as part of the gospel of Jesus Christ.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p data-aid="149807771" id="p17" style="--height:28.8021px;"><a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/dc-testament/dc/104.15-16?lang=eng#p15">Doctrine and Covenants 104:15–16</a> says:</p>
<p data-aid="149807778" id="p18" style="--height:57.6042px;">“It is my purpose to provide for my saints, for all things are mine.</p>
<p data-aid="149807785" id="p19" style="--height:115.208px;">“But it must needs be done in mine own way; and behold this is the way that I, the Lord, have decreed to provide for my saints, that the poor shall be exalted, in that the rich are made low.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807792" id="p20" style="--height:144.01px;">This is the Church of Jesus Christ. His gospel blesses families here on earth and throughout the eternities. It guides us in our lives as we strive to become eternal families. I know this is true. In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149808430" id="p1" style="--height:144.01px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="97"></span>My dear brothers and sisters, I love you. I cherish this opportunity to speak with you today. I pray daily that you will be protected from the fierce attacks of the adversary and have the strength to push forward through whatever challenges you face.</p>
<p data-aid="149808441" id="p2" style="--height:345.625px;">Some trials are deeply private burdens no one else can see. Others are played out on the world stage. The armed conflict in eastern Europe is one of these. I have been to Ukraine and Russia many times. I love those lands, the people, and their languages. I weep and pray for all who are affected by this conflict. As a church we’re doing all we can to help those who are suffering and struggling to survive. We invite everyone to continue to fast and pray for all the people being hurt by this calamity. Any war is a horrifying violation of everything the Lord Jesus Christ stands for and teaches.</p>
<p data-aid="149808452" id="p39" style="--height:316.823px;">None of us can control nations or the actions of others or even members of our own families. But we can control ourselves. My call today, dear brothers and sisters, is to end conflicts that are raging in <em>your</em> heart, <em>your</em> home, and <em>your</em> life. Bury any and all inclinations to hurt others—whether those inclinations be a temper, a sharp tongue, or a resentment for someone who has hurt you. The Savior commanded us to turn the other cheek,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> to love our enemies, and to pray for those who despitefully use us.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808464" id="p4" style="--height:144.01px;">It can be painfully difficult to let go of anger that feels so justified. It can seem impossible to forgive those whose destructive actions have hurt the innocent. And yet, the Savior admonished us to “forgive all men.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808475" id="p6" style="--height:259.219px;">We are followers of the Prince of Peace. Now more than ever, we need the peace only He can bring. How can we expect peace to exist in the world when we are not <em>individually</em> seeking peace and harmony? Brothers and sisters, I know what I’m suggesting is not easy. But followers of Jesus Christ should set the example for all the world to follow. I plead with you to do all you can to end <em>personal</em> conflicts that are currently raging in your hearts and in your lives.</p>
<p data-aid="149808487" id="p7" style="--height:86.4063px;">May I underscore this call to action by discussing a concept I was reminded of recently while watching a basketball game.</p>
<p data-aid="149808499" id="p8" style="--height:259.219px;">In that game, the first half was a seesaw battle, back and forth. Then, during the last five seconds of the first half, a guard on one team made a beautiful three-point shot. With only one second left, his teammate stole the inbound pass and made another basket at the buzzer! So that team went into the locker room four points ahead with a palpable surge of momentum. They were able to carry that momentum into the second half and win the game.</p>
<p data-aid="149808511" id="p9" style="--height:115.208px;"><em>Momentum</em> is a powerful concept. We all have experienced it in one form or another—for example, in a vehicle that picks up speed or with a disagreement that suddenly turns into an argument.</p>
<p data-aid="149808523" id="p10" style="--height:172.813px;">So I ask, what can ignite <em>spiritual momentum</em>? We have seen examples of both positive and negative momentum. We know followers of Jesus Christ who became converted and grew in their faith. But we also know of once-committed believers who fell away. Momentum can swing either way.</p>
<p data-aid="149808535" id="p11" style="--height:288.021px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="98"></span>We have never needed <em>positive</em> spiritual momentum more than we do now, to counteract the speed with which evil and the darker signs of the times are intensifying. Positive spiritual momentum will keep us moving forward amid the fear and uncertainty created by pandemics, tsunamis, volcanic eruptions, and armed hostilities. Spiritual momentum can help us withstand the relentless, wicked attacks of the adversary and thwart his efforts to erode our personal spiritual foundation.</p>
<p data-aid="149808547" id="p12" style="--height:86.4063px;">Many actions can ignite positive spiritual momentum. Obedience, love, humility, service, and gratitude<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a> are but a few.</p>
<p data-aid="149808559" id="p13" style="--height:86.4063px;">Today I would like to suggest five specific actions we can take to help us maintain positive spiritual momentum.</p>
<p data-aid="149808571" id="p14" style="--height:28.8021px;">First: <strong>Get on the covenant path and stay there.</strong></p>
<p data-aid="149808583" id="p15" style="--height:115.208px;">Not long ago, I had a vivid dream in which I met a large group of people. They asked me many questions, the most frequent of which was about the covenant path and why it is so important.</p>
<p data-aid="149808595" id="p16" style="--height:201.615px;">In my dream, I explained that we enter the covenant path by being baptized and making our first covenant with God.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a> Each time we partake of the sacrament, we promise <em>again</em> to take the name of the Savior upon us, to remember Him, and to keep His commandments.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> In return, God assures us that we may <em>always</em> have the Spirit of the Lord to be with us.</p>
<p data-aid="149808607" id="p17" style="--height:144.01px;">Later we make additional covenants in the temple, where we receive even greater promises. Ordinances and covenants give us access to godly power. The covenant path is the <em>only</em> path that leads to exaltation and eternal life.</p>
<p data-aid="149808619" id="p18" style="--height:115.208px;">In my dream, a woman then asked how someone who has broken his or her covenants can get back on that path. My answer to her question leads to my second suggestion:</p>
<p data-aid="149808631" id="p19" style="--height:30.4688px;"><strong>Discover the <em>joy</em> of daily repentance.</strong></p>
<p data-aid="149808643" id="p20" style="--height:259.219px;">How important is repentance? Alma taught that we should “preach nothing save it were repentance and faith on the Lord.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a> Repentance is required of every accountable person who desires eternal glory.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a> There are no exceptions. In a revelation to the Prophet Joseph Smith, the Lord chastised early Church leaders for not teaching the gospel to their children.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a> Repenting is the <em>key</em> to progress. Pure faith keeps us moving forward on the covenant path.</p>
<p data-aid="149808655" id="p21" style="--height:201.615px;">Please do not fear or delay repenting. Satan delights in your misery. Cut it short. Cast his influence out of your life! Start today to experience the joy of putting off the natural man.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a> The Savior loves us always but <em>especially</em> when we repent. He promised that though “the mountains shall depart, and the hills be removed … <em>my kindness</em> shall not depart from thee.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808667" id="p22" style="--height:144.01px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="99"></span>If you feel you have strayed off the covenant path too far or too long and have no way to return, that simply is not true.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a> Please contact your bishop or branch president. He is the Lord’s agent and will help you experience the joy and relief of repenting.</p>
<p data-aid="149808679" id="p23" style="--height:345.625px;">Now, a caution: Returning to the covenant path does <em>not</em> mean that life will be easy. This path is rigorous and at times will feel like a steep climb.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> This ascent, however, is designed to test and teach us, refine our natures, and help us to become saints. It is the <em>only</em> path that leads to exaltation. One prophet<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> described the “blessed and happy state of those that keep the commandments of God. For behold, they are blessed in all things, both temporal and spiritual; and if they hold out faithful to the end they are received into heaven … [and] dwell with God in a state of never-ending happiness.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808691" id="p24" style="--height:57.6042px;">Walking the covenant path, coupled with daily repentance, fuels positive spiritual momentum.</p>
<p data-aid="149808702" id="p25" style="--height:57.6042px;">My third suggestion: <strong>Learn about God and how He works.</strong></p>
<p data-aid="149808713" id="p26" style="--height:172.813px;">One of our greatest challenges today is distinguishing between the truths of God and the counterfeits of Satan. That is why the Lord warned us to “pray always, … that [we] may conquer Satan, and … <em>escape the hands of the servants of Satan</em> that do uphold his work.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808723" id="p27" style="--height:288.021px;">Moses provided an example of how to discern between God and Satan. When Satan came tempting Moses, he detected the deception because he had just had a face-to-face interaction with God. Moses quickly realized who Satan was and commanded him to depart.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a> When Satan persisted, Moses knew how to call upon God for more help. Moses received divine strength and rebuked the evil one <em>again</em>, saying, “Depart from me, Satan, for this one God only will I worship.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808733" id="p28" style="--height:86.4063px;">We should follow that example. Cast Satan’s influence out of your life! Please do not <em>follow</em> him down to his “gulf of misery and endless wo.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808742" id="p40" style="--height:230.417px;">With frightening speed, a testimony that is not nourished daily “by the good word of God”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a> can crumble. Thus, the antidote to Satan’s scheme is clear: we need daily experiences worshipping the Lord and studying His gospel. I plead with you to let God prevail in your life. Give Him a fair share of your time. As you do, notice what happens to your positive spiritual momentum.</p>
<p data-aid="149808751" id="p29" style="--height:28.8021px;">Suggestion number 4: <strong>Seek and expect miracles.</strong></p>
<p data-aid="149808760" id="p30" style="--height:259.219px;">Moroni assured us that “God has not ceased to be a God of miracles.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a> <em>Every</em> book of scripture demonstrates how willing the Lord is to intervene in the lives of those who believe in Him.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a> He parted the Red Sea for Moses, helped Nephi retrieve the brass plates, and restored His Church through the Prophet Joseph Smith. Each of these miracles took time and may not have <span class="page-break" data-page="100"></span>been exactly what those individuals originally requested from the Lord.</p>
<p data-aid="149808769" id="p31" style="--height:288.021px;">In the same way, the Lord will bless <em>you</em> with miracles <em>if</em> you believe in Him, “doubting nothing.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a> Do the spiritual work to seek miracles. Prayerfully ask God to help you exercise that kind of faith. I promise that you can experience for yourself that Jesus Christ “giveth power to the faint; and to them that have no might he increaseth strength.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note24" data-scroll-id="note24"><sup class="marker">24</sup></a> Few things will accelerate your spiritual momentum more than realizing the Lord is helping you to move a mountain in your life.</p>
<p data-aid="149808778" id="p32" style="--height:57.6042px;">Suggestion number 5: <strong>End conflict in your personal life.</strong></p>
<p data-aid="149808787" id="p33" style="--height:172.813px;">I repeat my call to end the conflicts in <em>your</em> life. Exercise the humility, courage, and strength required both to forgive and to seek forgiveness. The Savior has promised that “if [we] forgive men their trespasses, [our] heavenly Father will also forgive [us].”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/47nelson?lang=eng#note25" data-scroll-id="note25"><sup class="marker">25</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808796" id="p34" style="--height:259.219px;">Two weeks from today we celebrate Easter. Between now and then, I invite you to seek an end to a personal conflict that has weighed you down. Could there be a more fitting act of gratitude to Jesus Christ for His Atonement? If forgiveness presently seems impossible, plead for power through the atoning blood of Jesus Christ to help you. As you do so, I promise personal peace and a burst of spiritual momentum.</p>
<p data-aid="149808804" id="p35" style="--height:144.01px;">When the Savior atoned for all mankind, He opened a way that those who follow Him can have access to His healing, strengthening, and redeeming power. These spiritual privileges are available to all who seek to hear Him and follow Him.</p>
<p data-aid="149808811" id="p36" style="--height:144.01px;">My dear brothers and sisters, with all the pleadings of my heart, I urge you to get on the covenant path and stay there. Experience the joy of repenting daily. Learn about God and how He works. Seek and expect miracles. Strive to end conflict in your life.</p>
<p data-aid="149808818" id="p37" style="--height:172.813px;">As you act on these pursuits, I promise you the ability to move forward on the covenant path with increased momentum, despite whatever obstacles you face. And I promise you greater strength to resist temptation, more peace of mind, freedom from fear, and greater unity in your families.</p>
<p data-aid="149808825" id="p38" style="--height:86.4063px;">God lives! Jesus is the Christ! He lives! He loves us and will help us. Of this I testify in the sacred name of our Redeemer, Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149808482" id="p1" style="--height:345.625px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="101"></span>The gospel plan shows our Heavenly Father’s love for all His children. To understand this, we must seek to understand His plan and His commandments. He loves His children so much that He gave His Only Begotten Son, Jesus Christ, to be our Savior and Redeemer, to suffer and die for us. In the restored Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints, we have a unique understanding of our Heavenly Father’s plan. This gives us a different way of viewing the purpose of mortal life, the divine judgment that follows it, and the ultimate glorious destiny of all of God’s children.</p>
<p data-aid="149808494" id="p2" style="--height:374.427px;">I love you, my brothers and sisters. I love all of God’s children. When Jesus was asked, “Which is the great commandment in the law?” He taught that to love God and to love our neighbors are the first of God’s great commandments.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> Those commands are first because they invite us to grow spiritually by seeking to imitate God’s love for us. I wish we all had a better understanding of the loving doctrine and policies that our Heavenly Father and His Son, Jesus Christ, have established in The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints. What I say here seeks to clarify how God’s love explains that doctrine and the Church’s inspired policies.</p>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808506" id="title2" style="--height:33.6111px;">I.</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808518" id="p3" style="--height:230.417px;">A common misunderstanding of the judgment that ultimately follows mortal life is that good people go to a place called <em>heaven</em> and bad people go to an everlasting place called <em>hell</em>. This erroneous assumption of only two ultimate destinations implies that those who cannot keep all the commandments required for heaven will necessarily be forever destined for hell.</p>
<p data-aid="149808530" id="p4" style="--height:518.438px;">A loving Heavenly Father has a better plan for His children. The revealed doctrine of the restored Church of Jesus Christ teaches that <em>all the children of God</em>—with exceptions too limited to consider here—will finally wind up in a kingdom of <em>glory</em>.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> “In my Father’s house are many mansions,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> Jesus taught. From modern revelation we know that those mansions are in three different kingdoms of glory. In the Final Judgment each of us will be judged according to our deeds and the desires of our hearts.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a> Before that, we will need to suffer for our unrepented sins. The scriptures are clear on that.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a> Then our righteous Judge will grant us residence in one of those kingdoms of glory. Thus, as we know from modern revelation, all “shall be judged&nbsp;…&nbsp;, and every man shall receive according to his own works, his own dominion, in the mansions which are prepared.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808542" id="p5" style="--height:144.01px;">The Lord has chosen to reveal comparatively little about two of these kingdoms of glory. In contrast, the Lord has revealed much about the highest kingdom of glory, which the Bible describes as the “glory of the sun.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808554" id="p6" style="--height:374.427px;">In the “celestial” glory<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a> there are three degrees, or levels.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a> The highest of these is exaltation in the celestial kingdom, wherein we may become like our Father and His Son, Jesus Christ. To help us develop the godly <span class="page-break" data-page="102"></span>attributes and the change in nature necessary to realize our divine potential, the Lord has revealed doctrine and established commandments based on eternal law. This is what we teach in The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints because the purpose of the doctrine and policies of this restored Church is to prepare God’s children for salvation in the celestial glory and, more particularly, for exaltation in its highest degree.</p>
<p data-aid="149808566" id="p7" style="--height:374.427px;">The covenants made and the blessings promised to the faithful in the temples of God are the key. This explains our worldwide building of temples, about which the choir has sung so beautifully. Some are puzzled at this emphasis, not understanding that the covenants and ordinances of the temple guide us toward achieving exaltation. This can be understood only in the context of the revealed truth of <em>three</em> degrees of glory. Because of our Heavenly Father’s great love for all of His children, He has provided other kingdoms of glory—as Elder Quentin&nbsp;L. Cook explained yesterday—all of which are more wonderful than we can comprehend.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808578" id="p8" style="--height:172.813px;">The Atonement of Jesus Christ makes all of this possible. He has revealed that He “glorifies the Father, and <em>saves all the works of his hands</em>.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a> That salvation is granted in different kingdoms of glory. We know from modern revelation that “all kingdoms have a law given.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a> Significantly:</p>
<p data-aid="149808590" id="p9" style="--height:57.6042px;">“He who is not able to abide the law of a celestial kingdom cannot abide a celestial glory.</p>
<p data-aid="149808602" id="p10" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And he who cannot abide the law of a terrestrial kingdom cannot abide a terrestrial glory.</p>
<p data-aid="149808614" id="p11" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And he who cannot abide the law of a telestial kingdom cannot abide a telestial glory.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808626" id="p12" style="--height:172.813px;">In other words, the kingdom of glory we receive in the Final Judgment is determined by the laws we choose to abide by in our Heavenly Father’s loving plan. Under that plan there are multiple kingdoms so that all of His children can be assigned to a kingdom where they can “abide.”</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808638" id="title3" style="--height:33.6111px;">II.</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808650" id="p13" style="--height:115.208px;">The teachings and policies of the Lord’s restored Church apply these eternal truths in a way that can be fully understood only in the context of our Heavenly Father’s loving plan for <em>all</em> of His children.</p>
<p data-aid="149808663" id="p14" style="--height:172.813px;">Thus, we honor individual agency. Most are aware of this Church’s great efforts to promote religious freedom. These efforts are in furtherance of our Heavenly Father’s plan. We seek to help <em>all</em> of His children—not just our own members—enjoy the precious freedom to choose.</p>
<p data-aid="149808675" id="p15" style="--height:259.219px;">Similarly, we are sometimes asked why we send missionaries to so many nations, even among Christian populations. We are also asked why we give enormous humanitarian aid to persons who are not members of our Church without linking this to our missionary efforts. We do this because the Lord has taught us to esteem all of His children as our brothers and sisters, and we want to share our spiritual and temporal abundance with everyone.</p>
<p data-aid="149808687" id="p16" style="--height:259.219px;">Eternal doctrine also provides a distinctive perspective on children. Through this perspective we see the bearing and nurturing of children as part of the divine plan. It is a joyful and sacred duty of those given the power to participate in it. Therefore, we are commanded to teach and contend for principles and practices that provide the best conditions for the development and happiness of children under God’s plan.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808698" id="title4" style="--height:33.6111px;">III.</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808709" id="p17" style="--height:460.833px;">Finally, The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints is properly known as a family-centered Church. But not well understood is the reality that our family-centeredness is not limited to mortal relationships. Eternal relationships are also fundamental to our theology. The mission of the restored Church is to help all the children of <span class="page-break" data-page="103"></span>God qualify for what God desires as their ultimate destiny. By the redemption provided through the Atonement of Christ, all may attain eternal life (exaltation in the celestial kingdom), which Mother Eve declared “God giveth unto all the obedient.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> This is more than salvation. President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson has reminded us that “in God’s eternal plan, salvation is an individual matter; [but] exaltation is a family matter.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808719" id="p18" style="--height:201.615px;">Fundamental to us is God’s revelation that exaltation can be attained only through faithfulness to the covenants of an eternal marriage between a man and a woman.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> That divine doctrine is why we teach that “gender is an essential characteristic of individual premortal, mortal, and eternal identity and purpose.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808729" id="p19" style="--height:172.813px;">That is also why the Lord has required His restored Church to oppose social and legal pressures to retreat from His doctrine of marriage between a man and a woman, to oppose changes that homogenize the differences between men and women or confuse or alter gender.</p>
<p data-aid="149808738" id="p20" style="--height:432.031px;">The restored Church’s positions on these fundamentals frequently provoke opposition. We understand that. Our Heavenly Father’s plan allows for “opposition in all things,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a> and Satan’s most strenuous opposition is directed at whatever is most important to that plan. Consequently, he seeks to oppose progress toward exaltation by distorting marriage, discouraging childbearing, or confusing gender. However, we know that in the long run, the divine purpose and plan of our loving Heavenly Father will not be changed. Personal circumstances may change, and God’s plan assures that in the long run, the faithful who keep their covenants will have the opportunity to qualify for every promised blessing.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808747" id="p21" style="--height:374.427px;">A uniquely valuable teaching to help us prepare for eternal life, “the greatest of all the gifts of God,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a> is the 1995 proclamation on the family.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a> Its declarations are, of course, different from some current laws, practices, and advocacy, such as cohabitation and same-sex marriage. Those who do not fully understand the Father’s loving plan for His children may consider this family proclamation no more than a changeable statement of policy. In contrast, we affirm that the family proclamation, founded on irrevocable doctrine, defines the kind of family relationships where the most important part of our eternal development can occur.</p>
<p data-aid="149808756" id="p22" style="--height:86.4063px;">That is the context for the unique doctrine and policies of the restored Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808765" id="title5" style="--height:33.6111px;">IV.</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808774" id="p23" style="--height:460.833px;">In many relationships and circumstances in mortal life, each of us must live with differences. As followers of Christ who should love our fellow men, we should live peacefully with those who do not believe as we do. We are all children of a loving Heavenly Father. For all of us, He has destined life after death and, ultimately, a kingdom of glory. God desires all of us to strive for His highest possible blessings by keeping His highest commandments, covenants, and ordinances, all of which culminate in His holy temples being built throughout the world. We must seek to share these truths of eternity with others. But with the love we owe to all of our neighbors, we always accept their decisions. As a Book of Mormon prophet taught, we must press forward, having “a love of God and of all men.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808785" id="p25" style="--height:201.615px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="104"></span>As President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson declared in our last conference: “There has never been a time in the history of the world when knowledge of our Savior is more personally vital and relevant to <em>every human soul</em>. … The pure doctrine of Christ is powerful. It changes the life of everyone who understands it and seeks to implement it in his or her life.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/51oaks?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a></p>
</section>
<p data-aid="149808793" id="p26" style="--height:57.6042px;">May we all implement that sacred doctrine in our own lives, I pray in the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>
