<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149807701" id="p1" style="--height:460.833px;">A powerful king desired for his son to rule over one of his kingdoms. The prince had to learn and grow in wisdom to sit on the throne. One day, the king met with the prince and shared his plan. They agreed the prince would go to a different town and gain experiences. He would face challenges as well as enjoy many good things there. The king then sent him to the town, where the prince was expected to prove his faithfulness to the king and demonstrate that he was fit to receive the privileges and responsibilities the king had in store for him. The prince was given the liberty to choose to receive these privileges and responsibilities or not, depending on his desires and his faithfulness. I am sure you want to know what happened to the prince. Did he return to inherit the kingdom?</p>
<p data-aid="149807709" id="p2" style="--height:230.417px;">Dear brothers and sisters, each of us is a prince or princess. We have been sent to mortality by a loving Heavenly Father to enjoy the blessing of a body that would become immortal through the Atonement and Resurrection of Jesus Christ. We are expected to prepare to return to God’s presence by proving that we will “do all things whatsoever the <span class="page-break" data-page="105"></span>Lord [our] God shall command [us]” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/pgp/abr/3.25?lang=eng#p25">Abraham 3:25</a>).</p>
<p data-aid="149807716" id="p13" style="--height:374.427px;">To help us, the Savior came to redeem us and show the path to return to God. God’s children are invited to come to the Savior and be perfected in Him. In the scriptures, we find the invitation for us to come to the Lord repeated over 90 times, and more than half of these are personal invitations from the Lord Himself. Accepting the Savior’s invitation means partaking of His ordinances and keeping our covenants with Him. Jesus Christ is “the way, the truth, and the life” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/john/14.6?lang=eng#p6">John 14:6</a>), and He invites us “all to come unto him and partake of his goodness; and he denieth none that come unto him” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/bofm/2-ne/26.33?lang=eng#p33">2&nbsp;Nephi 26:33</a>).</p>
<p data-aid="149807724" id="p14" style="--height:230.417px;">Our gospel learning and teaching deepen our conversion to Heavenly Father and Jesus Christ and help us become more like Them. Even though not all things have been revealed concerning “the precise time and manner in which the blessings of exaltation [will be] bestowed,” we are nonetheless assured of them (M.&nbsp;Russell Ballard, “<a class="cross-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2021/04/28ballard?lang=eng&amp;para=24#p24">Hope in Christ</a>,” <cite>Liahona</cite>, May 2021, 55).</p>
<p data-aid="149807731" id="p3" style="--height:86.4063px;">Alma the high priest, teaching in the land of Zarahemla, recounted a profound invitation by Jesus Christ:</p>
<p data-aid="149807738" id="p15" style="--height:86.4063px;">“Behold, he sendeth an invitation unto all men, for the arms of mercy are extended towards them, and he saith: Repent, and I will receive you.</p>
<p data-aid="149807745" id="p16" style="--height:57.6042px;">“Yea, he saith: Come unto me and ye shall partake of the fruit of the tree of life” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/bofm/alma/5.33-34?lang=eng#p33">Alma 5:33–34</a>).</p>
<p data-aid="149807752" id="p17" style="--height:316.823px;">The Savior Himself invites us to come unto Him and take His yoke upon us that we may have rest in this tumultuous world (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/matt/11.28-29?lang=eng#p28">Matthew 11:28–29</a>). We come unto Christ by “exercising faith in [Him], repenting daily, making covenants with God as we receive the ordinances of salvation and exaltation, and enduring to the end by keeping those covenants” (<cite>General Handbook: Serving in The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</cite>, <a class="cross-ref" href="/study/manual/general-handbook/1-work-of-salvation-and-exaltation?lang=eng&amp;para=title_number3#title_number3">1.2.1</a>, ChurchofJesusChrist.org). The path to perfection is the covenant path, and Jesus Christ is the center of all ordinances and covenants.</p>
<p data-aid="149807759" id="p4" style="--height:345.625px;">King Benjamin taught that because of the covenants we make, we become sons and daughters of Christ, who has spiritually begotten us, and under His head are we made free, for “there is no other name given whereby salvation cometh” (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/bofm/mosiah/5.7-8?lang=eng#p7">Mosiah 5:7–8</a>). We are saved as we endure to the end by “following the example of the Son of the living God” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/bofm/2-ne/31.16?lang=eng#p16">2&nbsp;Nephi 31:16</a>). Nephi counseled that all is not done by merely getting into the strait and narrow path; we “must press forward with a steadfastness in Christ, having a perfect brightness of hope, and a love of God and of all men” (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/bofm/2-ne/31.19-20?lang=eng#p19">2&nbsp;Nephi 31:19–20</a>).</p>
<p data-aid="149807766" id="p18" style="--height:460.833px;">The doctrine of Christ helps us find and stay on the covenant path, and the gospel is so arranged that the Lord’s promised blessings are received through sacred ordinances and covenants. God’s prophet, President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson, admonished us in his January&nbsp;16, 2018, telecast to “keep on the covenant path. Your commitment to follow the Savior by making covenants with Him and then keeping those covenants will open the door to every spiritual blessing and privilege available to men, women, and children everywhere. … The end for which each of us strives is to be endowed with power in a house of the Lord, sealed as families, faithful to covenants made in a temple that qualify us for the greatest gift of God—that of eternal life” (“<a class="cross-ref" href="/study/liahona/2018/04/as-we-go-forward-together?lang=eng">As We Go Forward Together</a>,” <cite>Ensign</cite> or <cite>Liahona</cite>, Apr. 2018, 7).</p>
<p data-aid="149807773" id="p20" style="--height:230.417px;">God will not abandon His relationship with, or withhold His promised blessings of eternal life from, any faithful covenant keeper. And as we honor sacred covenants, we are drawn closer to the Savior. Elder David&nbsp;A. Bednar taught us yesterday that gospel covenants and ordinances operate in our lives like a compass to give us cardinal direction to come unto Christ and become more like Him.</p>
<p data-aid="149807780" id="p5" style="--height:144.01px;">Covenants mark the path back to God. The ordinances of baptism and receiving the gift of the Holy Ghost, priesthood ordination, and the sacrament lead us to the Lord’s temple to partake of His ordinances of exaltation.</p>
<p data-aid="149807787" id="p6" style="--height:57.6042px;">I would like to mention two things our Savior emphasized to help us faithfully keep covenants:</p>
<ol class="decimal" start="1">
<li data-marker="1.">
<p data-aid="149807795" id="p7" style="--height:288.021px;">The Holy Ghost can teach us, remind us of the Savior’s teachings, and abide with us forever (see <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/john/14.16,26?lang=eng#p16">John 14:16, 26</a>). He can be our constant companion to guide us on the covenant path. President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson taught that “in coming days, it will not be possible <span class="page-break" data-page="106"></span>to survive spiritually without the guiding, directing, comforting, and constant influence of the Holy Ghost” (“<a class="cross-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2018/04/revelation-for-the-church-revelation-for-our-lives?lang=eng">Revelation for the Church, Revelation for Our Lives</a>,” <cite>Ensign</cite> or <cite>Liahona</cite>, May 2018, 96).</p>
</li>
<li data-marker="2.">
<p data-aid="149807802" id="p8" style="--height:345.625px;">The Savior instituted the ordinance of the sacrament that we may always remember Him and have His Spirit to be with us. Baptism opens the gate to eternal life, and the sacrament helps us to steadfastly press forward along the covenant path. As we take the sacrament, it shall be a testimony unto the Father that we do always remember His Son. And as we always remember Him and keep His commandments, we shall have His Spirit to be with us. Added to this promise, the Lord renews the promised remission of sin as we humbly repent of our sins.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p data-aid="149807809" id="p9" style="--height:144.01px;">In staying faithful to our covenants, we should endeavor to always have the Spirit to prepare us to worthily partake of the sacrament, and likewise, we regularly partake of the sacrament to always have the Spirit with us.</p>
<p data-aid="149807816" id="p10" style="--height:172.813px;">When our daughter was five years old, she had a battery-powered model car and loved to drive it around the house. One evening, she came to me and said, “Daddy, my car no longer drives. Could we get some gas from your car to put in it so it can drive again? Perhaps it needs gas like your car to drive.”</p>
<p data-aid="149807823" id="p19" style="--height:259.219px;">I later observed that the battery power was down, so I said we would get it to drive in about an hour. With so much excitement, she said, “Yes! We will take it to the gas station.” I simply connected the battery to an electric source to charge, and after an hour she was able to drive the car, powered by the charged battery. She thereafter learned that it is important to always recharge the battery by connecting it to an electric source.</p>
<p data-aid="149807829" id="p11" style="--height:403.229px;">As our daughter learned the relationship between the battery and power to drive her toy car, so we learn about Jesus Christ, the sacrament, and the Spirit. We need the Spirit to help us navigate through mortality as we faithfully keep covenants, and we need the sacrament to energize our spiritual being. Renewing our baptismal covenant and partaking of the sacrament drive faithfulness to all other covenants. A happy ending is assured as we prayerfully study and honor the Savior’s invitation and enjoy His promised blessings. He said, “And that thou mayest more fully keep thyself unspotted from the world, thou shalt go to the house of prayer and offer up thy sacraments upon my holy day” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/dc-testament/dc/59.9?lang=eng#p9">Doctrine and Covenants 59:9</a>).</p>
<p data-aid="149807836" id="p12" style="--height:201.615px;">I testify that covenant keepers are promised “peace in this world, and eternal life in the world to come” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/dc-testament/dc/59.23?lang=eng#p23">Doctrine and Covenants 59:23</a>). I bear witness that as you regularly partake of the Savior’s emblems through the sacrament, you will have His Spirit to guide you on the covenant path and stay faithful to your covenants. In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149808524" id="p1" style="--height:288.021px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="107"></span>Moral agency is God’s precious gift to each of His children.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> We are “free to choose liberty and eternal life, through the great Mediator of all men, or to choose captivity and death, according to the captivity and power of the devil.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> God <em>won’t</em> force us to do good, and the devil <em>can’t</em> force us to do evil.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> Though some may think that mortality is a contest between God and the adversary, a word from the Savior “and Satan is silenced and banished. … It is [our] strength that is being tested—not God’s.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808536" id="p27" style="--height:288.021px;">In the end we will therefore reap what our lifelong choices have sown.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a> So what does the sum total of our thoughts, desires, words, and works say about our love for the Savior, His chosen servants, and His restored Church? Do our baptismal, priesthood, and temple covenants mean more to us than the praise of the world or the number of “likes” on social media? Is our love for the Lord and His commandments stronger than our love for anything or anyone else in this life?</p>
<p data-aid="149808548" id="p3" style="--height:345.625px;">The adversary and his followers have always sought to destroy the works of Christ and His prophets. The Savior’s commandments, if not ignored altogether, have been rationalized into meaninglessness by many in today’s world. Messengers of God who teach “inconvenient” truths are often dismissed. Even the Savior Himself was called “a man gluttonous, and a winebibber,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> accused of disturbing public sentiment and being divisive. Weak and conniving souls “took counsel how they might entangle him in his talk,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a> and His “sect” of early Christians was “every where … spoken against.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808560" id="p4" style="--height:345.625px;">The Savior and His early followers dealt with serious internal <span class="page-break" data-page="108"></span>and external opposition, and we experience the same. Today it is almost impossible to courageously live our faith without occasionally attracting a few actual and virtual fingers of scorn from the worldly. Confidently following the Savior is rewarding, but at times we may get caught in the crosshairs of those advocating an “eat, drink, and be merry”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a> philosophy, where faith in Christ, obedience, and repentance are substituted by the illusion that God will justify a little sin because He loves us so much.</p>
<p data-aid="149808572" id="p5" style="--height:403.229px;">Speaking “by [His] own voice or by the voice of [His] servants,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a> did the Savior not say about our day that “the time will come when they will not endure sound doctrine; but after their own lusts shall they heap to themselves teachers” and that many “shall turn away their ears from the truth, and shall be turned unto fables”?<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a> Did He not lament that “in vain they do worship me, teaching for doctrines the commandments of men”?<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a> Did He not warn that “of your own selves shall men arise, speaking perverse things, to draw away disciples after them”?<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> Did He not foresee that “evil [would be called] good, and good evil”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> and that “a man’s foes shall be they of his own household”?<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808584" id="p6" style="--height:259.219px;">So what about us? Should we be intimidated or afraid? Should we live our religion at periscope depth? Surely not! With faith in Christ, we need not fear the reproach of men or be afraid of their revilings.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> With the Savior at the helm and living prophets to lead and guide us, “who can be against us?”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a> Let us be confident, not apologetic, valiant, not timid, faithful, not fearful as we hold up the Lord’s light in these last days.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808596" id="p7" style="--height:115.208px;">The Savior made clear that “whosoever therefore shall confess me before men, him will I confess also before my Father. … But whosoever shall deny me before men, him will I also deny before my Father.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808608" id="p8" style="--height:144.01px;">Consequently, while some would prefer a God who comes without commandments, let us boldly testify, in the words of Elder D.&nbsp;Todd Christofferson, that “a God who makes no demands is the functional equivalent of a God who does not exist.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808621" id="p9" style="--height:115.208px;">While some would prefer to be selective in the commandments they follow, let us joyfully accept the Savior’s invitation to “live by <em>every</em> word which proceedeth forth out of the mouth of God.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808633" id="p10" style="--height:144.01px;">While many believe the Lord and His Church condone doing “whatsoever [our] heart desireth,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a> let us valiantly proclaim that it is wrong to “follow a multitude to do evil,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a> because “crowds cannot make right what God has declared to be wrong.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note24" data-scroll-id="note24"><sup class="marker">24</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808645" id="p11" style="--height:201.615px;">“O remember, remember … how strict [yet liberating] are the commandments of God.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note25" data-scroll-id="note25"><sup class="marker">25</sup></a> Teaching them clearly may at times be seen as an act of intolerance. Let us therefore respectfully demonstrate that it is not only possible but essential to love a child of God who embraces <span class="page-break" data-page="109"></span>beliefs different from our own.</p>
<p data-aid="149808657" id="p12" style="--height:115.208px;">We can accept and respect others without endorsing their beliefs or actions that do not align with the Lord’s will. There is no need to sacrifice truth on the altar of agreeableness and social desirability.</p>
<p data-aid="149808669" id="p13" style="--height:115.208px;">Zion and Babylon are incompatible. “No man can serve two masters.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note26" data-scroll-id="note26"><sup class="marker">26</sup></a> Let’s all remember the Savior’s penetrating question, “Why call ye me, Lord, Lord, and do <em>not</em> the things which I say?”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note27" data-scroll-id="note27"><sup class="marker">27</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808681" id="p14" style="--height:57.6042px;">Let us demonstrate our love for the Lord through wholehearted, voluntary obedience.</p>
<p data-aid="149808693" id="p15" style="--height:144.01px;">If you feel caught between your discipleship and the world, please remember that your loving Savior “sendeth an invitation&nbsp;…&nbsp;, for the arms of mercy are extended [to you], and he saith: Repent, and I will receive you.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note28" data-scroll-id="note28"><sup class="marker">28</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808704" id="p16" style="--height:230.417px;">President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson taught that Jesus Christ “will perform some of His mightiest works between now and when He comes again.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note29" data-scroll-id="note29"><sup class="marker">29</sup></a> But he also taught that “those who choose the Lord’s way will likely endure persecution.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note30" data-scroll-id="note30"><sup class="marker">30</sup></a> Being “counted worthy to suffer shame for his name”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note31" data-scroll-id="note31"><sup class="marker">31</sup></a> may at times be our lot as we “allow His voice to take priority over any other.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note32" data-scroll-id="note32"><sup class="marker">32</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808714" id="p17" style="--height:230.417px;">“Blessed is he,” the Savior said, “whosoever shall <em>not</em> be offended in me.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note33" data-scroll-id="note33"><sup class="marker">33</sup></a> Elsewhere we learn that “great peace have they which <em>love</em> thy law: and <em>nothing</em> shall offend them.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note34" data-scroll-id="note34"><sup class="marker">34</sup></a> Nothing! So let’s ask ourselves, “Am I enduring for a while, but when tribulation or persecution arises because of the word, by and by am I offended?<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note35" data-scroll-id="note35"><sup class="marker">35</sup></a> Am I firmly built on the rock of Jesus Christ and His servants?”</p>
<p data-aid="149808724" id="p18" style="--height:259.219px;">Moral relativists advocate that truth is merely a social construct, that there are no moral absolutes. What they are really saying is that there is no sin,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note36" data-scroll-id="note36"><sup class="marker">36</sup></a> that “whatsoever a man [does is] no crime,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note37" data-scroll-id="note37"><sup class="marker">37</sup></a> a philosophy for which the adversary is claiming proud authorship! Let us therefore beware of wolves in sheep’s clothing, who are always recruiting and “[often use] their intellectual reservations to cover their [own] behavioral lapses.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note38" data-scroll-id="note38"><sup class="marker">38</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808734" id="p19" style="--height:144.01px;">If we really want to be valiant disciples of Christ, we will find a way. Otherwise, the adversary offers enticing alternatives. But as faithful disciples, “we need not apologize for our beliefs nor back down from that which we know to be true.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note39" data-scroll-id="note39"><sup class="marker">39</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808743" id="p20" style="--height:172.813px;">In conclusion, a word about the 15&nbsp;servants of God seated behind me. While the worldly “say to the seers, See not; and to the prophets, Prophesy not,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note40" data-scroll-id="note40"><sup class="marker">40</sup></a> the faithful are “crowned with blessings from above, yea, and with commandments not a few, and with revelations in their time.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note41" data-scroll-id="note41"><sup class="marker">41</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808752" id="p21" style="--height:230.417px;">Not surprisingly, these men frequently become the lightning rods for those unhappy with the word of God as the prophets proclaim it. Those who reject the prophets don’t realize that “no prophecy of the scripture is [to be] of any private interpretation” or the result of the will of man “but [that] holy men of God [speak now] as they [are] moved by the Holy Ghost.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note42" data-scroll-id="note42"><sup class="marker">42</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808761" id="p22" style="--height:374.427px;">Like Paul, these men of God are “not … ashamed of the testimony of our Lord” and are His “prisoner[s]”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note43" data-scroll-id="note43"><sup class="marker">43</sup></a> in the sense that the doctrine they teach is not theirs but His who called them. Like Peter, they “cannot but speak the things which [they] have seen and heard.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note44" data-scroll-id="note44"><sup class="marker">44</sup></a> I testify that the First Presidency and the Quorum of the Twelve are good and honest men who love God and His children and who are loved by Him. Their words we should receive as if from the Lord’s own mouth “in all patience and faith. For by doing these things the gates of hell shall not prevail against [us]; … and the Lord God will disperse the powers of darkness from before [us].”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note45" data-scroll-id="note45"><sup class="marker">45</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808770" id="p23" style="--height:230.417px;">“No unhallowed hand can stop the work from progressing”;<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note46" data-scroll-id="note46"><sup class="marker">46</sup></a> it will march on triumphantly with or without you or me, so “choose you this day whom ye will serve.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note47" data-scroll-id="note47"><sup class="marker">47</sup></a> Don’t be fooled or intimidated by the loud adversarial noises emanating from the great and spacious building. Their desperate decibels are no match for the serene <span class="page-break" data-page="110"></span>influence of the still, small voice upon broken hearts and contrite spirits.</p>
<p data-aid="149808779" id="p24" style="--height:172.813px;">I testify that Christ lives, that He is our Savior and Redeemer, and that He leads His Church through the First Presidency and the Quorum of the Twelve Apostles, thus assuring that we are not “tossed to and fro, and carried about with every wind of doctrine.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note48" data-scroll-id="note48"><sup class="marker">48</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808788" id="p25" style="--height:115.208px;">“True disciples of Jesus Christ,” President Nelson taught, “are willing to stand out, speak up, and be different from the people of the world. They are undaunted, devoted, and courageous.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/53klebingat?lang=eng#note49" data-scroll-id="note49"><sup class="marker">49</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808797" id="p26" style="--height:57.6042px;">Brothers and sisters, it’s a good day to be good! In the sacred name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149807932" id="p1" style="--height:201.615px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="111"></span>For just over three years now, we have been on a journey together as members of the Lord’s Church. It was October 2018 when the First Presidency and the Quorum of the Twelve Apostles invited us to learn of Jesus Christ by studying the scriptures in a new and inspiring fashion, with the <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> resource as our guide.</p>
<p data-aid="149807939" id="p2" style="--height:86.4063px;">On any journey, it’s good to pause occasionally to assess our progress and to make sure we are still moving toward our goal.</p>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807947" id="title2" style="--height:33.6111px;">Conversion Is Our Goal</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807954" id="p3" style="--height:57.6042px;">Consider this profound statement from the introduction to <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite>:</p>
<p data-aid="149807961" id="p4" style="--height:86.4063px;">“The aim of all gospel learning and teaching is to deepen our conversion to Heavenly Father and Jesus Christ.&nbsp;…</p>
<p data-aid="149807968" id="p5" style="--height:201.615px;">“… The kind of gospel learning that strengthens our faith and leads to the miracle of conversion doesn’t happen all at once. It extends beyond a classroom into our hearts and homes. It requires consistent, daily efforts to understand and live the gospel. Gospel learning that leads to true conversion requires the influence of the Holy Ghost.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807973" id="p6" style="--height:259.219px;">That is the miracle we seek—when one person has an experience in the scriptures<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> and that experience is blessed by the influence of the Holy Ghost. Such experiences are precious foundation stones for our conversion to the Savior. And as President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson recently reminded us, spiritual foundations must be constantly reinforced.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> Long-lasting conversion is a lifelong process.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a> Conversion is our goal.</p>
<p data-aid="149807980" id="p7" style="--height:201.615px;">To be most effective, your experiences with the scriptures must be your own.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a> Reading or hearing about another person’s experiences and insights can be helpful, but that won’t bring the same converting power. There is no substitute for the time <em>you</em> spend in the scriptures, hearing the Holy Ghost speak directly to <em>you</em>.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807985" id="title3" style="--height:67.2222px;">What Is the Holy Ghost Teaching Me?</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807990" id="p8" style="--height:115.208px;">Each week when I open my <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> manual, I write this question at the top of the page: “What is the Holy Ghost teaching me this week as I read these chapters?”</p>
<p data-aid="149807995" id="p9" style="--height:115.208px;">As I study the scriptures, I ponder that question over and over again. And without fail, spiritual impressions come, and I make note of them in my manual.</p>
<p data-aid="149808000" id="p10" style="--height:259.219px;">Now, how do I know when the Holy Ghost is teaching me? Well, it usually happens in small and simple ways. Sometimes a passage of scripture will seem to jump off the page to my attention. At other times, I feel like my mind is enlightened with a broader understanding of a gospel principle. I also feel the influence of the Holy Ghost when my wife, Anne Marie, and I talk about what we are reading. Her perspectives always invite the Spirit.</p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808005" id="title4" style="--height:33.6111px;">The Prophet and the Passover</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808011" id="p11" style="--height:144.01px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="112"></span>This year we are studying the Old Testament—sacred scripture that fills our souls with light. While reading the Old Testament, I feel like I am spending time with trusted guides: Adam, Eve, Enoch, Noah, Abraham, and so many others.</p>
<p data-aid="149808016" id="p12" style="--height:172.813px;">This week, while studying <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/ot/ex/7?lang=eng">Exodus chapters 7–13</a>, we learn how the Lord freed the children of Israel from centuries of captivity in Egypt. We read about nine plagues—nine impressive manifestations of God’s power—that Pharaoh witnessed without softening his heart.</p>
<p data-aid="149808021" id="p13" style="--height:259.219px;">Then the Lord told His prophet, Moses, about a tenth plague—and how each family in Israel could prepare for it. As part of a ritual they would call the Passover, the Israelites were to sacrifice a male lamb, one without blemish. Then they were to mark the doorframes of their homes with the blood of the lamb. The Lord promised that all the homes that were marked with the blood would be protected from the terrible plague that was about to come.</p>
<p data-aid="149808026" id="p14" style="--height:115.208px;">The scriptures say, “And the children of Israel … did as the Lord … commanded Moses” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/ot/ex/12.28?lang=eng#p28">Exodus 12:28</a>). There is something very powerful in that simple statement of obedience.</p>
<p data-aid="149808031" id="p15" style="--height:86.4063px;">Because the children of Israel followed the counsel of Moses and acted in faith, they were saved from the plague and, in time, freed from their captivity.</p>
<p data-aid="149808036" id="p16" style="--height:57.6042px;">So what did the Holy Ghost teach me in these chapters this week?</p>
<p data-aid="149808041" id="p17" style="--height:57.6042px;">Here are a few thoughts that have rested on my mind:</p>
<ul class="bullet">
<li>
<p data-aid="149808046" id="p18" style="--height:57.6042px;">The Lord works through His prophet to protect and save His people.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p data-aid="149808051" id="p19" style="--height:86.4063px;">The faith and humility to follow the prophet preceded the miracle of protection and deliverance.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p data-aid="149808055" id="p20" style="--height:57.6042px;">The blood on the doorframe was an outward sign of inward faith in Jesus Christ, the Lamb of God.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808060" id="title5" style="--height:67.2222px;">The Prophet and the Lord’s Promises</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808065" id="p21" style="--height:115.208px;">I am impressed with the parallel between the way the Lord blessed His people in this Old Testament account and the way He is also blessing His people today.</p>
<p data-aid="149808069" id="p22" style="--height:144.01px;">When the Lord’s living prophet, President Nelson, introduced us to <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> as a means of studying the scriptures, he invited us to transform our homes into sanctuaries of faith and centers of gospel learning.</p>
<p data-aid="149808073" id="p23" style="--height:28.8021px;">Then he promised four specific blessings:</p>
<ol class="decimal" start="1">
<li data-marker="1.">
<p data-aid="149808077" id="p24" style="--height:28.8021px;"><em>your</em> Sabbath days will be a delight,</p>
</li>
<li data-marker="2.">
<p data-aid="149808081" id="p25" style="--height:57.6042px;"><em>your</em> children will be excited to learn and live the Savior’s teachings,</p>
</li>
<li data-marker="3.">
<p data-aid="149808085" id="p26" style="--height:57.6042px;">the influence of the adversary in <em>your</em> life and in <em>your</em> home will decrease, and</p>
</li>
<li data-marker="4.">
<p data-aid="149808089" id="p27" style="--height:57.6042px;">these changes in <em>your</em> family will be dramatic and sustaining.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a></p>
</li>
</ol>
<p data-aid="149808094" id="p28" style="--height:172.813px;">Now, we don’t have any journal entries from those who experienced the Passover with Moses in Egypt. However, we do have many testimonials from Saints who, with equal faith, are following President Nelson’s counsel today and receiving the promised blessings.</p>
<p data-aid="149808097" id="p29" style="--height:28.8021px;">Here are a few such testimonials:</p>
<p data-aid="149808101" id="p30" style="--height:144.01px;">A mother of a young family said: “We talk of Christ and rejoice in Christ in our home. To me that is the greatest blessing—that my children can grow up with these gospel conversations in the home that bring them closer to the Savior.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808105" id="p31" style="--height:115.208px;">A senior brother called his study of the scriptures through <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> “a conduit filled with divine light that helps us see gospel doctrine that is necessary for our spiritual well-being.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808109" id="p32" style="--height:115.208px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="113"></span>A young wife described the blessings in her marriage: “I have been able to know my husband’s heart more deeply, and I have been able to open my heart more to him as we study together.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808113" id="p33" style="--height:230.417px;">A mother of a large family noticed how her efforts to teach her family changed. She mentioned: “Looking back, it was like I was playing the piano with snow gloves on. I was going through the motions, but the music wasn’t quite right. Now the gloves are off, and while my music still isn’t perfect, I hear the difference. <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> has given me vision, ability, focus, and purpose.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808117" id="p34" style="--height:230.417px;">A young husband said: “My most important priorities at home have become more clear since I’ve made <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> a regular part of my mornings. Studying leads me to think more about the things that matter most to me, like the temple, my relationship with my wife, and my calling. I’m grateful that my home is a sanctuary where God comes first.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808121" id="p35" style="--height:172.813px;">A sister shared: “My daily experiences with <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> are rarely noteworthy, but over time I can see how I am being changed by such a constant, focused study of the scriptures. That kind of study humbles me, teaches me, and changes me a little at a time.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808125" id="p36" style="--height:172.813px;">A returned missionary reported: “The <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> program has gotten me closer to the level of scripture study that I did on my mission, and I have been able to move from a checklist mentality of scripture study to truly enriching sessions of getting to know God.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808129" id="p37" style="--height:144.01px;">A brother said: “I feel the Holy Ghost welcomed more into my life and feel God’s revelatory guidance in making decisions. I have more profound conversations regarding the beauty in the simple doctrine of Christ and His Atonement.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808133" id="p38" style="--height:172.813px;">A seven-year-old child shared: “I’m getting baptized soon, and <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> is getting me ready. My family and I talk about baptism, and I don’t feel nervous about getting baptized now. <cite>Come, Follow Me</cite> helps the Holy Ghost come into my heart, and I feel warm when I read the scriptures.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808137" id="p39" style="--height:172.813px;">And then finally, from a mother of several children: “As we study the word of God, He has helped our family move from concern to power; from trial and challenge to deliverance; from contention and criticism to love and peace; and from the adversary’s influence to God’s influence.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/54pace?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808141" id="p40" style="--height:230.417px;">These and many other faithful followers of Christ have symbolically placed the blood of the Lamb of God on the entrance to their homes. They are demonstrating their inward commitment to follow the Savior. Their faith precedes the miracle. It is the miracle of one person having an experience in the scriptures and that experience being blessed by the influence of the Holy Ghost.</p>
<p data-aid="149808145" id="p41" style="--height:201.615px;">When we study the scriptures, there is no spiritual famine in the land. As Nephi said, “Whoso would hearken unto the word of God, and would hold fast unto it, they would never perish; neither could the temptations and the fiery darts of the adversary overpower them unto blindness, to lead them away to destruction” (<a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/bofm/1-ne/15.24?lang=eng#p24">1&nbsp;Nephi 15:24</a>).</p>
<p data-aid="149808149" id="p42" style="--height:201.615px;">In ancient times, as the children of Israel followed the Lord’s direction given through the prophet Moses, they were blessed with safety and freedom. Today, as we follow the Lord’s direction given through our living prophet, President Nelson, we are equally blessed with conversion in our hearts and protection in our homes.</p>
<p data-aid="149808153" id="p43" style="--height:144.01px;">I testify that Jesus Christ lives. This is His Church, restored to the earth through the Prophet Joseph Smith. President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson is the Lord’s prophet today. I love and sustain him. In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</section>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149807935" id="p1" style="--height:403.229px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="115"></span>I have a dear friend who is a brilliant, retired university professor, a prolific author, and, above all, a committed disciple of Jesus Christ. He has visited the Holy Land dozens of times to participate in conferences, conduct academic research, and lead tours. According to him, every time he visits the land where Jesus walked, he marvels because he undoubtedly learns something new, astonishing, and fascinating about the Savior, His mortal ministry, and His beloved homeland. The awe my friend shows when he talks about all that he learns in the Holy Land is contagious, and this amazement has been fundamental in his great achievements and academic pursuits in his life.</p>
<p data-aid="149807942" id="p2" style="--height:374.427px;">As I have listened to his experiences and felt of his enthusiasm, I have reflected on how much more spiritual wonder, so to speak, that we can and should feel for the gospel of Jesus Christ and the difference it can make in our discipleship and in our journey toward eternal life. The wonder I refer to is the sensation of emotion, awe, or amazement common to all who wholeheartedly center their lives on the Savior and His teachings and humbly recognize His presence in their lives. Such a feeling of wonder, inspired by the influence of the Holy Ghost, stimulates the enthusiasm to joyfully live the doctrine of Christ.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807949" id="p3" style="--height:316.823px;">The scriptures contain several examples of how this sensation is manifest. The prophet Isaiah, for example, expressed the depth of his gratitude for the Lord through his rejoicing in Him.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> Those who heard Jesus preaching in the synagogue at Capernaum were astonished at His doctrine and the strength with which He taught.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> It was this same feeling that penetrated every fiber of young Joseph Smith’s heart as he read from the Bible <a class="scripture-ref" href="/study/scriptures/nt/james/1?lang=eng">the first chapter of James</a>, leading him to seek the wisdom of God.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807956" id="p4" style="--height:460.833px;">My brothers and sisters, when we truly are in awe of Jesus Christ and His gospel, we are happier, we have more enthusiasm for God’s work, and we recognize the Lord’s hand in all things. Additionally, our study of God’s words is more meaningful; our prayers, more intentional; our worship, more reverent; our service in God’s kingdom, more diligent. All these actions contribute to the Holy Spirit’s influence being more frequent in our lives.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a> Thus, our testimony of the Savior and His gospel will be strengthened, we will keep Christ alive in us,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> and we will live our lives “rooted and built up in him, and stablished in the faith, … abounding therein with thanksgiving.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a> When we live in this way, we <span class="page-break" data-page="116"></span>become more spiritually resilient and protected against falling into the trap of spiritual apathy.</p>
<p data-aid="149807963" id="p5" style="--height:460.833px;">Such apathy is characterized by the gradual loss of our excitement to engage fully in the Lord’s gospel. It generally begins when we are feeling that we have already attained all the necessary knowledge and blessings for our happiness in this life. This complacency, so to speak, causes us to take the gospel gifts for granted, and from then on, we run the risk of neglecting both our regular immersion in the essentials of the gospel of Jesus Christ<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a> and the covenants we have made. Consequently, we gradually distance ourselves from the Lord, weakening our ability to “hear Him,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a> becoming indifferent and insensitive to the greatness of His work. Doubt regarding the truths we have already received may enter our mind and heart, making us vulnerable to the enemy’s temptations.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807970" id="p15" style="--height:288.021px;">Pastor Aiden Wilson Tozer, a renowned writer and valiant Christian, wrote, “Complacency is a deadly foe of all spiritual growth.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a> Wasn’t this exactly what happened to the people of Nephi shortly after the birth of Christ? They “began to be less and less astonished at a sign or a wonder from heaven, … [disbelieving] all which they had heard and seen.” Thus did Satan “blind their eyes and lead them away to believe that the doctrine of Christ was a foolish and a vain thing.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807976" id="p6" style="--height:489.635px;">My beloved brothers and sisters, in His perfect and infinite love and knowing our human nature,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> the Savior has established the way for us to avoid falling into the trap of spiritual apathy. The Savior’s invitation gives us a broader perspective, especially considering the complex world in which we live: “Learn of me, and listen to my words; walk in the meekness of my Spirit, and you shall have peace in me.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> As we accept the Savior’s invitation, we demonstrate our humility, our desire to be teachable, and our hope to become more like Him.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a> This invitation also includes serving Him and ministering to God’s children “with all [our] heart, might, mind and strength.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> At the core of our effort in this journey are, of course, the two great commandments: to love the Lord our God and love our neighbor as ourselves.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807981" id="p7" style="--height:518.438px;">This type of behavior is part of Jesus’s divine character and was evident in everything He did during His earthly ministry.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a> Therefore, when we intentionally and truly dedicate ourselves to look unto Him and learn from His perfect example,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a> we come to know Him better. We grow in enthusiasm and desire to incorporate into our lives the ultimate standard of how we should live, the example we should set, and the commandments we should follow. We also gain additional understanding, wisdom, divine character, and grace toward God and our neighbors.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a> I can assure you that our ability to feel the Savior’s influence and love will be intensified in our lives, magnifying our faith, our desire to act righteously, and the motivation to serve Him and others.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a> In addition, our gratitude for the blessings and challenges we experience in mortality will solidify and become part of our true worship.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149807986" id="p8" style="--height:432.031px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="117"></span>My dear friends, all these things strengthen our spiritual wonder regarding the gospel and move us to joyfully keep the covenants we make with the Lord—even in the midst of the trials and challenges we experience. Of course, for these outcomes to happen, we need to immerse ourselves with faith and real intent in the Savior’s teachings,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a> striving to incorporate His attributes into our way of being.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note24" data-scroll-id="note24"><sup class="marker">24</sup></a> In addition, we need to draw nearer to Him through our repentance,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note25" data-scroll-id="note25"><sup class="marker">25</sup></a> seeking His forgiveness and His redeeming power in our lives and keeping His commandments. The Lord Himself promised that He would direct our paths if we would trust in Him with all our hearts, acknowledging Him in all our ways and not leaning on our own understanding.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note26" data-scroll-id="note26"><sup class="marker">26</sup></a></p>
<div><div class="imageWrapper-wTPPD"><figure class="imageWithModal-bCN6D loadImageItem-u5D4D" title="Wes and Elder Jones"><img width="500" height="396" alt=""><div class="container-W4jed"><div class="innerFlex-R9N_u"><svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" role="presentation" style="width: 1.5rem; height: 1.5rem;"> <path fill="currentColor" d="M20 4.75L19.25 4v16l.75-.75H4l.75.75V4L4 4.75h16zM3.25 4v16c0 .414.336.75.75.75h16a.75.75 0 0 0 .75-.75V4a.75.75 0 0 0-.75-.75H4a.75.75 0 0 0-.75.75zm11.07 8.888c.23-.357.606-.353.828-.008l2.887 4.482c.227.352.06.638-.357.638H6.326c-.421 0-.581-.3-.37-.648l4.006-6.622c.217-.358.567-.359.793.014l2.396 3.96 1.17-1.816zm1.59-2.735c1.14 0 2.066-.907 2.066-2.026 0-1.12-.926-2.027-2.067-2.027s-2.066.907-2.066 2.027c0 1.119.925 2.026 2.066 2.026z"> </path></svg><div class="sc-1szn76m-0 dODiQr i18nString-raclU">Image</div><div class="sc-1szn76m-0 dODiQr title-RrK9J">Wes and Elder Jones</div></div></div></figure></div></div>
<p data-aid="149807991" id="p9" style="--height:489.635px;">A man I met recently, whose name is Wes and who is attending the conference today, accepted Christ’s invitation to learn of Him and of His gospel and began to experience the awe of His love after 27 years of distancing himself from the covenant path. He told me that one day he was contacted via Facebook by a missionary, Elder Jones, who was temporarily assigned to Wes’s area before going to his originally assigned mission in Panama. When Elder Jones came across Wes’s profile, not even knowing beforehand that he was already a member of the Church, he felt the guidance of the Holy Ghost and knew that he should immediately contact Wes. He quickly acted on this impression. Wes was amazed by this unexpected contact and began to realize that the Lord was aware of him despite his distance from the covenant path.</p>
<p data-aid="149807996" id="p16" style="--height:374.427px;">From then on, Wes and the missionaries began to communicate frequently. Elder Jones and his companion provided weekly acts of service and spiritual messages that helped Wes to recover his awe of the Savior and His gospel. It rekindled the flame of his testimony of the truth and of the Savior’s love for him. Wes felt the peace that comes from the Comforter and gained the strength he needed to return to the fold. He told me that this experience brought him spiritually and emotionally back to life and helped him to eliminate the feelings of bitterness accumulated over the years because of the difficult experiences he had been through.</p>
<p data-aid="149808001" id="p10" style="--height:489.635px;">As my aforementioned thoughtful professor friend has observed, there is always something wonderful and fascinating to learn about Jesus Christ and His gospel.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note27" data-scroll-id="note27"><sup class="marker">27</sup></a> The Lord has made wonderful promises that are extended to all those, including us, who seek to learn of Him and incorporate His words into their lives. To Enoch, He said, “Behold my Spirit [shall be] upon you, wherefore all thy words will I justify; and the mountains shall flee before you, and the rivers shall turn from their course; and thou shalt abide in me, and I in you.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note28" data-scroll-id="note28"><sup class="marker">28</sup></a> Through His servant King Benjamin, He declared, “Ye shall be called the children of Christ, his sons, and his daughters; for behold, this day he hath spiritually begotten you; for ye say that your hearts are changed through faith on his name; therefore, ye are born of him and have become his sons and his daughters.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note29" data-scroll-id="note29"><sup class="marker">29</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808006" id="p17" style="--height:172.813px;">Therefore, as we genuinely and continually strive to learn of the Savior and follow His example, I promise you, in His name, that His divine attributes will be written in our minds and hearts,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note30" data-scroll-id="note30"><sup class="marker">30</sup></a> that we will become more like Him, and that we will walk with Him.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note31" data-scroll-id="note31"><sup class="marker">31</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808010" id="p11" style="--height:288.021px;">My beloved brothers and sisters, I pray that we will ever stand in awe of Jesus Christ and His complete, infinite, and perfect love. May the remembrance of what our eyes have seen and our hearts have felt increase our amazement at the Savior’s atoning sacrifice, which can heal us of our spiritual and emotional wounds and help us to draw closer to Him. May we marvel at the great promises that the Father has in His hands and that He has prepared for those who are faithful:</p>
<p data-aid="149808015" id="p12" style="--height:57.6042px;">“The kingdom is yours and the blessings thereof are yours, and the riches of eternity are yours.</p>
<p data-aid="149808020" id="p13" style="--height:57.6042px;">“And he who receiveth all things with thankfulness shall be made glorious.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/55soares?lang=eng#note32" data-scroll-id="note32"><sup class="marker">32</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808025" id="p14" style="--height:115.208px;">Jesus is the Redeemer of the world, and this is His Church. I bear witness of these truths in the awe-inspiring, sacred, and sublime name of our Savior, Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<p data-aid="149807933" id="p1" style="--height:374.427px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="118"></span>As young parents, Brother and Sister Samad learned the gospel of Jesus Christ in their simple two-room home in Semarang, Indonesia.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note1" data-scroll-id="note1"><sup class="marker">1</sup></a> Seated around a small table, with a dim light that seemed to provide more mosquitoes than illumination, two young missionaries taught them eternal truths. Through sincere prayer and the guidance of the Holy Ghost, they came to believe what they were taught and chose to be baptized and become members of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints. That decision, and their pattern of living since, has blessed Brother and Sister Samad and their family in every aspect of their lives.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note2" data-scroll-id="note2"><sup class="marker">2</sup></a> </p>
<p data-aid="149807940" id="p2" style="--height:201.615px;">They are among the early pioneer Saints in Indonesia. Later they received the ordinances of the temple, and Brother Samad served as the branch president and then district president, driving throughout Central Java to <span class="page-break" data-page="119"></span>fulfill his responsibilities. For the past decade, he has served as the first patriarch of the Surakarta Indonesia Stake.</p>
<div><div class="imageWrapper-wTPPD"><img id="img1" data-img-id="a1e9b6f2b11911ec8275eeeeac1ee811858141a9" data-assetid="a1e9b6f2b11911ec8275eeeeac1ee811858141a9" data-missing-asset="false" data-width="500" data-height="732" data-aspect-ratio="0.6830601092896175" alt="Indonesia: Randy Funk" class="imageWithModal-bCN6D" height="732" src="https://assets.ldscdn.org/39/27/3927cd61e070effa69d7c58fff97f7c9ff0782ce/3927cd61e070effa69d7c58fff97f7c9ff0782ce.image/jpeg" srcset="https://assets.ldscdn.org/96/13/96134fdd8d2d82181b9efdd565a741a14a6020bc/96134fdd8d2d82181b9efdd565a741a14a6020bc.image/jpeg 60w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/77/05/7705476e9ba2e1485ec10acd45a78aa7651ca19d/7705476e9ba2e1485ec10acd45a78aa7651ca19d.image/jpeg 100w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/a5/d7/a5d71bf3d345f916e7f0975a7cdf147f641c36f3/a5d71bf3d345f916e7f0975a7cdf147f641c36f3.image/jpeg 200w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/5e/71/5e71618fcdfe6e072b1419fa28b0156110f24ae3/5e71618fcdfe6e072b1419fa28b0156110f24ae3.image/jpeg 250w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/0a/5c/0a5c2667e9b38d8f5fa9602f1ae62f5e36a2496d/0a5c2667e9b38d8f5fa9602f1ae62f5e36a2496d.image/jpeg 320w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/39/27/3927cd61e070effa69d7c58fff97f7c9ff0782ce/3927cd61e070effa69d7c58fff97f7c9ff0782ce.image/jpeg 500w,https://assets.ldscdn.org/68/8b/688bef526bb525c907e4cbf11a9836cc78856df9/688bef526bb525c907e4cbf11a9836cc78856df9.image/jpeg 640w" width="500"></div></div>
<p data-aid="149807946" id="p3" style="--height:316.823px;">As one of the missionaries in that humble, faith-filled home 49 years ago, I have witnessed in them what King Benjamin taught in the Book of Mormon: “I would desire that ye should consider on the blessed and happy state of those that keep the commandments of God. For behold, they are blessed in all things, both temporal and spiritual.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note3" data-scroll-id="note3"><sup class="marker">3</sup></a> The blessings that flow into the lives of those who follow the example and teachings of Jesus Christ, who choose to be counted among His disciples, are numerous, joyful, and eternal.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note4" data-scroll-id="note4"><sup class="marker">4</sup></a> </p>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807953" id="title2" style="--height:33.6111px;">The Fold of God</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807960" id="p4" style="--height:115.208px;">Alma’s baptismal covenant invitation to those gathered at the Waters of Mormon begins with this phrase: “Now, as ye are desirous to come into the fold of God.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note5" data-scroll-id="note5"><sup class="marker">5</sup></a> </p>
<div><div class="imageWrapper-wTPPD"><figure class="imageWithModal-bCN6D loadImageItem-u5D4D" title="Sheep"><img width="500" height="750" alt=""><div class="container-W4jed"><div class="innerFlex-R9N_u"><svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" role="presentation" style="width: 1.5rem; height: 1.5rem;"> <path fill="currentColor" d="M20 4.75L19.25 4v16l.75-.75H4l.75.75V4L4 4.75h16zM3.25 4v16c0 .414.336.75.75.75h16a.75.75 0 0 0 .75-.75V4a.75.75 0 0 0-.75-.75H4a.75.75 0 0 0-.75.75zm11.07 8.888c.23-.357.606-.353.828-.008l2.887 4.482c.227.352.06.638-.357.638H6.326c-.421 0-.581-.3-.37-.648l4.006-6.622c.217-.358.567-.359.793.014l2.396 3.96 1.17-1.816zm1.59-2.735c1.14 0 2.066-.907 2.066-2.026 0-1.12-.926-2.027-2.067-2.027s-2.066.907-2.066 2.027c0 1.119.925 2.026 2.066 2.026z"> </path></svg><div class="sc-1szn76m-0 dODiQr i18nString-raclU">Image</div><div class="sc-1szn76m-0 dODiQr title-RrK9J">Sheep</div></div></div></figure></div></div>
<p data-aid="149807967" id="p5" style="--height:172.813px;">A fold, or sheepfold, is a large enclosure, often constructed with stone walls, where the sheep are protected at night. It has only one opening. At the end of the day, the shepherd calls the sheep. They know his voice, and through the gate they enter the safety of the fold. </p>
<p data-aid="149807974" id="p6" style="--height:201.615px;">The people of Alma would have known that shepherds stand at the narrow opening of the fold so that when the sheep enter, they are numbered<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note6" data-scroll-id="note6"><sup class="marker">6</sup></a> and their wounds and ailments noted and cared for one by one. The safety and well-being of the sheep depend on their willingness to come into the fold and to stay in the fold.</p>
<p data-aid="149807979" id="p7" style="--height:172.813px;">Among us there may be some who feel they are at the edge of the flock, perhaps thinking they are less needed or valued or that they don’t belong in the fold. And, as in the sheepfold, in the fold of God we sometimes step on one another’s toes and need to repent or forgive. </p>
<p data-aid="149807984" id="p8" style="--height:374.427px;">But the Good Shepherd<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note7" data-scroll-id="note7"><sup class="marker">7</sup></a>—our true shepherd—is always good. Within the fold of God, we experience His watchful, nurturing care and are blessed to feel His redeeming love. He said, “I have graven thee upon the palms of my hands; thy walls are continually before me.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note8" data-scroll-id="note8"><sup class="marker">8</sup></a> Our Savior has graven upon His palms our sins, pains, afflictions,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note9" data-scroll-id="note9"><sup class="marker">9</sup></a> and all that is unfair in life.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note10" data-scroll-id="note10"><sup class="marker">10</sup></a> All are welcome to receive these blessings, as they “are desirous to come”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note11" data-scroll-id="note11"><sup class="marker">11</sup></a> and choose to be in the fold. The gift of agency is not simply the right to choose; it is the opportunity to choose the right. And the walls of the fold are not a constraint but a source of spiritual safety.</p>
<p data-aid="149807989" id="p9" style="--height:57.6042px;">Jesus taught that there is “one fold, and one shepherd.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note12" data-scroll-id="note12"><sup class="marker">12</sup></a> He said: </p>
<p data-aid="149807994" id="p24" style="--height:57.6042px;">“He that entereth in by the door is the shepherd of the sheep.&nbsp;… </p>
<p data-aid="149807999" id="p25" style="--height:28.8021px;">“And the sheep hear his voice&nbsp;…&nbsp;, </p>
<p data-aid="149808004" id="p26" style="--height:57.6042px;">“… and the sheep follow him: for they know his voice.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note13" data-scroll-id="note13"><sup class="marker">13</sup></a> </p>
<p data-aid="149808009" id="p27" style="--height:144.01px;">Jesus then stated, “I am the door: by me if any man enter in, he shall be saved,”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note14" data-scroll-id="note14"><sup class="marker">14</sup></a> teaching clearly that there is only one way into the fold of God and only one way to be saved. It is by and through Jesus Christ.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note15" data-scroll-id="note15"><sup class="marker">15</sup></a> </p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808013" id="title3" style="--height:67.2222px;">Blessings Come to Those in the Fold of God</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808018" id="p10" style="--height:316.823px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="120"></span>We learn how to come into the fold from the word of God, which is the doctrine taught by Jesus Christ and His prophets.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note16" data-scroll-id="note16"><sup class="marker">16</sup></a> When we follow the doctrine of Christ and come into the fold through faith in Jesus Christ, repentance, baptism and confirmation, and continuing faithfulness,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note17" data-scroll-id="note17"><sup class="marker">17</sup></a> Alma promised four specific, personal blessings. <em>You</em> may (1)&nbsp;“be redeemed of God,” (2)&nbsp;“be numbered with those of the first resurrection,” (3)&nbsp;“have eternal life,” and (4)&nbsp;the Lord will “pour out his Spirit more abundantly upon you.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note18" data-scroll-id="note18"><sup class="marker">18</sup></a> </p>
<p data-aid="149808023" id="p11" style="--height:57.6042px;">After Alma taught about these blessings, the people clapped their hands for joy. Here’s why: </p>
<p data-aid="149808028" id="p12" style="--height:172.813px;">First: To <em>redeem</em> means to pay off a debt or obligation or to free from what distresses or harms.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note19" data-scroll-id="note19"><sup class="marker">19</sup></a> No amount of personal improvement on our part can make us clean from the sins we have committed or whole from the wounds we have suffered without the Atonement of Jesus Christ. He is our Redeemer.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note20" data-scroll-id="note20"><sup class="marker">20</sup></a> </p>
<p data-aid="149808033" id="p13" style="--height:172.813px;">Second: Because of Christ’s Resurrection, all will be resurrected.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note21" data-scroll-id="note21"><sup class="marker">21</sup></a> After our spirits depart our mortal bodies, we will undoubtedly look forward to when we can again with a resurrected body embrace those we love. We will eagerly look forward to being among those of the First Resurrection.</p>
<p data-aid="149808038" id="p14" style="--height:115.208px;">Third: Eternal life means to live with God and as He lives. It is “the greatest of all the gifts of God”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note22" data-scroll-id="note22"><sup class="marker">22</sup></a> and will bring a fulness of joy.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note23" data-scroll-id="note23"><sup class="marker">23</sup></a> It is the ultimate purpose and objective of our lives.</p>
<p data-aid="149808043" id="p15" style="--height:86.4063px;">Fourth: The companionship of a member of the Godhead, the Holy Ghost, provides much-needed guidance and comfort during this mortal life.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note24" data-scroll-id="note24"><sup class="marker">24</sup></a> </p>
<p data-aid="149808048" id="p16" style="--height:288.021px;">Consider some causes of unhappiness: misery comes from sin,<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note25" data-scroll-id="note25"><sup class="marker">25</sup></a> sadness and loneliness from the death of a loved one, and fear from the uncertainty of what happens when we die. But when we enter the fold of God <span class="page-break" data-page="121"></span>and keep our covenants with Him, we feel the peace of knowing and trusting that Christ will redeem us from our sins, that the separation of our body and spirit will end more quickly, and that we will live eternally with God in a most glorious manner. </p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808053" id="title4" style="--height:33.6111px;">Trust in Christ and Act in Faith</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808058" id="p17" style="--height:316.823px;">Brothers and sisters, the scriptures are filled with examples of the Savior’s majestic power and His compassionate mercy and grace. During His earthly ministry, His blessings of healing came to those who trusted Him and acted in faith. For example, the infirm man at the pool of Bethesda walked when, with faith, he followed the Savior’s command to “rise, take up thy bed, and walk.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note26" data-scroll-id="note26"><sup class="marker">26</sup></a> Those who were sick or afflicted in any manner in the land of Bountiful were healed when “with one accord” they “did go forth.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note27" data-scroll-id="note27"><sup class="marker">27</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808063" id="p18" style="--height:201.615px;">Similarly, to receive the marvelous blessings promised to those who come into the fold of God requires us to do just that—we need to choose to come. Alma the Younger taught, “And now I say unto you that the good shepherd doth call after you; and if you will hearken unto his voice he will bring you into his fold.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note28" data-scroll-id="note28"><sup class="marker">28</sup></a></p>
<p data-aid="149808067" id="p19" style="--height:172.813px;">Several years ago a dear friend passed away from cancer. When his wife, Sharon, first wrote about his diagnosis, she said: “We Choose Faith. Faith in our Savior, Jesus Christ. Faith in our Heavenly Father’s plan, and faith that He knows our needs and fulfills His promises.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note29" data-scroll-id="note29"><sup class="marker">29</sup></a> </p>
<p data-aid="149808071" id="p20" style="--height:230.417px;">I have met many Latter-day Saints like Sharon who feel the inward peace of being securely within the fold of God, especially when temptation, opposition, or adversity comes.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note30" data-scroll-id="note30"><sup class="marker">30</sup></a> They have chosen to have faith in Jesus Christ and to follow His prophet. Our dear prophet, President Russell&nbsp;M. Nelson, has taught, “Everything good in life—every potential blessing of eternal significance—begins with faith.”<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note31" data-scroll-id="note31"><sup class="marker">31</sup></a></p>
</section>
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149808075" id="title5" style="--height:33.6111px;">Come Fully into the Fold of God</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149808079" id="p21" style="--height:201.615px;">My great-great-great-grandfather James Sawyer Holman came to Utah in 1847, but he wasn’t among those to arrive in July with Brigham Young. He came later that year and, according to family records, was responsible to bring the sheep. He didn’t reach the Salt Lake Valley until October, but he and the sheep made it.<a class="note-ref" href="/study/general-conference/2022/04/56funk?lang=eng#note32" data-scroll-id="note32"><sup class="marker">32</sup></a> </p>
<p data-aid="149808083" id="p22" style="--height:172.813px;">Figuratively speaking, some of us are still on the plains. Not everyone arrives in the first group. My dear friends, please continue the journey—and help others—to come fully into the fold of God. The blessings of the gospel of Jesus Christ are immeasurable because they are eternal. </p>
<p data-aid="149808087" id="p23" style="--height:201.615px;">I am profoundly grateful to be a member of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints. I bear witness of the love of our Heavenly Father and our Redeemer, Jesus Christ, and of the peace that comes only from Them—the inner peace and the blessings found in the fold of God. In the name of Jesus Christ, amen.</p>
</section>
</div>

<div class="body-block">
<section>
<header>
<h2 data-aid="149807936" id="title2" style="--height:33.6111px;">An Offering unto Him</h2>
</header>
<p data-aid="149807943" id="p1" style="--height:172.813px;"><span class="page-break" data-page="122"></span>Just days before He gave His life for us, Jesus Christ was at the temple in Jerusalem, watching people make donations to the temple treasury. “Many that were rich cast in much,” but then, along came a poor widow, “and she threw in two mites.” It was such a small amount, it would hardly be worth recording.</p>
<div><div class="imageWrapper-wTPPD"><img id="img1" data-img-id="11415af1b11811ec8275eeeeac1ee811b0a74d50" data-assetid="11415af1b11811ec8275eeeeac1ee811b0a74d50" data-missing-asset="false" data-width="500" data-height="323" data-aspect-ratio="1.5479876160990713" alt="Jesus Christ.
